Qasama: The Hanafi Procedure and Inter-Madhhab Dispute
Presents the Hanafi ruling on qasama and the opposing positions of Shafi'i and Malik

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on qasama, compare it with the Shafi'i and Maliki positions, and explain the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence) of each disagreement.

Core Idea
In Hanafi law, qasama requires no circumstantial evidence; fifty men from the locality swear and diyah is paid.

This passage opens the chapter on qasama (oath of compurgation) in Ashraf al-Hidayah, presenting the core Hanafi rule and the opposing views of Imam al-Shafi'i and Imam Malik. The Hanafi position is straightforward: when a slain person is found in a locality and the killer is unknown, fifty men from that locality are sworn by the heir. The oath denies knowledge of the killing. Shafi'i requires the presence of lawth (strong circumstantial evidence) for this procedure, while Malik additionally allows qisas in cases of intentional killing. Understanding these differences is critical for applying blood money or retaliation in unresolved homicide cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi position
From the matn of al-Quduri, state the rule: fifty men from the locality are sworn by the heir when a slain person is found and the killer is unknown. The oath is that they did not kill him nor know his killer.
This rule applies regardless of whether there is lawth (circumstantial evidence).
2
Identify the Shafi'i position and its key condition
Imam al-Shafi'i requires the existence of lawth before qasama can be applied. Without lawth, the heirs themselves swear and no diyah is imposed on the locality.
Lawth includes bloodstained weapon, enmity, or testimony.
3
Identify the Maliki position and its outcome
Imam Malik holds that in cases of intentional killing with lawth, the plaintiff can choose a defendant from the accused group and demand qisas (retaliation), not just diyah.
This is more severe than the Hanafi position, which only gives diyah.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf for each dispute
For Hanafi vs Shafi'i: under Hanafi, qasama is easier to trigger (no lawth), leading to faster compensation. Under Shafi'i, victims may fail to get compensation if lawth is absent. For Hanafi vs Maliki: Maliki allows qisas in intentional killing, while Hanafi restricts to diyah.
These differences affect the severity and likelihood of punishment.

Source Text

ایک ہے۔
Chapter of Qasama. Ashraf al-Hidayah Urdu commentary on al-Hidayah, Volume 19. Diyah becomes obligatory, and Imam Malik says that if the plaintiff claims intentional killing, he may take qisas from whomever he chooses among the defendants (the people of the locality). (Ghrar al-Afkar - Shami). Note: In some cases, the slain person needs to be established, so this was placed in a separate chapter at the end of the book of Diyat. Note 2: By 'specific cause' is meant the presence of the slain in the locality; 'specific number' is fifty; 'specific type' means a male who is sane, adult, or a responsible owner—this includes men and women; 'specific method' means fifty men, and if there are children and the full number is not completed, then the oath is repeated. Statement on Qasama: He (al-Quduri) said: When a slain person is found in a locality and his killer is unknown, fifty men from among them are sworn, chosen by the heir (wali), [saying] 'By Allah, we did not kill him, nor do we know his killer.' Al-Shafi'i said: If there is lawth (circumstantial evidence), the heirs are sworn fifty oaths and judgment is given for diyah against the accused, whether the claim is intentional or erroneous. Malik said: Judgment for qisas is given if the claim is for intentional killing, and this is one of Shafi'i's two opinions. Translation: Al-Quduri said: When a slain person is found in a locality and his killer is unknown, fifty men from the locality are sworn, chosen by the heir—the words of the oath are: 'By Allah, we did not kill him, nor do we know his killer.' Al-Shafi'i said: When there is circumstantial evidence, the heirs are sworn fifty oaths and Diyah is decreed against the accused, whether the claim is intentional or erroneous. Malik said: Qisas is decreed when the claim is for intentional killing, and this is one of Shafi'i's two opinions.
Source pages p. 25

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on Qasama (oath of compurgation) in Ashraf al-Hidayah, a commentary on al-Hidayah. The author first provides the Hanafi ruling from the matn of al-Quduri: when a slain person is found in a locality and the killer is unknown, fifty men from that locality must be sworn by the heir (wali). The oath is that they did not kill him nor know his killer. Then the views of Imam al-Shafi'i and Imam Malik are presented. Shafi'i requires the presence of lawth (strong circumstantial evidence) for this procedure; if lawth exists, the heirs themselves swear fifty oaths and receive diyah from the accused. Malik goes further in cases of intentional killing with lawth, allowing qisas (retaliation) against a chosen defendant. The passage also includes preliminary notes explaining the specific cause (the slain being found in the locality), specific number (fifty), specific type (responsible male, but women are included), and specific method (repeating oaths if the exact number of men is insufficient). This sets the stage for the detailed discussion on qasama, where the Hanafi position is that no lawth is required, unlike Shafi'i and Malik.

Key Terms
قسامة (qasama): The legal procedure of oath-taking by fifty men from the locality when a slain person is found and the killer is unknown.
یمین (yamin): An oath sworn by each of the fifty men, denying killing or knowledge of the killer.
ولی (wali): The legal guardian or heir of the slain person, who selects the fifty men to be sworn.
دیت (diyah): Blood money paid as compensation for homicide, usually 100 camels or equivalent.
لوث (lawth): Strong circumstantial evidence pointing to a specific killer, such as a bloodstained weapon, open enmity, or testimony.
عمد (amad): Intentional homicide.
خطأ (khata'): Unintentional homicide or error.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when a slain person is found in a locality and no killer is known, who is sworn?
A) The heirs of the slain
B) Fifty men from the locality
C) The accused
D) The judge

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school applies qasama without requiring circumstantial evidence, making diyah accessible to the victim's family even when the killer is unknown.

Definition and Signs of Lawth in Qasama
Defines lawth according to Malik and Shafi'i with examples.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the four signs of lawth as defined by Malik and Shafi'i and explain why the Hanafi school does not require lawth for qasama.

Core Idea
Lawth is strong circumstantial evidence required by Malik and Shafi'i to initiate qasama, but not by the Hanafi school.

This passage defines the term lawth (strong circumstantial evidence) as understood by the Maliki and Shafi'i schools. In qasama (oath-taking in murder cases), these schools require lawth to proceed. The Hanafi school, however, does not require it. Understanding this distinction is crucial for grasping the different procedural approaches to murder investigations across the madhhabs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition of lawth
Find the Arabic sentence that defines lawth: 'واللوث عندهما أن يكون هناك علامة القتل على واحد بعينه أو ظاهر يشهد للمدعى'. This translates to 'lawth according to them (Malik and Shafi'i) is that there is a sign of killing pointing to a specific person, or an apparent circumstance testifying for the plaintiff.'
Note that the definition includes both a direct sign (علامة) and a broader circumstance (ظاهر).
2
List the four signs of lawth
From the commentary, extract the four scenarios: (1) a bloodstained sword found with someone, (2) open enmity between victim and suspect, (3) testimony of a single just witness (provided the witness is not from the same locality), (4) testimony of a group even if they are not just.
These are considered strong enough to incline the heart toward guilt.
3
Note the condition for the single just witness
The commentary specifies that the just witness must not be from the locality of the victim. This ensures impartiality and prevents bias.
This condition is not mentioned for the other signs.
4
Contrast with the Hanafi position
Recall that in Hanafi fiqh, qasama is initiated without any requirement of lawth. The definition here is provided to explain the Maliki/Shafi'i view, not the Hanafi ruling.
This cross-madhhab awareness avoids a common misunderstanding.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لوث کا معنی
واللوث عندهما أن يكون هناك علامة القتل على واحد بعينه أو ظاهر يشهد للمدعى من عداوة ظاهرة أو شهادة عدل أو جماعة غير عدول أن أهل المحلة قتلوه ترجمہ اور ان دونوں ( مالک و شافعی) کے نزدیک لوث یہ ہے کہ وہاں کسی معین شخص پر قتل کی علامت ہو یا ظاہر حال مدعی کے لئے شاہ یعنی عداوت ظاہرہ ہو یا ایک عادل کی شہادت ہو یا ایسی جماعت کی شہادت ہو جو غیر عادل ہیں کہ اہل محلہ نے اس کو قتل کیا ہے۔ تشریح یہاں سے لوث کی تفسیر بیان کر رہے ہیں جس کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ کوئی ایسا قرینہ مل جائے جس سے قلب میں بات جم جائے کہ یہی لوگ اس کے قائل ہیں جس کے مختلف طریقے ہیں کسی کی ان میں تلوار خون آلود ہو ۔

۲ یا مقتول کے اور ان میں سے کسی کے درمیان عداوت چل رہی تھی۔ -۳- ایک عادل شخص نے شہادت دی ہو کہ اہل محلہ ہی اس کے قاتل ہیں مگر اس شاہد کیلئے ضروری ہے کہ وہ اس محلہ کا نہ ہو۔

Meaning of Lawth. And lawth according to them (Malik and Shafi'i) is that there is a sign of killing pointing to a specific person, or an apparent circumstance testifying for the plaintiff, such as open enmity, or the testimony of a just person, or the testimony of a group who are not just, that the people of the locality killed him. Translation: And according to those two (Malik and Shafi'i), lawth is that there is a sign of killing on a specific person, or an apparent circumstance that testifies for the plaintiff, i.e., open enmity, or the testimony of one just person, or the testimony of a group who are not just, that the people of the locality killed him. Commentary: Here they are explaining the interpretation of lawth, the gist of which is that any such circumstantial evidence is found that settles in the heart that these people are the killers, and it has various ways: someone among them has a bloodstained sword. Or there was enmity between the slain and one of them. Or a just person testified that the people of the locality are the killers, but it is necessary for this witness that he is not from that locality. Or a group testified but that group was not just. So all these situations are included in lawth, whose ruling has been mentioned.
Source pages p. 25

Commentary
This passage defines the term 'lawth' (strong circumstantial evidence) according to Imam Malik and Imam al-Shafi'i, as used in the context of qasama. The author first gives the Arabic definition: it includes a physical sign pointing to a specific individual, or an apparent circumstance like open enmity, or the testimony of a single just person, or even the testimony of a group of unjust persons, all indicating that the people of the locality are the killers. The Urdu translation and commentary elaborate that the core idea is any evidence that strongly inclines the heart to believe that these people are the killers. Examples given: a bloodstained sword found with someone, prior enmity between the victim and a particular person, testimony of a just witness (provided the witness is not from the same locality), or testimony of a group even if they are not just. These are the four scenarios that constitute lawth. Importantly, the Hanafi school does not require lawth for qasama—the procedure applies regardless. This definition is presented to explain the opposing view, not to establish the Hanafi position.

Key Terms
لوث (lawth): Strong circumstantial evidence that points to the killer, such as a bloodstained weapon, open enmity, or testimony (just or unjust) that the people of the locality committed the murder.
عداوت ظاہرہ (adawat zahirah): Open enmity between the victim and a specific person, considered a sign of lawth.
قرینہ (qarinah): Circumstantial evidence that leads to a strong suspicion; in this context, it is synonymous with lawth.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, which of the following is NOT listed as a sign of lawth?
A) Bloodstained sword
B) Open enmity
C) Testimony of a single just witness from the same locality
D) Testimony of an unjust group

Key Takeaway
Lawth is a condition for qasama in Maliki and Shafi'i fiqh but not in Hanafi; its signs include physical evidence, enmity, and specific forms of testimony.

The Ruling Without Lawth and the Difference on Oath Repetition
Compares Hanafi and Shafi'i rulings on oath repetition without lawth in qasama.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the difference between the Hanafi and Shafi'i rulings on oath repetition in qasama without lawth and identify the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf).

Core Idea
Without lawth, Hanafi repeats oaths to fifty; Shafi'i returns the oath to the wali, altering liability.

When circumstantial evidence (lawth) is absent, both Hanafi and Shafi'i schools agree on taking oaths from the locality's men. However, a critical difference arises when the number of men is less than fifty: the Hanafi school requires repetition of the oath among them, while the Shafi'i school returns the oath to the heirs (wali). This difference has a direct impact on who bears the diyah if the oath is sworn. In this lesson, we will examine the precise points of agreement and disagreement, and trace the practical consequences of each ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify common ground
Both schools agree that when there is no lawth, the oath should be taken from the people of the locality.
This is the starting point of the comparison.
2
Isolate the point of dispute
The dispute arises when the number of qualified men in the locality is less than fifty. Hanafi requires repetition of the oath among these men until fifty oaths are sworn. Shafi'i does not allow repetition; instead, the oath is returned to the wali (heir).
The key term here is 'takarrur' (repetition) and 'radd al-yamin' (returning the oath).
3
State the Hanafi position and implication
Hanafi: The oath is repeated from the same individuals to reach fifty oaths. Even after swearing, they remain liable for diyah.
This is based on the Hanafi view that the oath does not exonerate the locality from financial liability.
4
State the Shafi'i position and implication
Shafi'i: The oath is not repeated; if the locality cannot produce fifty men, the oath is taken from the wali. If the locality does swear (i.e., they somehow produce fifty men without repetition), they are exonerated from diyah.
In Shafi'i, swearing frees the locality from liability.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence of the dispute: Under Hanafi, the burden of producing fifty oaths is on the locality, and they remain liable for diyah even after swearing. Under Shafi'i, the burden shifts to the heirs if the locality cannot produce fifty men, and the locality is exonerated if they swear.
This directly affects who pays the diyah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن لم يكن الظاهر شاهدا له فمذهبه مثل مذهبنا غير أنه لا يكرر اليمين بل يردها على الولى فإن حلفوا لا دية عليهم
ترجمہ اور اگر ظاہر حال مدعی کے لئے شاہد نہ ہو تو شافعی کا مذہب ہمارے مذہب کے مثل ہے علاوہ اس بات کے کہ وہ یمین کو مکر نہیں کرتے بلکہ یمین کو ولی پر لوٹا دیتے ہیں پس اگر اہل محلہ نے قسم کھالی تو ان پر دیت نہ ہوگی ۔
تشریح مصنف فرماتے ہیں کہ اگر لوث نہ ہو تو پھر ہمارے مذہب کے مطابق ہیں یعنی امام شافعی کے نزدیک بھی اہل محلہ سے حلف لیا جائے گا، بس ایک فرق ہے کہ اگر اہل محلہ پچاس سے کم ہوں تو ہمارے نزدیک ان سے مکر و قسم لیجائے گی اور شافعی کے نزدیک اب بجائے اہل محلہ کے ولی سے قسم لیجائے گی ، بہر حال اہل محلہ سے قسم کی صورت میں جب انہوں نے قسم کھائی تو امام شافعی کے نزدیک اب اہل محلہ پر دیت واجب نہ ہوگی اور ہمارے نزدیک ہوتی ہے۔ ( کمامر )
And if the apparent circumstance is not a witness for him, then his (Shafi'i's) madhhab is like our madhhab, except that he does not repeat the oath, but returns it to the wali. If they swear, then no diyah is upon them. Translation: And if the apparent circumstance is not a witness for the plaintiff, then Shafi'i's madhhab is similar to our madhhab, except that he does not repeat the oath, but returns the oath to the wali. So if the people of the locality swore, then no diyah is upon them. Commentary: The author says that if there is no lawth, then it is according to our madhhab, i.e., according to Imam Shafi'i, an oath will be taken from the people of the locality as well. There is only one difference: if the people of the locality are fewer than fifty, then according to us (Hanafi), the oath is repeated from them, and according to Shafi'i, instead of the people of the locality, the oath is taken from the wali. In any case, in the scenario where the people of the locality take the oath, according to Imam Shafi'i, diyah is not obligatory upon them, while according to us it is obligatory. (As has passed.)
Source pages p. 26

Commentary
This passage addresses the situation when there is no lawth (circumstantial evidence). The author compares the Hanafi and Shafi'i positions. Both schools agree that in the absence of lawth, the people of the locality are sworn. The only difference is regarding the repetition of oaths when the number of men is less than fifty. In the Hanafi school, if the locality has fewer than fifty men, the oath is repeated among them until the total number of fifty oaths is reached. In the Shafi'i school, the oath is not repeated; instead, the oath is returned to the wali (heir) who swears the required fifty oaths. The practical consequence is that if the locality's men swear (in the Shafi'i view), they are free from diyah; in the Hanafi view, even if they swear, they are still liable for diyah (as established earlier in the chapter). The commentary clarifies that the Shafi'i position on this specific detail aligns with the Hanafi on the basic procedure, but differs on the repetition and consequent liability. This is a key point of dispute within the otherwise similar application of qasama when lawth is absent.

Key Terms
یمین (yamin): An oath; in this context, the oath taken from the locality's men or from the wali in qasama.
تکرر (takarrur): Repetition of the oath; in Hanafi, the same oath is sworn multiple times by the same individuals to reach fifty oaths.
رد یمین (radd al-yamin): Returning the oath to the plaintiff (wali); in Shafi'i school, when the defendants cannot complete fifty oaths, the oath is returned to the heirs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the scenario without lawth, what does the Hanafi school do if there are fewer than fifty men in the locality?
A) They stop the process
B) They repeat the oath until fifty oaths are sworn
C) They transfer the oath to the heirs
D) They acquit the locality

Key Takeaway
In qasama without lawth, the Hanafi school requires oath repetition to reach fifty, and the locality remains liable for diyah; the Shafi'i school returns the oath to the wali if men are fewer, and the locality is exonerated if they swear.

intermediate
8 min
The Oath in Qasamah: Exoneration from Qisas Only
Hanafi rebuttal to Shafi'i's proof on qasamah oath and diyah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school holds that the oath in qasamah exonerates only from qisas and not diyah, and contrast this with the Shafi'i position.

Core Idea
The qasamah oath lifts only qisas; diyah remains due from the community.

Imam al-Shafi'i argued that the oath in qasamah, like any defendant's oath, should completely exonerate the residents from all liability. The Hanafi response, rooted in a precise understanding of the oath's legal purpose, refines this: the oath is prescribed specifically to establish qisas by pressuring a confession. Therefore, its effect is limited to qisas, while diyah is independently imposed due to the slain being found among them or their negligence. This lesson unpacks that rebuttal.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Begin by articulating what the Hanafi school says about the effect of the oath in qasamah: it exonerates the defendants from qisas (retaliation) but not from diyah (blood money).
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Recognize that the opposing school, Imam al-Shafi'i, holds that the oath should exonerate from both qisas and diyah, just as oaths in other claims do.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Understand the Shafi'i argument: the oath is meant to exonerate the defendant from the entire claim, so swearing removes all liability.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Examine the Hanafi rebuttal: the oath only exonerates from the specific right for which it was prescribed. In qasamah, the oath was prescribed to bring qisas to light by prompting confession, so it only affects qisas. Diyah is based on a separate legal basis – the slain being found among the residents or their negligence.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Identify the practical difference: in Hanafi law, swearing residents pay diyah but face no qisas; in Shafi'i law, they would be free from both.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
دوسری دلیل کا جواب
وكذا اليمين مبرئة عما وجب له اليمين والقسامة ما شرعت لتجب الدية إذا نكلوا بل شرعت ليظهر القصاص بتحرزهم عن اليمين الكاذبة فيقروا بالقتل فإذا حلفوا حصلت البراءة عن القصاص ثم الدية تجب بالقتل الموجود منهم ظاهر الوجود القتيل بين أظهرهم لا بنكولهم أو وجبت بتقصيرهم المحافظة كما في القتل الخطأ
ترجمہ اور ایسے ہی یمین اس چیز سے بری کرتی ہے جس کے لئے یمین واجب ہوتی ہو اور قسامت اس لئے مشروع نہیں ہوتی اور چیز ہوا لیے تا کہ دیت واجب ہو جائے جب کہ اہل محلہ انکار کر دیں بلکہ یمین اس لئے مشروع ہوتی ہے تا کہ ان کے جھوٹی قسم سے بچتے ہوئے قصاص ظاہر ہو جائے پس وہ قتل کا اقرار کر لیں پس جب انہوں نے قسم کھالی تو قصاص سے برات حاصل ہوگئی پھر دیت اس قتل کی وجہ سے واجب ہوتی ہے جو ظاہراً ان کی جانب سے پایا گیا ہے مقتول کے ان کے درمیان پائے جانے کی وجہ سے (دیت کا وجوب ) ان کے انکار کی وجہ سے نہیں ہے یا دیت واجب ہوئی ہے ان کی محافظت کے اندر کوتا ہی کرنے کی وجہ سے جیسا کہ قتل خطاء میں ۔
تشریح امام شافعی نے فرمایا تھا کہ یمین تو مدعلی علیہ کو بری کرنے کے لئے مشروع ہے تو یہ اس کا جواب ہے جواب کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ یمین مدعی علیہ کو بری کرنے کیلئے مشروع ہے ہمارا بھی اس اصول سے اتفاق ہے مگر یہ یاد رکھئے کہ یمین اس حق سے بری کرتی ہے جس کے لئے یمین مشروع ہوتی تھی اور یہاں یمین اثبات قصاص کے لئے مشروع ہوئی تھی تا کہ یہ لوگ جھوٹی قسم سے بچنے کی غرض سے قسم سے انکار کر کے قتل کا اقرار کر لیں تو قصاص واجب ہو جاتا لیکن جب انہوں نے قسم کھالی تو اب قصاص واجب نہ ہوگا یعنی ان کی قسموں نے ان کو قصاص سے بری کر دیا ، اب رہادیت کا وجوب تو وہ اس لئے ثابت ہوا کہ قتل ظاہر ا انہیں کی طرف سے صادر ہوا ہے کیونکہ مقتول انہی کے درمیان ملا ہے بہر حال وجوب دیت کا مدار انکار پر نہیں ہے بلکہ اس امر ظاہری پر ہے جو ہم نے ذکر کیا ہے یا پھر دیت ان پر اس لئے واجب ہوئی کہ ان کی جانب سے حفاظت میں کوتاہی اور کمی پائی گئی ہے جیسے قتل خطاء میں بھی اس بنیاد پر دیت واجب ہوا کرتی ہے۔
Second proof's answer: And likewise the oath exonerates from that for which the oath was made obligatory. Qasamah was not prescribed so that diyah becomes obligatory when they refuse; rather it was prescribed so that qisas becomes evident due to their avoidance of a false oath and then they confess to the murder. So when they swear, exoneration from qisas is obtained. Then diyah is obligatory due to the murder that is apparently from them, due to the slain being found among them, not due to their refusal; or it is obligatory due to their negligence in guarding, as in accidental murder.
Source pages p. 30

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute where the Hanafi school rebuts Imam Shafi'i's argument that the oath in qasamah is to exonerate the defendant. The Hanafis agree that the oath exonerates, but only from what it was prescribed for. Here, the oath was prescribed to establish qisas by making the defendants confess to murder to avoid a false oath. If they swear, qisas is lifted, but diyah becomes obligatory due to the apparent fact of the slain being found among them or due to their negligence. Thus, diyah is not tied to their refusal but to the external circumstances.

Key Terms
القسامة (al-qasamah): An oath taken by fifty men of a locality when a slain person is found among them, to deny involvement in the murder.
النكول (al-nukool): Refusal to take the oath, which in qasamah does not by itself impose diyah but leads to imprisonment until the oath is taken.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi response to Shafi'i, what does the oath in qasamah exonerate the defendants from?
A) Both qisas and diyah
B) Qisas only
C) Diyah only
D) Neither qisas nor diyah

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the qasamah oath only removes qisas; diyah is due from the community due to the evident presence of the slain among them or their negligence.

Imprisonment for Refusing the Qasamah Oath
Ruling with proof and comparative analysis

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that a resident who refuses the qasamah oath is imprisoned until he swears, and distinguish this from financial nukool.

Core Idea
The oath in qasamah is wajib for its own sake; refusal leads to imprisonment, not judgment.

In qasamah, the sanctity of blood makes the oath an independent obligation. If a resident refuses to swear, the court does not automatically rule against him; instead, he is imprisoned to compel the oath. This contrasts with financial cases where refusal leads to a judgment. Let's examine the reasoning behind this distinction.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its conditions
The text states: 'Whoever among them refuses the oath shall be imprisoned until he swears.' This is the ruling: imprisonment is the consequence of nukool in qasamah.
The ruling applies to residents of the locality (ahl al-mahallah) who are accused in a qasamah case.
2
Locate the proof (dalil)
The reason given: 'because the oath is due in itself here to honor the matter of blood.' This is a form of istihsan based on the sanctity of blood (ta'zim al-dam).
The proof is not a direct text but a juristic preference grounded in the gravity of homicide.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The phrase 'li'an al-yamin fihi mustahaqqun li-dhatiha' indicates that the oath is wajib independently, not as a substitute. This justifies imprisonment to enforce it, as it is an obligation that cannot be waived by payment.
The legal reasoning connects the oath to the veneration of blood, elevating its status.
4
Compare with financial nukool
In financial cases, nukool leads to a judgment against the defendant because the oath is a substitute for the claim. Paying the claim drops the oath. But in qasamah, paying diyah does not drop the oath; the oath remains wajib.
This contrast highlights the unique nature of qasamah: both oath and diyah are required.
5
Summarize the practical consequence
The mufta bihi position: imprison the refuser until he swears. This is from Zahir al-Riwayah.
There is no intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on this point.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اگر اہل محلہ قسم کھانے سے انکار کر دیں تو قید کیا جائے ومن أبى منهم اليمين حبس حتى يحلف؛ لأن اليمين فيه مستحقة لذاتها تعظيما لأمر الدم ولهذا يجمع بينه وبين الدية بخلاف النكول فى الأموال لأن اليمين بدل عن أصل حقه ولهذا يسقط ببذل المدعى وفيما نحن فيه لا يسقط ببذل الدية
ترجمہ اور اُن میں سے جس نے قسم سے انکار کر دیا تو اس کو قید کیا جائے گا یہاں تک کہ وہ قسم کھائے اس لئے کہ اس میں یمین بذات خود واجب ہے امر دم کی تعظیم کی وجہ سے اور اسی وجہ سے یمین اور دیت کے درمیان جمع کیا جائے گا بخلاف اموال میں انکار کرنے کے، اس لئے کہ یمین اس کے حق کا بدل ہے اور اسی وجہ سے مال مدعی کے صرف کرنے سے یمین ساقط ہو جاتی ہے اور جس مسئلہ میں ہم گفتگو کر رہے ہیں اس میں دیت دینے سے یمین ساقط نہ ہو گی۔
تشریح اگر اہل محلہ میں سے کسی نے قسم سے انکار کر دیا تو جب تک وہ قسم نہ کھائے اس وقت تک اس کو قید میں رکھا جائے گا اس لئے کہ باب قسامت میں مال ہی مقصود نہیں ہے بلکہ یمین بھی مقصود اصل ہے اس لئے کہ یہ خون کا معاملہ ہے جو بہت معظم ہے لہذا یہاں قسم بھی واجب ہے اور دیت بھی واجب ہے البتہ اگر اموال میں مدعی علیہ نے قسم سے انکار کر دیا تو اس کو قید نہیں کیا جائے گا بلکہ اس کے اوپر مال لازم کر دیا جائے گا اسلئے کہ باب اموال میں قسم مدعی کے حق کا بدل ہے اور جب مدعی نے حق ادا کر دیا یعنی مال دیدیا تو یمین ساقط ہو جائے گی لیکن باب قسامت میں اگر اہل محلہ دیت دیدیں تو اس پر اکتفاء نہ ہو گا بلکہ ان کو قسم کھانا بھی لازم ہوگا اور مال دینا بھی۔
And whoever among them refuses the oath shall be imprisoned until he swears, because the oath is due in itself here to honor the matter of blood. For this reason, it is combined with diyah, unlike the refusal in financial matters, because the oath there is a substitute for the original right, and therefore it is dropped by the plaintiff's acceptance of property. In our case, it is not dropped by paying diyah.
Source pages p. 30

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. It states that any resident who refuses to take the qasamah oath will be imprisoned until he swears. The reason is that in qasamah, the oath is obligatory for its own sake to honor the sanctity of blood. Therefore, both the oath and diyah are required. In contrast, in financial cases, refusal (nukool) does not lead to imprisonment; rather, the defendant is forced to pay the claim. In financial matters, the oath is a substitute for the plaintiff's right, so if the plaintiff accepts payment, the oath is dropped. But in qasamah, even if the defendants pay diyah, they must still take the oath because the oath is not a substitute but an independent obligation.

Key Terms
اليمين (al-yameen): A solemn oath taken by the accused to deny involvement in the murder.
النكول (al-nukool): Refusal to take the oath; in qasamah it leads to imprisonment, in financial cases it leads to a ruling against the defendant.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because the oath is a substitute for diyah
B) Because the oath is obligatory for its own sake to honor blood
C) Because he is guilty until proven innocent
D) Because the plaintiff insists on the oath

Key Takeaway
In qasamah, the oath is an independent wajib that must be fulfilled even if diyah is paid; refusal leads to imprisonment.

Application of Qasamah Ruling in Three Scenarios
Extension of the qasamah ruling to claims against all, some unspecified, or specified residents

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three scenarios in which the qasamah ruling applies and explain why the ruling is consistent across them.

Core Idea
The qasamah oath is wajib against a locality's residents whether the guardian accuses all, some unspecified, or specific individuals.

We previously learned the basic rule of qasamah: if a slain person is found in a locality, the residents must collectively swear fifty oaths or pay diyah. This lesson extends that ruling to three distinct scenarios that clarify the scope of the claim. Understanding these scenarios prevents the misconception that specifying the accused lifts the collective responsibility.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base ruling
Recall that qasamah is wajib when a slain person is found in a locality and the murderer is unknown. The residents must take a collective oath.
2
Recognize the three scenarios
The passage lists: (1) claim against all residents, (2) claim against some unspecified residents, (3) claim against specified individuals. Understand that these are the only possibilities when the murderer is unknown.
3
Understand the legal reasoning
Why is the ruling the same in all three? The specified individuals are not distinguishable from the rest in terms of the collective liability. The ambiguity remains because the murderer could be any resident, including the specified one.
The key point: the claim does not remove the ambiguity.
4
Note the authority
This ruling is based on the absolute wording of Imam al-Quduri in his Mukhtasar and confirmed in al-Mabsut, indicating it is the relied-upon Zahir al-Riwayah position.

Source Text

This that we have mentioned applies when the guardian claims murder against all the residents of the locality, and likewise if he claims against some unspecified individuals, whether the claim is for intentional or accidental killing, because they are not distinguishable from the rest. And if he claims against specified individuals that they killed his guardian intentionally or accidentally, the answer is the same. The absolute statement in the book indicates this, and the same answer is in al-Mabsut.
Source pages p. 31

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement clarifying the application of the previous qasamah ruling. It mentions three scenarios where the same ruling (imposition of qasamah and diyah) applies: (1) The guardian claims murder against all residents of the locality. (2) The guardian claims against some unspecified residents (i.e., not naming individuals). (3) The guardian claims against specific named individuals. In all cases, the residents must take the collective oath (qasamah), and if they refuse, they are imprisoned. This is based on the general wording of Imam al-Quduri in his Mukhtasar and confirmed in al-Mabsut.

Key Terms
المحلة (al-mahallah): A locality or residential area where a slain person is found, whose residents are subject to qasamah.
الدعوى (al-da'wa): The legal claim by the guardian of the slain person against the residents.

Key Takeaway
The qasamah ruling is consistent whether the guardian accuses all, some unspecified, or specific residents — the collective liability remains.

Istihsan as a Basis for Qasamah and Diyah on the Locality
Explains istihsan reasoning for qasamah/diyah on locality

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on qasamah and diyah for the locality and distinguish the role of istihsan from qiyas in deriving this ruling.

Core Idea
Qasamah and diyah on the locality are wajib by text, not by analogy, using istihsan.

The Hanafi school holds a unique position on qasamah (oaths) and diyah (blood money) when a murder victim is found in a locality but the killer is unknown. This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind this ruling, focusing on how istihsan (juristic preference) allows the jurist to apply general texts directly, rather than relying on analogy. You will learn to trace the proof structure and identify when analogy is valid and when it is abandoned.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its subject
The ruling is that qasamah and diyah are wajib upon the people of the locality (ahl al-mahallah). Note the legal subject: the entire locality, not a specific accused.
2
Distinguish the two scenarios mentioned
The passage contrasts two scenarios: (1) when the claim is against the locality (where texts apply), and (2) when the claim is against a specific individual outside the locality (where there is no text, so qiyas would be attempted but is invalid).
3
Understand the role of istihsan
Istihsan is employed to apply the general texts to the locality case, overriding the default qiyas that would otherwise require a specific accused. The texts are absolute and do not distinguish between types of claims.
Istihsan here is abandoning a qiyas for a stronger evidence (the general nass).
4
Explain why qiyas is impermissible in the second scenario
If there is no text, one would have to use qiyas, but the original case of qasamah is itself an exception to qiyas (thabit khilaf al-qiyas). Therefore, extending it by qiyas is invalid.
This is a key Hanafi principle: matters proven by nass or ijma cannot be extended by qiyas to new cases if the underlying reason is not shared.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفى الاستحسان تجب القسامة والدية على أهل المحلة لأنه لافصل فى إطلاق النصوص بين دعوى ودعوى فتوجيه بالنص لا بالقياس بخلاف ما إذا ادعى على واحد من غيرهم لأنه ليس فيه نص فلو أو جبناهما الأوجبناهما بالقياس وهو ممتنع
ترجمہ اور استحسان کے اندر اہل محلہ پر قسامت اور دیت واجب ہے اس لئے کہ نصوص کے اطلاق میں ایک دعوئی اور دوسرے دعوئی میں کوئی فرقہ نہیں ہے تو ہم اسکو ( قسامت ودیت کو ) نص سے واجب کریں گے نہ کہ قیاس سے بخلاف اس صورت کے جبکہ ولی نے ان کے غیر میں سے نہ ایک پر دعویٰ کیا ہو اس لئے کہ اس میں نص نہیں ہے پس اگر ہم ان دونوں کو واجب کریں تو ہم ان کو قیاس سے واجب کریں گے اور نہیں ہے۔
تشریح استحسانا تینوں صورتوں میں اہل محلہ پر قسامت اور دیت واجب ہے اس لئے کہ نصوص مطلق ہیں ان میں یہ تفصیل نہیں ہے کہ دعوئی ایسا ہو تو یوں ہے اور ایسا ہو تو یوں ہے توہم نے تیسری صورت کے اندر بھی قسامت اور دیت کو نص سے ثابت کیا ہے قیاس سے نہیں اس لئے کہ نصوص میں امان ہے۔ ہاں اگر اہل محلہ کے علاوہ میں سے کسی ایک پر ولی نے قتل کا دعوی کیا ہو تو پھر اہل محلہ پر نہ قسامت ہے اور نہ دیت ہے۔ کیونکہ اس صورت میں کوئی نص تو ہے نہیں تو اس حکم کا رتبہ قیاس سے کرنا ہوگا اور قیاس یہاں باطل ہے کیونکہ مقیس علیہ خود خلاف قیاس ہے۔
And according to istihsan, qasamah and diyah are obligatory upon the people of the locality because there is no distinction in the absolute application of the texts between one claim and another. So we make them obligatory by text, not by analogy. Unlike the case when he claims against one of those other than them, because there is no text for that. If we made them both obligatory, we would make them by analogy, and that is impermissible. Translation: And according to istihsan, qasamah and diyah are wajib upon the people of the locality because in the absolute application of the texts there is no distinction between one claim and another. So we make them wajib by text, not by qiyas. Unlike when the claimant claims against one person other than them, because there is no text. So if we make both wajib, we make them by qiyas, and that is not allowed. Explanation: By istihsan, in all three cases, qasamah and diyah are wajib upon the people of the locality because the texts are absolute; they do not contain this detail. So we have established qasamah and diyah by text in the third case as well, not by qiyas, because the texts are general. Yes, if the claimant claims murder against one person other than the people of the locality, then there is no qasamah and no diyah upon the people of the locality, because there is no text in this case. So this ruling would have to be made by qiyas, and qiyas is invalid here because the original case itself is contrary to qiyas.
Source pages p. 33

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof using istihsan. The author states that according to istihsan (juristic preference), qasamah and diyah are obligatory upon the people of the locality (ahl al-mahallah) when a murdered person is found there and the murderer is unknown. This is because the texts (nusus) regarding qasamah are general and do not distinguish between a direct claim against a suspect and a claim against the locality. Therefore, the ruling is derived from the text itself, not from analogy (qiyas). In contrast, if the claimant accuses a specific individual outside the locality, there is no text to cover that, so it would require qiyas, but qiyas is invalid here because the original case (qasamah) is itself an exception to qiyas.

Key Terms
قسامة (qasamah): A procedure involving oaths taken by the people of a locality where a murder victim is found, to determine liability.
دية (diyah): Blood money paid as compensation for homicide.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference; a method of reasoning that abandons a qiyas for a stronger evidence.
نص (nass): Textual evidence from Quran or Hadith.
قياس (qiyas): Analogical reasoning.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the basis for making qasamah and diyah obligatory on the people of the locality when the murderer is unknown?
A) Qiyas (analogy) to other cases
B) Nass (text) because the texts are general and do not distinguish
C) Consensus of the companions
D) Personal opinion of the judge

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi ruling on qasamah and diyah for the locality is wajib by text and istihsan, not by analogy.

Ruling on Murder Claim Against a Specific Outsider: Single Oath and Dispute Over Qisas
States legal effects when claim is on a specific outsider

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when a murder claim is made against a specific individual outside the locality and distinguish the consequences for property (diyah) versus retaliation (qisas) claims, including the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.

Core Idea
Murder claim against an outsider: a single oath replaces qasamah; refusal proves property but not qisas without further dispute.

This passage from al-Hidayah clarifies that when a murder claim is made against a specific individual outside the locality, the procedure is not qasamah. The accused takes only one oath. If he swears, he is exonerated. If he refuses, the outcome depends on whether the claim is for diyah (property) or qisas (retaliation). For diyah, the claim is proven by consensus; for qisas, there is a known disagreement between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn. Let us walk through this legal operation step by step.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its context
What is the act being ruled upon? A murder claim against a specific individual outside the locality—this is not a claim against the people of the locality (which would trigger qasamah).
The key is whether the accused is a known individual or part of an unknown group.
2
Determine the proof required
If the claimant has bayyinah (two witnesses), the claim is proven directly. If not, the defendant is asked to take a single oath. Why only one? Because this is not qasamah—qasamah requires fifty oaths and applies only to locality claims.
The absence of nass (text) and the prohibition of qiyas prevent applying qasamah here.
3
Analyse the effect of the oath
If the defendant swears, he is entirely exonerated (bari'). No claim remains against him.
4
Analyse the effect of refusal (nukul)
If the defendant refuses to swear, the ruling splits: for a property claim (diyah), the claim is proven by consensus. For a retaliation claim (qisas), there is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Hanifa holds that the claim is proven; the Sahibayn hold it is not.
The dispute is referred to the Book of Claims (Kitab al-Da'wa) for full details.
5
Identify the practical consequence (thamarah)
According to Abu Hanifa, refusal leads to qisas (retaliation). According to the Sahibayn, only diyah is established. The mufta bihi is not specified here—later works may clarify tarjih.
This difference affects whether the defendant faces execution or only financial liability.

Source Text

ثم حكم ذلك أن يثبت ما ادعاه إذا كان له بينة وإن لم تكن استحلفه يمينا واحدة لأنه ليس بقسامة لانعدام النص وامتناع القياس ثم إن حلف برئ وإن نكل والدعوى فى المال ثبت به وإن كان في القصاص فهو على الاختلاف مضى في كتاب الدعوى

ترجمہ پھر اس کا حکم یہ ہے کہ مدعی جس کا دعویٰ کرتا ہے اس کا ثبوت ہوگا جب کہ اس کے پاس بینہ ہو اور اگر بعینہ نہ ہو تو مدعی علیہ سے ایک سیمین کے ساتھ حلف لے گا اس لئے کہ یہ قسامت نہیں ہے نص نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے اور قیاس کے ممتنع ہونے کی وجہ سے پھر اگر اس نے قسم کھالی تو وہ بری ہو جائے گا اور اگر انکار کر دیا حالانکہ دعوی مال کے سلسلہ میں ہے تو اس سے مال ثابت ہوگا اور اگر دعوی قصاص میں ہے تو وہ اس اختلاف پر ہے جو کتاب الدعویٰ میں گزر چکا ہے۔

تشریح یہاں صاحب ہدایہ یہ واضح کر دینا چاہتے ہیں کہ جب مدعی نے اہل محلہ کے علاوہ کسی غیر شخص پر قتل کا دعویٰ کیا ہو تو اس کا کیا حکم ہے تو فرمایا کہ اگر مدعی کے پاس بینہ ہو تو ولی کا دعوی ثابت ہو جائے گا اور اگر مدعی کے پاس بعینہ نہ ہو تو مدعی مدعی علیہ کو ایک مرتبہ قسم کھلائے گا پچاس قسمیں اس لئے نہیں ہیں کہ یہ قسامت نہیں ہے کیونکہ اس صورت میں نہ نص موجود ہے اور نہ یہاں قیاس ہی کیا جا سکتا ہے اس لئے کہ مقیس عالیہ خود متمتع ہے۔ تو اگر مدعلی علیہ نے قسم کھالی تو وہ بری ہو گیا اور کوئی مہمان اس کے ذمہ نہیں رہا اور اگر مدعی علیہ نے قسم سے انکار کر دیا تو اب دیکھا جائے کہ مدعی کا دعوئی مال میں ہے یا قصاص میں تو اگر اس کا دعوی مال

اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد - ۱۶
باب القسامة

یعنی دیت کے اندر ہو تو مال بالا تفاق ثابت ہو جائے گا اور اگر قصاص میں ہو تو اس میں امام ابو حنیفہ اور صاحبین کا اختلاف ہے یعنی امام صاحب کے نزدیک قصاص کے اندر دعوی ثابت ہوگا اور صاحبین کے نزدیک ثابت نہ ہوگا اس کی بحث کتاب الدعویٰ میں گزرچکی ہے۔
Then the ruling of that is that what he claims is proven if he has evidence, and if not, he makes him take a single oath because it is not qasamah, due to the absence of text and the prohibition of analogy. Then if he swears, he is cleared; and if he refuses, and the claim is for property, it is proven by that; and if it is for retaliation, then it is based on the difference (of opinion) that has passed in the Book of Claims. Translation: Then the ruling of this is that the claimant's claim is proven if he has evidence, and if he does not have evidence, he will make the defendant take a single oath, because this is not qasamah due to the absence of text and the impossibility of qiyas. Then if he swears, he is exonerated; and if he refuses, if the claim is regarding property, then the property is proven; and if the claim is regarding qisas, then it is according to the disagreement that has passed in the Book of Claims. Explanation: Here the author of Hidayah wants to clarify the ruling when the claimant claims murder against a specific person other than the people of the locality. He says that if the claimant has evidence, the claim is proven; and if he does not have evidence, then the claimant will make the defendant take a single oath, not fifty, because this is not qasamah. This is because in this case there is no text and qiyas cannot be performed. So if the defendant swears, he is exonerated; and if he refuses, then it will be seen whether the claim is for property or qisas. If the claim is for diyah, then by agreement the property is proven; and if it is for qisas, then there is a difference of opinion between Abu Hanifa and the two companions: according to Imam Abu Hanifa, the claim for qisas is proven, while according to the two companions, it is not proven. This discussion has passed in the Book of Claims.
Source pages p. 33

Commentary
This passage gives the ruling when a murder claim is against a specific individual outside the locality. The author states that if the claimant has evidence (bayyinah), the claim is proven. If not, the accused takes only one oath (not fifty, because this is not qasamah). If he swears, he is exonerated. If he refuses, and the claim is for property (diyah), the claim is proven against him by consensus. If the claim is for retaliation (qisas), there is a difference of opinion between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani), as detailed in the Book of Claims.

Key Terms
بينة (bayyinah): Evidence, usually two witnesses.
يمين واحدة (yamin wahidah): A single oath, as opposed to the fifty oaths in qasamah.
قصاص (qisas): Retaliation, qatl.
قسامة (qasamah): Fifty oaths required when a murder victim is found in a locality and the killer is unknown.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Murder claims against a specific outsider require only a single oath; refusal to swear establishes property claims by consensus, but for qisas there is a valid intra-Hanafi disagreement.

Who is Exempt from Qasamah: Children, Insane, Women, and Slaves
Clarifies exemptions from qasamah oath

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four categories exempt from qasamah according to the Hanafi school and explain the two distinct legal reasons for their exemption.

Core Idea
Qasamah requires both valid speech and ability to help—those lacking either are exempt.

The institution of qasamah places a collective oath on the locality when a homicide occurs and the killer is unknown. However, not every resident is liable to take this oath. In this passage from al-Quduri, Imam Abu Hanifa specifies four categories of people who are exempt from qasamah. The exemption is based on two distinct legal causes: incapacity for valid speech and inability to provide assistance. Understanding these exemptions clarifies the rationale behind the qasamah procedure.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
The phrase 'لا قسامة على' (no qasamah upon) introduces the legal exemption.
The ruling is negative: qasamah is not required.
2
List the exempt categories
The text mentions four: child (صبي), insane person (مجنون), woman (امرأة), slave (عبد).
These are the only exemptions in the Hanafi school.
3
Extract the two legal causes
The first two are exempt due to lack of qawl sahih (valid speech); the latter two due to lack of nasrah (assistance).
The causes are different.
4
Understand the principle
Qasamah is an oath that requires the capacity to make a valid statement and the ability to provide support in vengeance.
Both conditions must be met for liability.
5
Apply to a scenario
In a village where a body is found, only free adult males are subject; children, insane, women, and slaves are exempt.
Practical application.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ولا قسامة على صبى ولا مجنون؛ لأنهما ليسا من أهل القول الصحيح واليمين قول صحيح. قال ولا امرأة ولا عبد لأنهما ليسا من أهل النصرة واليمين على أهلها

ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور بچہ اور مجنون پر قسامت نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ وہ دونوں قول صحیح کے اہل نہیں ہے اور یمین قول صحیح ہے

قدوری نے فرمایا اور نہ عورت پر اور نہ غلام پر اس لئے کہ یہ دونوں اہل نصرت میں سے نہیں ہیں اور یمین اہل نصرت پر ہے۔ تشریح قسامت میں بچہ اور مجنون عورت اور غلام پر قسم نہ ہوگی اس لئے کہ قسم قول صحیح کو کہتے ہیں اور قسم ان لوگوں پر واجب ہوتی ہے جو مدد کر سکتے ہوں اور یہاں پہلے دونوں قول صحیح نہیں بول سکتے اور آخری دونوں اگر چہ قول صحیح کا تکلم کر سکتے ہیں لیکن مدد نہیں کر سکتے ۔
He said: There is no qasamah upon a child nor a lunatic because they are not from the people of valid speech, and the oath is valid speech. He said: And no woman nor slave because they are not from the people of assistance, and the oath is upon its people. Translation: Quduri said: And there is no qasamah upon a child and a lunatic because both are not from the people of valid speech and the oath is valid speech. Quduri said: And no woman nor slave because both are not from the people of assistance and the oath is upon its people. Explanation: In qasamah, a child, lunatic, woman, and slave will not be sworn because the oath is called valid speech, and the oath is obligatory upon those who can provide help. Here the first two cannot speak valid speech, and the last two although they can speak valid speech, cannot provide help.
Source pages p. 35

Commentary
This passage states a ruling from the Hanafi school regarding who is subject to the oath of qasamah in homicide cases. The matn from al-Quduri lists four categories exempt: a child (sabi) and an insane person (majnun) because they cannot utter a valid oath (qawl sahih), and a woman and a slave because they are not from ahl al-nasrah—those who can provide assistance or support in vengeance. The oath (yamin) is only imposed on those capable of making a valid statement and who are able to lend support. The commentary explains that the first two lack the capacity for valid speech, while the latter two, though capable of speech, lack the ability to provide help. This ruling is based on the definition of yamin as qawl sahih and the condition that qasamah is only on ahl al-nasrah.

Key Terms
القسامة (al-qasamah): The oath taken by the people of a locality in cases of suspected homicide when the killer is unknown, to swear that they did not kill, and if they refuse, they are liable for blood money.
صبي (sabi): A male child who has not reached puberty. In this context, he is not competent to swear a valid oath.
مجنون (majnun): An insane person lacking legal capacity. Cannot swear a valid oath.
امرأة (imra'ah): An adult woman. Exempt from qasamah because she is not from ahl al-nasrah.
عبد ('abd): A slave. Exempt from qasamah because not from ahl al-nasrah.
قول صحيح (qawl sahih): A valid statement that is legally admissible, such as an oath. Child and insane cannot produce it.
يمين (yamin): An oath, which in this context is the oath of qasamah. It is classified as qawl sahih.
نصرة (nasrah): Assistance or support, specifically the ability to help in taking vengeance or defending the locality. Women and slaves are not from ahl al-nasrah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because a slave cannot speak
B) Because a slave is not from ahl al-nasrah
C) Because a slave is always a child
D) Because a slave is insane

Key Takeaway
Children and insane are exempt due to inability to utter a valid oath; women and slaves are exempt due to inability to provide assistance.

Conditions for Qasamah: Need for Injury or Blood from Eye/Ear
Explains when qasamah and diyah are not required due to absence of injury signs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for imposing qasamah and diyah, and identify which physical signs indicate homicide according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Qasamah and diyah require visible signs of homicide; natural orifices do not create presumption of murder.

In the Hanafi school, when a dead body is found, the community may be required to swear oaths (qasamah) and pay blood money (diyah) if homicide is suspected. However, this obligation is not automatic. The text from al-Hidayah lays out a crucial condition: there must be clear physical evidence that the death was caused by violence. Without such evidence, the death is presumed natural, and no qasamah or diyah applies. This lesson examines which specific signs satisfy this condition and which do not, grounding the ruling in customary practice and probability.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal scenario
A dead body is found without any visible trace of violence. The text states that in such a case, no qasamah and no diyah are required.
The default is that death is natural unless signs indicate otherwise.
2
Recognize the rationale
The obligation of qasamah follows the probability (ihtimal) of killing, and diyah follows the action of the killer. Without signs, there is no probability.
Probability, not certainty, triggers qasamah.
3
List the acceptable signs
The text explicitly mentions: a wound (jarahah), trace of beating (athar darb), strangulation (khanaq), or blood coming from the eye or ear.
These signs are deemed reliable indicators of homicide by custom.
4
Distinguish non-indicative signs
Blood from the mouth (fam), anus (dubr), or genitals (dhakar) does not count because these orifices naturally discharge blood without external cause.
This distinction is based on customary observation.
5
Understand the legal outcome
If none of the acceptable signs are present, the body is considered a natural death, and the community bears no liability.
This protects communities from unjust liability.

Source Text

قال وإن وجد ميتا لا أثر به فلا قسامة ولا دية لأنه ليس بقتيل إذا القتيل فى العرف من فاتت حياته بسـ [؟] يباشره حي وهذا ميت حتف أنفه والغرامة تتبع فعل العبد والقسامة تتبع احتمال القتل ثم يجب عليهم القسم فلابد من أن يكون به اثر یستدل به علی کونه قتيلا وذلك بأن يكون به جراحة أو أثر ضرب أو خنق وكذا إذا كان خرج الدم من عينه أو أذنه لأنه لا يخرج منهما إلا بفعل من جهة الحي عادة بخلاف ما إذا خرج من فيه أو دبره أو ذكره لأن الدم يخرج من هذه المخارق عادة بغير فعل أحد وقد ذكرناه في الشهيد

ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور اگر میت پائی جائے جس پر کوئی (قتل کا اثر نہ ہو تو نہ قسامت ہے اور نہ دیت ہے اس لئے کہ وہ مقتول نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ عرف میں مقتول وہ ہے جس کی زندگی ایسے سبب سے فوت ہوئی ہو جس کو کسی زندہ شخص نے کیا ہو اور یہ ایسا امیت ہے جو اپنی موت پر مرا ہے اور تاوان فعل عبد کے تابع ہے اور قسامت احتمال قتل کے تابع ہے پھر ان پر قسم واجب ہوتی ہے تو ضروری ہے کہ ایسا اثر ہو جس سے اس کے مقتول ہونے پر استدلال کیا جاسکے اور وہ یہ ہے کہ زخم ہو یا چوٹ کا اثر ہو یا گلا گھونٹنے کا اور ایسے ہی جبکہ اس کی آنکھ یا کان سے خون نکل رہا ہو اس لئے کہ ان دونوں سے عادہ خون نہیں نکلتا مگر زندہ کی جانب سے کسی فعل کی وجہ سے بخلاف اس صورت کے جب کہ خون اس کے منھ یا اسکی ڈبر [؟] یا اس کے ذکر سے نکلے اس لئے کہ ان منافذ سے بغیر کسی کے فعل کے عادہ خون نکل جاتا ہے اور ہم اس کو باب الشہید میں ذکر کر چکے ہیں۔

تشریح اگر کسی محلہ میں کوئی مرا ہوا انسان ملا لیکن اس پر قتل کا کوئی اثر نہیں ہے نہ کوئی زخم ہے نہ مارنے پیٹنے کا کوئی اثر ہے نہ گلا گھونٹنے کا کوئی اثر ہے نہ اس کی آنکھ سے اور کان سے خون جاری ہے تو یہ مقتول نہیں ہے بلکہ اپنی موت مرا ہے اور قسامت اور دیت مقتول میں واجب ہوتی ہے لہذا یہاں نہ قسامت ہے اور نہ دیت ہے کیونکہ یہاں نہ قتل ہے اور نہ احتمال قتل ہے۔ اور اسکے ذکر سے خون جاری ہو یاد ہبر [؟] سے یا منھ سے تو وہ قتل نہ ہوگا کیونکہ ان مقامات سے بھی عاوہ [؟] خود بخود بھی خون رکھتا ہے بغیر دوسرے کے کچھ کئے ہوئے

باب الشہید میں بھی اس کا بیان گزر چکا ہے۔
He said: And if a dead body is found without any trace, then no qasamah and no diyah because it is not a slain person. For the slain person in custom is one whose life ended by a cause that a living person directly caused, and this is one who died a natural death. The indemnity follows the action of the slave, and qasamah follows the possibility of killing. Then the oath is obligatory upon them, so it is necessary that there be a trace by which it can be inferred that he was killed. That is by there being a wound, or trace of beating, or strangulation. Likewise if blood has come out of his eye or ear because it does not come out from them except by an act from the living person usually, contrary to if it comes out of his mouth, anus, or genitals because blood comes out from these orifices usually without anyone's action. And we have mentioned it in the chapter of the martyr. 

Translation: Quduri said: And if a dead body is found upon which there is no trace of killing, then no qasamah and no diyah because he is not killed. Because customarily the killed is one whose life has ended by a cause that a living person has done, and this is a dead person who died his natural death. And the penalty follows the action of the slave, and qasamah follows the probability of killing. Then upon them the oath is obligatory, so it is necessary that there be a trace by which it can be inferred that he was killed, and that is that there be a wound or a trace of beating or strangling. Similarly when blood has come out of his eye or ear, because from these two blood does not usually come out except due to an act from the living, unlike the case when blood comes out of his mouth or his anus or his genitals, because from these orifices blood usually comes out without anyone's action. And we have mentioned this in the chapter of the martyr.

Explanation: If a dead human is found in a locality but there is no trace of murder, no wound, no trace of beating, no trace of strangulation, and no blood flowing from his eye and ear, then this is not a slain person but died naturally. And qasamah and diyah are obligatory only for a slain person, so here no qasamah and no diyah. And if blood flows from his genitals, anus, or mouth, then it is not murder because from these places blood also flows naturally without anyone doing anything. This has already been mentioned in the chapter of the martyr.
Source pages p. 35

Commentary
This passage discusses the requirement for qasamah to be imposed on the people of a locality: there must be clear signs that the death was caused by homicide. If a dead body is found without any trace of violence—no wounds, no bruises, no signs of strangulation, and no blood from the eye or ear—then it is presumed to be a natural death, and no qasamah or diyah applies. The text also distinguishes between orifices: blood from the eye or ear indicates foul play because it does not come out naturally, whereas blood from the mouth, anus, or genitals does not indicate homicide because these orifices naturally discharge blood. This ruling is based on customary practice and probability of murder.

Key Terms
قتيل (qatil): A person who has been killed by another. In this context, a dead body with signs of homicide.
أثر (athar): Trace or sign of violence indicating homicide, such as wounds or blood from eye/ear.
جراحة (jarahah): A wound or injury that indicates the deceased was killed.
ضرب (darb): Beating or striking that leaves traces.
خنق (khanaq): Strangulation, which leaves traces.
عين ('ayn): Eye. Blood from the eye is a sign of homicide.
أذن (udhun): Ear. Blood from the ear is a sign of homicide.
فم (fam): Mouth. Blood from the mouth is not considered a sign of homicide because it can occur naturally.
دبر (dubr): Anus. Blood from the anus is not a sign of homicide.
ذكر (dhakar): Male genitals. Blood from there is not a sign of homicide.
احتمال قتل (ihtimal qatl): The probability or likelihood of homicide, which is a basis for qasamah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, which of the following is NOT considered a sign of homicide for the purpose of qasamah?
A) A wound on the body
B) Blood from the ear
C) Blood from the mouth
D) Traces of strangulation

Key Takeaway
Qasamah and diyah require visible signs of homicide; blood from the mouth, anus, or genitals does not count as such a sign.

Diyat — Blood Money
intermediate
8 min
Rulings on Qasamah and Diyah When Body Parts Are Found
Details of qasamah/diyah application based on body parts found

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which qasamah and diyah become obligatory when a slain person's body is found, and apply the general principle to sequential finds.

Core Idea
Qasamah and diyah apply only when the majority of the body or half with head is found out of reverence for human life.

When a slain body is discovered, Islamic law prescribes qasamah (a collective oath) and diyah (blood money) on the locality. However, these obligations are not triggered by every body part. The Hanafi school defines precise thresholds based on the proportion of the body found. This lesson unpacks those thresholds and explains a general principle that prevents double liability when parts are found sequentially.

Guided Path
1
Identify the trigger amounts
Determine which combinations of body parts make qasamah and diyah obligatory: entire body, more than half, or half with the head.
Less than half, even with head, or isolated limbs do not trigger.
2
Understand the textual basis
Recognize that this ruling is based on textual evidence (nas) and is not derived by analogy. It is restricted to the cases explicitly mentioned.
The text says 'this is a ruling we have known from the text'.
3
Apply the majority-as-whole principle
Note that the majority of the body (akthar) is treated as the whole body out of reverence for the human being (ta'zim lil-adami).
This is an exception that expands the scope of the rule.
4
Apply the general principle for sequential finds
Learn the qa'idah kulliyyah: if the first part found is of a type that would trigger qasamah if the rest were found, then qasamah is not obligatory yet. Conversely, if the first part would not trigger qasamah even with the rest, then qasamah becomes obligatory.
This prevents two qasamahs for one soul.
5
Note the analogy with funeral prayer
Like qasamah, funeral prayer (salat al-janazah) is not repeated for the same deceased, following the same principle.
This illustrates the qa'idah's application beyond diyat.

Source Text

ترجمہ اور اگر مقتول کا بدن یا بدن کے نصف سے زیادہ یا نصف اور اس کا سر کسی محلہ میں پایا جائے تو اہل محلہ پر قسامت اور دیت واجب ہے اور اگر اس کا نصف ہے جو لمبائی میں چراہوا ہو یا نصف سے کم ہو اور اسکے ساتھ سر ہو یا اس کا ہاتھ یا اس کا پیر یا اس کا سر ملے تو اہل محلہ پر کچھ نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ یہ ایسا حکم ہے جس کو ہم نے نص سے جانا ہے اور نص اس حکم کے بارے میں بدن کے اندر وارد ہوئی ہے مگر اکثر کے لئے کل کا حکم ہے آدمی کی تعظیم کی وجہ سے۔

قسامت ہونے اور نہ ہونے کے سلسلے میں قاعدہ کلیہ

بخلاف الأقل لأنه ليس ببدن ولا ملحق به فلانجرى فيه القسامة ولأنا لو اعتبرناه تتكرر القسامتان والديتان بمقابلة نفس واحدة ولاتتواليان والأصل فيه أن الموجود الأول إن كان بحال لو وجد الباقى تجرى فيه القسامة لاتجب فيه وإن كان بحال لو وجد الباقى لاتجرى فيه القسامة تجب والمعنى ما أشرنا إليه وصلاة الجنازة فى هذا تنسحب على هذا الأصل؛ لأنها لا تتكرر

ترجمہ بخلاف اقل کے اس لئے کہ وہ بدن نہیں ہے اور نہ بدن کے ساتھ ملحق ہے تو اس میں قسامت جاری نہ ہوگی اور اگر ہم اقل کا اعتبار کریں تو دو قسامت اور دودیت واجب ہوں گی ایک نفس کے مقابلہ میں حالانکہ یہ دونوں (قسامت ودیت) پے در پے نہیں ہوتیں اور اس میں قاعدہ کلیہ یہ ہے کہ موجود اول اگر اس حال پر ہو کہ اگر باقی پایا جائے تو اس میں قسامت جاری ہو تو اس میں ( موجود اوّل میں ) قسامت واجب نہ ہوگی اور اگر وہ (موجود اول ) اس حال پر ہو کہ اگر باقی پایا جائے تو اس میں قسامت جاری نہ ہوتو قسامت واجب ہوگی اور وجہ اصلی ہے جس کی جانب ہم اشارہ کر چکے ہیں اور اس میں جنازہ کی نماز اسی اصل پر متفرع ہے اس لیئے نماز جنازہ مقرر نہیں ہوگی۔ تشریح ہاں اگر اقل حصہ پایا گیا ہے تو چونکہ یہ نہ پورا دن ہے اور نہ اس کے ساتھ ملحق ہے لہذا اس میں قسامت واجب نہ ہوگی
And if the body of the slain person is found, or more than half of the body, or half with the head, in a locality, then upon its people is the qasamah and the diyah. And if his half is found split lengthwise, or less than half is found with the head, or his hand or his leg or his head is found, then nothing upon them. Because this is a ruling we have known from the text (nas), and it has come concerning the body, except that the majority has the ruling of the whole out of respect for the human being.

Translation: And if the body of the slain, or more than half of the body, or half with his head, is found in a locality, then upon the people of the locality are qasamah and diyah. And if his half is split lengthwise, or less than half is found with his head, or his hand or his foot or his head is found, then nothing upon them. Because this is a ruling we have known from the text, and the text has come concerning the body, but the majority has the ruling of the whole due to the reverence of the human being.

Explanation: If the entire body of the slain or most of it is found in a locality, then qasamah and diyah are obligatory upon the people of the locality. And if less than half is found, even if with his head, or only the head, foot, or hand is found, then neither qasamah nor diyah is obligatory. This is because this specific ruling of qasamah and diyah is not established by analogy but by text (nas), contrary to analogy. So it is restricted to the heard case, and the heard case is the entire body. But out of caution and reverence for the human being, the majority of the body is made to stand in for the entire body.

General rule regarding whether qasamah applies or not:

Contrary to the lesser (amount) because it is not a body nor attached to it, so qasamah does not run in it. And if we consider the lesser, two qasamahs and two diyahs would be required in exchange for one soul, and they do not come consecutively. The principle in this is that the first found, if it is in a condition that if the rest were found qasamah would run in it, then qasamah is not obligatory upon it. And if it is in a condition that if the rest were found qasamah would not run in it, then qasamah is obligatory. And the meaning is what we have indicated. The funeral prayer (salat al-janazah) in this is derived from this principle because it is not repeated.

Translation: Contrary to the lesser, because it is not a body nor attached to the body, so qasamah will not run in it. And if we consider the lesser, two qasamahs and two diyahs would become obligatory in exchange for one soul, while they (qasamah and diyah) do not occur consecutively. And in this the general rule is that the first found, if it is in a condition that if the rest were found qasamah would run in it, then qasamah is not obligatory in it. And if it (the first found) is in a condition that if the rest were found qasamah would not run in it, then qasamah is obligatory. And the primary reason is what we have indicated. The funeral prayer is derived from this principle because it is not repeated.
Explanation: Yes, if a lesser portion is found, since it is neither a complete body nor attached to it, therefore qasamah is not obligatory in it.
Source pages p. 36

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on Al-Hidayah addresses the ruling when a dead body is found in parts. The Hanafi ruling is that if the entire body, or more than half, or half with the head is found in a locality, then the people of that locality are subject to qasamah and liable for diyah. However, if less than half is found—even if the head, hand, or foot is found—no qasamah or diyah applies. The ruling is derived from textual evidence (nas) and is not based on analogy. The majority of the body is treated as the whole out of respect for human dignity. A general principle is given: when body parts are found in separate instances, we look at the first part found: if the condition of that part is such that if the rest were later found and would trigger qasamah, then qasamah is not obligatory on the first part alone. Conversely, if the first part found is of a nature that even if the rest were found, qasamah would not apply (because the first part is less than half), then qasamah is obligatory on the first find. This prevents the possibility of double qasamah for the same soul. The same principle applies to funeral prayer: it is not repeated for the same body.

Key Terms
بدن (badan): The entire body of the slain person. The text specifies that the ruling of qasamah is tied to the body.
نصف (nisf): Half of the body. When half is found with the head, qasamah applies. If half is split lengthwise (two halves), it does not.
أكثر (akthar): More than half of the body; treated as the whole body for qasamah.
أقل (aqall): Less than half of the body; does not trigger qasamah.
رأس (ra's): Head. When found alone or with less than half, no qasamah.
يد (yad): Hand. Found alone does not trigger qasamah.
رجل (rijl): Foot or leg. Found alone does not trigger qasamah.
قاعدة كلية (qa'idah kulliyyah): A comprehensive legal principle governing the application of qasamah when body parts are found in separate instances.
تكرار (takrar): Repetition. The principle prevents double qasamah/diyah for the same soul.
صلاة الجنازة (salat al-janazah): Funeral prayer. Analogous to qasamah in that it is not repeated for the same deceased.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a slain person's leg is found alone in a locality, does qasamah apply?
A) Yes, because a leg is a significant part of the body.
B) No, because a leg alone is less than half of the body.
C) Yes, but only if the head is also found later.
D) No, because the ruling applies only when the entire body is found.

Key Takeaway
Qasamah and diyah are only obligatory when the majority of the body or half with the head is found; lesser parts do not trigger liability, and a general principle prevents double liability for the same soul.

Diyat — Blood Money

When Qasamah and Diyah Are Due on the Locality for a Found Body
Ruling on when a complete or partial body triggers the oath and blood money

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions that trigger qasamah and diyah on the locality for a found body, distinguish between the majority (akthar) and the lesser (aqall), and apply the general principle for sequential discovery of body parts.

Core Idea
Qasamah and diyah are wajib only for the whole body or its majority, not for lesser parts.

This passage from Al-Hidayah specifies when the inhabitants of a locality become liable for qasamah (oath-taking) and diyah (blood money) upon finding a dead body. It clarifies that only a complete body or more than half (or half with head) triggers this obligation; a lesser part does not. The ruling is based on textual evidence (nas) and is an exception to qiyas. Furthermore, a detailed principle is given for cases where body parts are found in stages, to prevent double liability. Understanding these rules is essential for applying the exceptional institution of qasamah correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the triggering conditions
List the cases where qasamah and diyah are wajib: whole body, more than half, half with head.
The text treats 'majority' (akthar) as equivalent to the whole out of respect for the human being.
2
Identify the non-triggering cases
List the cases where nothing is due: half split lengthwise, less than half with head, or a limb (hand, foot, head) alone.
These are excluded because the text only applies to the body (badan) or what is annexed to it.
3
Understand the textual basis
Recognize that this ruling is established by nas (text), not qiyas. It is an exceptional rule limited to the scope of the text.
Qasamah is contrary to general principles (khilaf al-qiyas), so it is restricted to the proven cases.
4
Apply the general principle for sequential findings
If body parts are found in stages, look at the first part. If finding the remaining part would itself trigger qasamah, then the first part does not; if the remaining would not trigger, then the first does.
This prevents repetition of qasamah and diyah for one soul. The same principle applies to funeral prayer.
5
Relate to funeral prayer analogy
Note that the rule for funeral prayer (salat al-janazah) follows the same logic: it is not repeated for one body, so similar sequential rule applies.
This shows consistency in the Hanafi approach to exceptional rulings.

Source Text
