باب القسامة
باب الشہید میں بھی اس کا بیان گزر چکا ہے۔
کن کن صورتوں میں اہل محلہ پر قسامت اور دیت ہے
ولو وجد بدن القتيل أو أكثر من نصف البدن أو النصف ومعه الرأس في محلة فعلى أهلها القسامة والدية وإن وجد نصفه مشقوقا بالطول أو وجد أقل من النصف ومعه الرأس أو وجد يده أو رجله أو رأسه فلاشيء عليهم؛ لأن هذا حكم عرفناه بالنص وقد ورد به فى البدن إلا أن للأكثر حكم الكل تعظيما للآدمي
ترجمہ اور اگر مقتول کا بدن یا بدن کے نصف سے زیادہ یا نصف اور اس کا سر کسی محلہ میں پایا جائے تو اہل محلہ پر قسامت اور دبیت واجب ہے اور اگر اس کا نصف ہے۔ جو لمبائی میں چراہوا ہو یا نصف سے کم ہو اور اسکے ساتھ سر ہو یا اس کا ہاتھ یا اس کا پیر یا اس کا سر ملے تو اہل محلہ پر کچھ نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ یہ ایسا حکم ہے جس کو ہم نے نص سے جانا ہے اور نص اس حکم کے بارے میں بدن کے اندر وارد ہوئی ہے مگر اکثر کے لئے کل کا حکم ہے آدمی کی تعظیم کی وجہ سے۔
تشریح اگر مقتول کا پورا بدن یا اس کا اکثر حصہ کسی محلہ میں ملے تو اہل محلہ پر قسامت اور دیت واجب ہے اور اگر نصف سے کم ملے خواہ اس کا سر بھی ہو یا فقط سر پاؤں یا ہاتھ ملے تو نہ قسامت واجب ہے اور نہ دیت کیونکہ مقتول کے بارے میں یہ مخصوص حکم یعنی قسامت ودیت قیاس سے ثابت نہیں بلکہ نص سے خلاف قیاس ثابت ہے تو اسکے مور د سماع پر مخصر کیا جائے گا اور مور دسماع پورا بدن ہے مگر بر بناء احتیاط اور انسان کی تعظیم کے پیش نظر اکثر بدن کو کل بدن کے قائم مقام کر دیا گیا ہے۔
قسامت ہونے اور نہ ہونے کے سلسلے میں قاعدہ کلیہ
بخلاف الأقل لأنه ليس ببدن ولا ملحق به فلانجرى فيه القسامة ولأنا لو اعتبرناه تتكرر القسامتان والديتان بمقابلة نفس واحدة ولاتتواليان والأصل فيه أن الموجود الأول إن كان بحال لو وجد الباقى تجرى فيه القسامة لاتجب فيه وإن كان بحال لو وجد الباقى لاتجرى فيه القسامة تجب والمعنى ما أشرنا إليه وصلاة الجنازة فى هذا تنسحب على هذا الأصل؛ لأنها لا تتكرر
ترجمہ بخلاف اقل کے اس لئے کہ وہ بدن نہیں ہے اور نہ بدن کے ساتھ ملحق ہے تو اس میں قسامت جاری نہ ہوگی اور اگر ہم اقل کا اعتبار کریں تو دو قسامت اور دودیت واجب ہوں گی ایک نفس کے مقابلہ میں حالانکہ یہ دونوں (قسامت ودیت) پے در پے نہیں ہوتیں اور اس میں قاعدہ کلیہ یہ ہے کہ موجود اول اگر اس حال پر ہو کہ اگر باقی پایا جائے تو اس میں قسامت جاری ہو تو اس میں ( موجود اوّل میں ) قسامت واجب نہ ہوگی اور اگر وہ (موجود اول ) اس حال پر ہو کہ اگر باقی پایا جائے تو اس میں قسامت جاری نہ ہوتو قسامت واجب ہوگی اور وجہ اصلی ہے جس کی جانب ہم اشارہ کر چکے ہیں اور اس میں جنازہ کی نماز اسی اصل پر متفرع ہے اس لیئے نماز جنازہ مقرر نہیں ہوگی۔ تشریح ہاں اگر اقل حصہ پایا گیا ہے تو چونکہ یہ نہ پورا دن ہے اور نہ اس کے ساتھ ملحق ہے لہذا اس میں قسامت واجب نہ ہوگی
اور دوسری وجہ یہ بھی ہے کہ اگر اقل کا اعتبار کر کے قسامت اور دیت واجب کر دی جائے تو پھر اکثر بدن کے ملنے سے قسامت اور دیت واجب ہوگی تو قسامت اور دیت کا تکرار لازم آئے گا حالانکہ قسامت اور دیت میں تکرار نہیں ہے اس کے متعلق مصنف نے ایک قاعدہ کلیہ بیان فرمایا ہے کہ یوں دیکھ لو کہ اب جو حصہ آپ کو ملا ہے اگر بعد میں اور حصہ بھی مل جائے تو اس دوسرے پر قسامت اور دیت واجب ہوگی یا نہیں اگر دوسرے میں قسامت و دیت ہو تو پہلے میں واجب نہ ہوگی اور اگر دوسرے میں واجب نہ ہوتی ہو پہلے میں واجب ہوگی اور اس قاعدہ کی بھی یہی وجہ ہے کہ قسامت اور دیت میں تکرار لازم نہ آئے اور نماز جنازہ کا بھی یہی حکم ہے یعنی اگر بدن کا کچھ حصہ ملا ہے تو دوسرے کو دیکھو کہ اگر وہ مل جائے تو اس پر نماز جنازہ ہوگی یا نہیں اگر ہو تو اول حصہ پر نہ ہوگی اور اگر دوسرے پر نہ ہو تو اول حصہ پر نماز جنازہ ہوگی۔ اس لئے کہ نماز جنازہ بھی مکرر نہیں ہوتی ، فلیتا مل۔
( محمد یوسف )
Chapter of Qasamah: The statement regarding it has also passed in the chapter of the martyr. In which cases are qasamah and diyah upon the people of the locality? If the body of the killed person is found, or more than half of the body, or half with the head in a locality, then upon its people are qasamah and diyah. And if half of it is found split lengthwise, or less than half with the head, or his hand, his foot, or his head is found, then nothing upon them; because this is a ruling we know by textual evidence, and it has been reported regarding the body. However, the majority has the ruling of the whole out of reverence for the human being. Translation: If the body of the killed person or more than half of the body or half and his head are found in a locality, then qasamah and diyah are obligatory upon the people of the locality. And if half of it is split lengthwise, or less than half with the head, or his hand, or his foot, or his head is found, then nothing upon them; because this is a ruling we know from the text, and the text has come regarding the body. But for the majority, the ruling of the whole is given, due to reverence for the human being. Explanation: If the whole body or most of it is found in a locality, then qasamah and diyah are obligatory. But if less than half is found, even if with his head or only head, foot, or hand, then neither qasamah nor diyah is obligatory. Because this specific ruling of qasamah and diyah is not established by analogy but by text, contrary to analogy. So it is limited to its proven scope, which is the whole body. But out of precaution and reverence for humans, the majority is substituted for the whole. The general rule regarding whether qasamah occurs or not: Contrary to the lesser, because it is neither a body nor attached to it, so qasamah will not be applied. And if we consider the lesser, two qasamahs and two diyahs would be required for one soul, and they are not consecutive. The principle is that the first found, if in such a state that if the remainder were found qasamah would apply, then qasamah is not required upon it; and if in such a state that if the remainder were found qasamah would not apply, then qasamah is required. The meaning is what we have indicated. The funeral prayer is related to this principle because it is not repeated. Translation: Contrary to the lesser, because it is not a body nor annexed to it, so qasamah will not be applied. And if we consider the lesser, two qasamahs and two diyahs would be obligatory for one soul, while these two (qasamah and diyah) do not occur consecutively. The general rule is that the first found, if in such a state that if the rest were found qasamah would apply, then qasamah is not obligatory upon it; and if the first found is in such a state that if the rest were found qasamah would not apply, then qasamah is obligatory. The reason is what we have indicated. The funeral prayer is branched upon this principle because it is not repeated. Explanation: Yes, if a lesser part is found, since it is neither a whole body nor annexed to it, therefore qasamah is not obligatory. And the second reason is that if we consider the lesser and make qasamah and diyah obligatory, then later when the majority of the body is found, qasamah and diyah would be obligatory again, leading to repetition of qasamah and diyah, while they are not repeated. Regarding this, the author stated a general rule: Look at the part you have now; if later another part is found, would qasamah and diyah be obligatory on that second part? If yes, then the first part does not require qasamah; if not, then the first part does. This is to avoid repetition. The same applies to funeral prayer: look at the part found; if a later part would require funeral prayer, the first does not; otherwise, it does. Because funeral prayer is also not repeated. (Muhammad Yusuf)
Source pages p. 36

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the text. It first establishes that when a complete body or more than half (or half with head) is found in a locality, the inhabitants bear qasamah (oath-taking) and diyah (blood money). However, if half is split lengthwise, or less than half with head, or a limb like hand, foot, or head alone is found, nothing is due. The proof is that this ruling is known from the text (nas) specifically for the body, and the majority is treated as the whole out of reverence for human dignity. The text is an exception to qiyas (analogy) because qasamah would not normally be imposed on a locality without a complete body. The passage then presents a general principle (qaidah kulliyyah) to handle cases where body parts are found in stages: the obligation depends on whether the later part would itself trigger qasamah. If the later part would trigger it, the first part does not; if not, the first does. This prevents repetition of qasamah and diyah for one soul. The same principle applies to funeral prayer (salat al-janazah), which also cannot be repeated for one body. This is a distinctive Hanafi position that emphasizes the exceptional nature of the ruling and the need for caution and respect for the deceased.

Key Terms
قسامة (qasāmah): An oath-taking procedure used to determine liability for a found dead body, administered to the people of the locality.
دية (diyah): Blood money or monetary compensation paid for unlawful killing, required from the locality in these cases.
بدن (badan): The entire body of the deceased; the complete physical structure.
أكثر (akthar): More than half of the body, considered as the whole body for the purpose of qasamah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a severed hand of a body is found in a locality but no other parts, what is the ruling on the people of the locality regarding qasamah and diyah?
A) They must perform qasamah and pay diyah.
B) They must perform qasamah but not pay diyah.
C) They are not obligated to perform qasamah or pay diyah.
D) They must pay diyah but not perform qasamah.

Key Takeaway
Qasamah and diyah are an exceptional obligation limited to cases where the complete body or its majority is found in a locality; lesser parts impose no liability.

Conditions for Qasamah and Diyah on a Found Fetus or Premature Child
Ruling on found fetus or premature child with or without signs of beating

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two conditions that make qasamah and diyah obligatory for a found fetus and apply them to distinguish when the locality is liable.

Core Idea
A fully formed child with beating wounds triggers qasamah and diyah; an incomplete child does not—presumption of stillbirth overrides.

When a fetus or prematurely born child is found dead in a locality, the question arises: who is liable? The Hanafi school sets clear boundaries: liability depends on whether the child was complete in creation and whether there are signs of beating. This ruling relies on rational presumptions (zahir) about live birth and cause of death. Understanding these conditions is essential for correctly applying the law of qasamah and diyah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The text presents two main scenarios: when a fetus/premature child is found (a) without any trace of beating, and (b) with a trace of beating. In each, further subdivide based on completeness of creation.
2
Distinguish complete vs incomplete creation
Define 'tam al-khalq' (full limbs, presumed viable) and 'naqis al-khalq' (missing/undeveloped, presumed stillborn). This distinction is central to the ruling.
3
Apply the rule for complete child with wounds
If both conditions (complete creation + beating signs) are met, qasamah and diyah are wajib because the apparent (zahir) is that the child was born alive and then killed.
4
Apply the rule for incomplete child even with wounds
If the child is incomplete, even with beating signs, no liability attaches because the presumption is that the child was stillborn; the wounds may be from birth or postmortem.
5
Note the cross-madhhab difference
Some schools may hold any child with wounds as a homicide victim regardless of completeness. The Hanafi school insists on completeness as a condition for the presumption of live birth.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf.

Source Text

ولو وجد فيهم جنين أو سقط ليس به أثر الضرب فلاشيء على أهل المحلة؛ لأنه لا يفوق الكبير حالا وإن كان به أثر الضرب وهو تام الخلق وجبت القسامة والدية عليهم؛ لأن الظاهر أن تام الخلق ينفصل حيا وإن كان ناقص الخلق فلاشيء عليهم؛ لأنه ينفصل ميتا لا حيا
ترجمہ اور اگر اہل محلہ کے درمیان جنین پایا جائے یا نا تمام گرا ہوا بچہ جس پر ضرب کا اثر نہ ہوتو اہل محلہ پر کوئی چیز نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ جنین حالت میں بڑے آدمی سے نہیں بڑھے گا اور اگر اس پر ضرب کا اثر ہو اور وہ تام الخلق ہو تو اہل محلہ پر قسامت اور دیت واجب ہے اس لئے کہ ظاہر یہی ہے کہ نام اخلاق زندہ جدا ہوتا ہے اور اگر وہ ناقص الخلق ہو تو ان پر کوئی چیز نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ وہ مردہ جدا ہوتا ہے نہ کہ زندہ
تشریح اور اگر محلہ والوں کے درمیان وہ بچہ ملا جو بھی جنین تھا مگر اب پیدا ہو گیا ہے اور محلہ میں پڑا ہے یا بچہ نا تمام ہے لیکن اس پر زخم الضرب کا کوئی اثر نہیں تو اہل محلہ پر کچھ بھی واجب نہ ہوگا کیونکہ اگر بڑا آدمی بھی مردہ پایا جاتا اور اس پر کوئی اثر نہ ہوتا تب بھی اہل محلہ پر دبیت واجب نہیں تھی لہذا اب بھی واجب نہ ہوگی اور اگر اس پر ضرب کا اثر ہو اور اعضاوا سکے سب بن چکے ہوں یعنی وہ تام الخلق ہو تو اب اہل محلہ پر قسامت اور دیت واجب ہوگی اس لئے کہ یہاں ظاہر یہی ہے کہ وہ اپنی ماں سے زندہ پیدا ہوا ہے اور اس کو کسی نے مارا ہے، اور اگر وہ ناقص الخلق ہو تو ان پر کچھ واجب نہ ہوگا اس لئے کہ یہاں ظاہر یہ ہے کہ وہ ماں کے پیٹ سے مردہ پیدا ہوا ہے نہ کہ زندہ۔
If a fetus or a prematurely shed (child) is found among them without any trace of beating, then nothing is upon the people of the locality; because it does not surpass the status of an adult. And if there is a trace of beating on it and it is complete in creation, then qasamah and diyah are obligatory upon them; because the apparent is that the complete in creation is separated alive. And if it is incomplete in creation, then nothing upon them; because it separates dead, not alive. Translation: And if a fetus is found among the people of the locality, or an incomplete fallen child that has no trace of beating, then nothing is due on the people of the locality; because a fetus in the womb does not surpass the status of an adult. And if there is a trace of beating on it and it is complete in creation, then qasamah and diyah are obligatory upon them; because the apparent is that the complete in creation is born alive. And if it is incomplete in creation, then nothing upon them; because it is born dead, not alive. Explanation: If among the people of the locality, a child is found that was a fetus but has now been born and lies in the locality, or the child is incomplete but there is no trace of beating, then nothing is obligatory upon the locality; because even if an adult was found dead with no trace, no diyah would be due. So here too it is not due. And if there is a trace of beating and all the limbs are complete, i.e., it is complete in creation, then qasamah and diyah are obligatory; because the apparent is that it was born alive from its mother and someone killed it. And if it is incomplete, nothing is due; because the apparent is that it was born dead from the womb, not alive.
Source pages p. 37

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling about finding a fetus or prematurely born child in a locality. The ruling distinguishes between three factors: (1) presence or absence of signs of beating, (2) completeness of creation (tam al-khalq vs. naqis al-khalq), and (3) the implication for qasamah and diyah. If there is no trace of beating, nothing is due regardless of completeness, because a dead body without wounds does not trigger these penalties even for an adult. If there are signs of beating and the child is fully formed (complete limbs), then qasamah and diyah are obligatory because the presumption (zahir) is that the child was born alive and then killed. If the child is incomplete (e.g., missing limbs or prematurely undeveloped), even with wounds, nothing is due because the presumption is that it was stillborn, and the wounds may have occurred after death or from the birth process. This ruling is based on rational presumption (dalil aqli) rather than explicit text, although it aligns with the overall principles of the bab.

Key Terms
جنين (janīn): A fetus or unborn child; also used here for a prematurely born child that may be incomplete.
تام الخلق (tām al-khalq): A child born with all limbs and features complete; presumed viable and born alive.
ناقص الخلق (nāqis al-khalq): A child born with missing or underdeveloped limbs; presumed stillborn.
أثر الضرب (athar al-ḍarb): Trace or mark of beating; physical evidence of violence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A newborn baby with all limbs complete is found dead in a locality, with visible signs of beating. According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on the people of the locality?
A) They are liable for qasamah and diyah because the child is complete and has wounds.
B) They are not liable because the child was a fetus.
C) They are liable for diyah only.
D) They are not liable because there is no proof the child was born alive.

Key Takeaway
Qasamah and diyah on a found fetus require both complete creation and beating traces; an incomplete child is presumed stillborn and no liability attaches.

Diyah on the Aqilah: Body Found on a Riding Animal
Ruling with analogy to possession-based liability

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that liability for diyah falls on the aqilah of the person possessing the animal when a corpse is found on it, distinguishing this from locality liability.

Core Idea
Possession (yad) of the animal transfers diyah liability from the locality to the possessor's aqilah.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses a specific scenario in diyat: a dead body is found on a riding animal that someone is driving. The ruling establishes that the blood money falls on the aqilah (tribal responsibility group) of the person in control of the animal, not on the people of the locality where the body is found. The key legal principle is possession (yad) as a basis for liability, analogous to finding a body inside someone's house. This lesson unpacks the reasoning and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the finding of a dead body on a riding animal being driven. The ruling is that diyah is wajib on the aqilah of the driver.
Also consider the cases of leader (holding reins) and rider.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is a qiyas (analogy) to the case where a body is found in someone's house. Possession (yad) is the common cause (illa).
The text explicitly says 'because he is in his possession, so it becomes as if he was found in his house.'
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The analogy works because possession creates a presumption of control and responsibility. Just as the owner of a house is responsible for a body found inside, the possessor of the animal is responsible for a body found on it.
Possession here includes driving, leading, or riding.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some schools might assign liability to the locality if the body is found in a public space. The Hanafi position prioritizes possession over locality.
The hanafi_position_box indicates mukhtalaf_fih.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The Hanafi position is mufta bihi (relied upon) in the school, based on the principle that yad is a decisive factor for liability.
Authority weight is zahir_riwayah.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال وإذا وجد القتيل على دابة يسوقها رجل فالدية على عاقلته دون أهل المحلة؛ لأنه في يده فصار كما إذا كان في داره وكذا إذا كان قائدها أو راكبها فإن اجتمعوا فعليهم؛ لأن القتيل فى أيديهم فصار كما إذا وجد في دارهم
ترجمہ اور اگر مقتول اس چوپائے پر پایا جائے جس کو ایک شخص ہانک رہا ہو تو دیت اس کی عاقلہ پر ہوگی نہ کہ اہل محلہ پر اس لئے کہ وہ مقتول اس کے قبضہ میں ہے تو اس کا ایسا حکم ہے جیسے وہ اس کے گھر میں پایا گیا ہو اور اسی طرح اگر وہ چوپائے کی باگ پکڑے ہوئے ہے یا اس پر سوار ہے تو حکم یہی ہے اور اگر سب (مذکورہ افراد) اکٹھے ہوں تو ان سب پر دیت ہے کیونکہ مقتول ان سب کے قبضہ میں ہے تو اس کا حکم یہ ہے جیسے وہ ان کے گھر میں پایا گیا ہو۔
تشریح اور اگر مقتول کسی چوپائے پر مردہ پایا جاتا ہے اور اس چوپائے کو کوئی شخص ہانک رہا ہے تو دیت اس شخص کی عاقلہ پر ہوگی اہل محلہ پر نہیں اس لئے کہ مقتول اس شخص کے قبضہ میں سمجھا جائے گا اور یہی حکم اس شخص کا ہے جس نے جانور کی باگ پکڑی ہوئی ہے اور اس شخص کا بھی ہے جو جانور پر سوار ہے تو اگر یہ سب افراد موجود ہوں تو ان سب پر دیت ہے۔
He (the author) said: And if the killed person is found on an animal that a man is driving, then the diyah is upon his 'aqilah (assistant group) to the exclusion of the people of the locality; because he (the killed) is in his (the man's) possession, so it becomes as if he was found in his house. Likewise, if he is the leader (holding the reins) or the rider. And if they are all together, then upon all of them; because the killed is in their possession, so it becomes as if he was found in their house. Translation: And if the killed person is found on a riding animal that a person is driving, then the diyah will be on his 'aqilah, not on the people of the locality, because the killed is in his possession, so its ruling is like it was found in his house. Similarly, if he is holding the reins of the animal or riding it, the same ruling applies. And if all (the mentioned individuals) are together, then the diyah is upon all of them, because the killed is in their possession, so its ruling is like it was found in their house. Explanation: If the killed person is found dead on an animal, and someone is driving that animal, then the diyah is on the 'aqilah of that person, not on the people of the locality, because the killed is considered to be in that person's possession. The same ruling applies to the person holding the reins and the person riding the animal. If all these persons are present, then diyah is upon all of them.
Source pages p. 37

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from the matn (original text) regarding a dead body found on a riding animal (dābba). The key principle is that liability shifts from the locality to the individual who has physical control (yad) over the deceased at the time of discovery. The person driving the animal, leading it, or riding it are considered to have the body in their possession, analogous to finding the body inside their house. Therefore, the diyah (blood money) is on the 'āqilah (tribal or mutual responsibility group) of that person, not on the people of the locality. If multiple persons are involved (e.g., one driving and another riding), they share the liability. This is a rational extension (qiyas) of the rule for finding a body in a dwelling, because possession (yad) creates a presumption of responsibility. The Hanafi school uses this analogy to determine the appropriate party to bear the diyah.

Key Terms
عاقلة (ʿāqila): The group of relatives or tribe responsible for paying diyah on behalf of a member; here it refers to the assistant group of the person in possession.
دابة (dābba): A riding animal, such as a horse, camel, or donkey.
يد (yad): Possession or control; here extended to include driving, leading, or riding an animal that carries the corpse.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A dead body is found on a horse in a locality. Two men are present: one is leading the horse by the reins, and the other is riding it. According to the Hanafi school, who bears the diyah?
A) The people of the locality.
B) The 'āqilah of the man leading the horse only.
C) The 'āqilah of both men together.
D) The 'āqilah of the rider only.

Key Takeaway
Possession (yad) of the animal bearing the corpse transfers diyah liability from the locality to the possessor's aqilah, based on qiyas to finding a body in a house.

Diyat — Blood Money
intermediate
6 min
Diyah Liability When a Corpse Is Found on a Handled Animal
Ruling with qiyas proof on diyah for corpse on handled animal

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on diyah obligation when a corpse is found on an animal being driven, led, or ridden, and explain the qiyas to the case of a house.

Core Idea
Control (yad) over the corpse triggers diyah on the handler's aqilah, like a house owner.

This lesson presents a key ruling from the chapter of Qasamah: if a murdered person is found on an animal that someone is driving, leading, or riding, the blood money is wajib on the aqilah of that person, not on the locality. The reasoning is based on a qiyas jaliy (clear analogy) to the case where a corpse is found in someone's house, because in both situations the person has physical control (yad) over the victim. Understanding this analogy deepens your grasp of how Hanafi fiqh extends rulings through illah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Ruling
Read the ruling: when a corpse is found on an animal that a person is driving (sa'iq), leading (qa'id), or riding (rakib), the diyah is wajib on the aqilah of that person, not the locality.
This is a financial obligation, not a criminal penalty.
2
Locate the Dalil (Proof)
The proof is not a direct Quranic or hadith text but a qiyas jaliy (clear analogy). The author compares it to the case of a house: 'as if the murdered person is in his house.'
Qiyas jaliy is a strong form of analogy accepted by all schools.
3
Analyze the Illah (Effective Cause)
The illah is physical control (yad). Just as a house owner has exclusive control over his house, a person handling an animal has control over the animal and anything on it. This control creates responsibility for the safety of anyone on the animal.
The illah is extracted by tanqih al-manat: the key attribute is yad (hand/control).
4
Apply to Multiple Handlers
If multiple persons are involved (e.g., one drives, one leads, one rides), all share liability because the corpse is in the 'hand' of all of them, analogous to a jointly owned house.
The diyah is divided equally among their aqilas.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب القسامة
اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد - ۱۶
ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور جبکہ مقتول کسی چوپائے پر پایا جائے جس کو کوئی شخص ہانکتا ہو تو دیت اس کے عاقلہ پر ہوگی نہ کہ اہل محلہ پر اس لئے کہ مقتول اس کے ہاتھ میں ہے تو ایسا ہو گیا جیسے اس کے گھر میں ہو اور ایسے ہی حکم ہے جب کہ وہ چوپائے کا قائد یا اس کا را کب ہوئپس اگر یہ سب جمع ہو جائیں تو دیت ان سب پر ہوگی اس لئے کہ مقتول ان کے ہاتھ میں ہے تو ایسا ہو گیا جیسے جب کہ مقتول ان کے گھر میں پایا جائے۔
تشریح ایک چوپائے کو کوئی شخص لئے جاتا ہے اور اس پر کوئی مقتول ہے تو اس کی دیت اس پر واجب ہوگی جیسے اگر مقتول اس کے گھر میں ماتا تو یہی حکم ہوتا، پھر وہ شخص پیچھے سے ہانکے یا آگے سے کھینچے یا اس پر سوار ہو سب برابر ہے اور اگر تین شخص ہوں ایک سائق اور ایک قائد اور ایک راکب تو ان سب پر دیت واجب ہوگی ۔ جیسے اگر ان کے گھر میں مقتول ماتا تو ان سب پر دیت واجب ہوتی ایسے ہی یہاں بھی واجب ہوگی۔
Chapter of Qasamah. Ashraf al-Hidayah Urdu commentary of Hidayah volume 16. Al-Quduri said: And when a murdered person is found on an animal that someone is driving, then the blood money is upon his aqilah, not upon the people of the locality, because the murdered person is in his hand; so it becomes as if he is in his house. And the same ruling applies when he is the leader (qa'id) of the animal or its rider. So if all of these are present together, then the blood money is upon all of them, because the murdered person is in their hand, so it becomes as if the murdered person is found in their house. Commentary: A person is taking an animal and upon it is a murdered person, then his blood money is obligatory upon him, just as if the murdered person died in his house, this same ruling applies. Then whether that person drives from behind, pulls from the front, or rides upon it, all are equal. And if there are three persons: a driver (sa'iq), a leader (qa'id), and a rider (rakib), then the blood money is obligatory upon all of them, just as if the murdered person died in their house, the blood money would be obligatory upon all of them; similarly here it is obligatory.
Source pages p. 38

Commentary
This passage from the chapter of Qasamah (oaths related to homicide) presents a ruling from Al-Quduri's Mukhtasar. The ruling deals with the scenario where a corpse is found on an animal that is being led by a person. The blood money (diyah) is imposed on the aqilah (the support group, typically the male agnates) of that person, not on the entire locality, because the person has control over the animal — the corpse is metaphorically 'in his hand', analogous to being found in his house. The same applies if the person is a qa'id (leading the animal) or a raakib (riding it). If multiple persons are involved in handling the animal (e.g., one driving from behind, one leading from front, and one riding), then all their aqilas are collectively responsible for the diyah, analogized to the case where the corpse is found in a house owned jointly by them. The commentary clarifies that the actions of driving, leading, or riding are all equivalent in establishing liability. The reasoning is based on qiyas (analogy) to the house scenario, which is a clear analogy (qiyas jaliy). This is a ruling from the Zahir al-Riwayah, as it is from the matn of Quduri, which is relied upon in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
دیت (diyah): Blood money; financial compensation paid by the aqilah of the unintentional killer to the heirs of the victim.
عاقلہ (aqilah): The support group of the perpetrator; typically male agnates (asabah) who share the responsibility of paying diyah.
سائق (sa'iq): The person driving the animal from behind.
قائد (qa'id): The person leading the animal from the front.
راکب (rakib): The person riding the animal.
ید (yad): Physical control or possession; the effective cause (illah) in this ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The person driving the animal
B) The owner of the animal
C) The locality where the animal is found
D) No one, because the killer is unknown

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, physical control (yad) over a corpse establishes diyah liability on the controller's aqilah, analogized to a house owner's responsibility.

Diyat — Blood Money
intermediate
10 min
Blood money for corpse found in a house
Ruling on qasamah and diyah when corpse found in someone's house

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state who bears the qasamah and who pays the diyah when a corpse is found in a house, and explain the Hanafi reasoning based on possession and support.

Core Idea
Qasamah on owner, diyah on aqilah: possession triggers oath, support triggers payment.

This lesson examines a specific case from al-Quduri: a slain person is found in someone's house. The Hanafi school distinguishes between the obligation of qasamah (oath) and the payment of diyah (blood money). Understanding this distinction clarifies the roles of individual control and collective responsibility in Hanafi criminal law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what is being ruled upon: qasamah and diyah. The passage states that qasamah is upon the house owner and diyah is upon his aqilah.
Qasamah is an oath of innocence required from the person in control.
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
The text provides two reasons: 'because the house is in his hand' (possession/yad) and 'because his support is from them' (the aqilah provides backing).
The proof is not a direct text from Quran/Sunnah but a legal reasoning (qiyas).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Explain how possession implies qasamah: the owner has exclusive control, so he must swear innocence. How support implies diyah: the aqilah is the source of strength and assistance, so the financial liability falls on them.
This is analogous to earlier cases of found corpses in localities.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some schools may hold that if the owner is the sole occupant, he must pay diyah personally. The Hanafi view separates qasamah and diyah obligations.
The practical difference: who actually pays the blood money.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال وإن وجد القتيل فى دار إنسان فالقسامة عليه؛ لأن الدار في يده والدية على عاقلته لأن نصرته منهم وقوته بهم
ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور اگر مقتول کسی انسان کے گھر میں پایا جائے تو قیامت اس پر ہوگی اس لئے کہ گھر اس کے قبضہ میں ہے اور دیت اس کے عاقلہ پر ہوگی اس لئے کہ اس کے مددگار وہی ہیں اور انہیں کی وجہ سے اس کی قوت ہے۔ تشریح ایک مقتول کسی کے گھر میں پایا جائے تو قسم صرف گھر والے پر ہوگی کیونکہ گھر کا مالک وہ اکیلا ہے تو وہ اکیلا اہل محلہ کے درجہ میں ہوگا اور دیت اس کی مددگار برادری پر ہوگی۔ کیونکہ عاقلہ کا فریضہ ہے امداد و نصرت کرنا اور عاقلہ کے بل بوتے پر ہی انسان اپنے اندر قوت و طاقت محسوس کرتا ہے۔
Al-Quduri said: And if the slain person is found in someone's house, then the qasamah is upon him because the house is in his hand; and the blood money is upon his aqilah because his support is from them and his strength is through them. Translation: If a slain person is found in a person's house, then the oath is upon him, because the house is in his possession. And the blood money is upon his aqilah, because his helpers are they and through them is his strength. Commentary: If a slain person is found in someone's house, the oath is only on the house owner, because the owner is alone; so he is in the position of the people of the locality. And the blood money is upon his supporting fraternity, because it is the duty of the aqilah to provide aid and support, and it is through the strength of the aqilah that a person feels power.
Source pages p. 39

Commentary
This passage from Quduri addresses the case where a corpse is found in someone's house. The qasamah (oath) is required from the house owner himself, because the house is under his exclusive control. However, the blood money (diyah) is upon his aqilah (agnatic group), not on him personally, because the aqilah is responsible for providing support and assistance in such liabilities. The commentary explains that the owner is likened to a single inhabitant of a locality in terms of qasamah, but the financial burden falls on his clan. This ruling is based on the principle that the aqilah bears the diyah for unintentional homicide or found bodies, as they are the source of the person's strength. The reasoning is analogous to the earlier cases where the person in control is liable for qasamah but his aqilah pays.

Key Terms
دار (dar): A house or dwelling that is in someone's possession (yad).
القسامة (al-qasamah): An oath sworn by the person in control of the place where a corpse is found, to deny responsibility for the killing.
العاقلة (al-aqilah): The agnatic group (male relatives on the father's side) who are responsible for paying blood money (diyah) on behalf of their member.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The owner bears both
B) The owner bears qasamah; his aqilah pays diyah
C) The aqilah bears qasamah; the owner pays diyah
D) The locality bears both

Key Takeaway
When a corpse is found in a house, the owner must take an oath (qasamah), but the blood money (diyah) is paid by his aqilah, not by him personally.

Diyat — Blood Money

Ruling: Slain Found in House — Qasama on Owner, Diyah on Aqilah
States ruling for a slain person found in a house

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a slain person is found in a house and explain the reasoning based on possession (yad) and support (nusrah).

Core Idea
Qasama is on the house owner, diyah on his aqilah — possession and support determine liability.

This passage from Al-Quduri's matn presents a specific case in the chapter of qasama. It illustrates how Hanafi fiqh allocates responsibility between the individual and his clan. The ruling hinges on the concepts of possession (yad) and support (nusrah), which determine who bears the oath and who pays compensation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and ruling
Recognize that the passage addresses the case of a slain person found inside a house. Note the two-part ruling: qasama on the owner, diyah on the aqilah.
The owner is the sole possessor; the aqilah are his male agnate relatives.
2
Understand the proof for qasama on the owner
The proof is talil (reasoning): because the house is in his possession (yad). In Hanafi law, exclusive possession places the burden of oath on the possessor, as he is deemed to be in the position of the whole locality.
3
Understand the proof for diyah on the aqilah
The diyah is on the aqilah because the owner's strength and support come from them. The aqilah assist the owner in bearing financial liabilities that are beyond his immediate capacity.
This reflects the social solidarity principle in Islamic law.
4
Distinguish individual and group responsibility
Note that the owner alone performs qasama, but the diyah is collective on the aqilah. This separation ensures that the oath is precise while the financial burden is shared.
This avoids requiring the entire clan to swear.
5
Apply the principle to similar cases
Consider analogous situations, e.g., a body found in a shop or car. The person in possession (owner/lessee) bears the oath, and his aqilah pays diyah.
Possession is key: the one who has control is liable.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال وإن وجد القتيل فى دار إنسان فالقسامة عليه؛ لأن الدار في يده والدية على عاقلته لأن نصرته منهم وقوته بهم ترجمہ: قدوری نے فرمایا اور اگر مقتول کسی انسان کے گھر میں پایا جائے تو قسامت اس پر ہوگی اس لئے کہ گھر اس کے قبضہ میں ہے اور دیت اس کے عاقلہ پر ہوگی اس لئے کہ اس کے مددگار وہی ہیں اور انہیں کی وجہ سے اس کی قوت ہے۔ تشریح: ایک مقتول کسی کے گھر میں پایا جائے تو قسم صرف گھر والے پر ہوگی کیونکہ گھر کا مالک وہ اکیلا ہے تو وہ اکیلا اہل محلہ کے درجہ میں ہوگا اور دیت اس کی مددگار برادری پر ہوگی۔ کیونکہ عاقلہ کا فریضہ ہے امداد و نصرت کرنا اور عاقلہ کے بل بوتے پر ہی انسان اپنے اندر قوت و طاقت محسوس کرتا ہے۔
He said: If the slain person is found in a person's house, then the qasama is upon him because the house is in his possession, and the diyah is upon his aqilah because his help is from them and his strength is through them. Translation: Al-Quduri said: And if a slain person is found in someone's house, then the qasama will be upon him because the house is in his possession, and the diyah will be upon his aqilah because his helpers are they and through them is his strength. Elaboration: If a slain person is found in someone's house, the oath will be only on the house owner because he is the sole owner of the house, so he alone will be in the position of the people of the locality, and the diyah will be on his helping brotherhood because the duty of the aqilah is to provide aid and support, and it is through the strength of the aqilah that a person feels power and strength within himself.
Source pages p. 39

Commentary
This is a ruling statement from the matn of Al-Quduri, followed by its Urdu translation and elaboration. The passage presents the ruling that when a dead body is found inside someone's house, the qasama (the solemn oath of fifty witnesses) is required from the owner of the house alone. The reason given is that the house is under his exclusive possession and control. As for the diyah (blood money), it is to be paid by his aqilah (the clan or male agnate relatives) because the owner's strength and support derive from them. The commentary clarifies that the owner stands in the place of the entire locality for the purpose of qasama, and the aqilah is responsible for the diyah because their role is to provide assistance and protection.

Key Terms
القسامة (al-qasāmah): A solemn oath sworn fifty times by the defendant (in Hanafi) to deny responsibility for a slain person found in his custody or property.
الدية (al-diyah): Blood money paid as compensation to the heirs of the victim in cases of unlawful killing where qasama is applied.
العاقلة (al-ʿāqilah): The male agnate relatives (clan) who are responsible for paying diyah on behalf of a person if he is liable for a killing.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Upon all residents of the house
C) Upon the aqilah of the owner
D) Upon the people of the locality

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, the discovery of a slain body in one's home triggers personal qasama and clan diyah based on possession and support.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute: Qasamah on Ahl al-Khattah vs Purchasers
Intra-Hanafi dispute: original vs. subsidiary residents in qasamah liability

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why Abu Hanifah and Muhammad restrict qasamah to ahl al-khattah and evaluate Abu Yusuf's opposing argument.

Core Idea
Qasamah liability follows the original custodians of a locality, not later buyers.

This passage from Ashraf al-Hidaya examines an intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifah/Muhammad and Abu Yusuf over who must perform qasamah when a corpse is found in a mixed locality. The ruling has practical implications for blood-money liability. By analyzing the proofs, you will understand how custom and the principle of original vs. subsidiary shape Hanafi rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
Abu Hanifah and Muhammad (the two) hold qasamah is only on ahl al-khattah (original inhabitants). Abu Yusuf holds it is on all owners including purchasers (mushtarin).
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf between the three leading imams.
2
Examine Abu Yusuf's dalil
Abu Yusuf cites the Khaybar incident where the Prophet imposed qasamah on Jews who were not owners but residents. He argues ownership alone creates authority of protection, so all owners are equal.
The dalil is a fi'li sunnah (the Prophet's action).
3
Analyze the Hanafi response
The two respond that the Jews of Khaybar were actual owners because the Prophet confirmed them on their lands (iqrar) and took kharaj, not jizyah. Thus they were ahl al-khattah in that context. Also, custom shows original residents are primary custodians.
The Hanafi rebuttal distinguishes the Khaybar precedent.
4
Understand the thamarah al-khilaf
In practice, if a corpse is found in a locality with both groups, under Abu Yusuf all owners must swear and share blood-money; under the majority, only original inhabitants are liable.
This difference affects who bears the burden of oaths and payment.
5
Note the tarjih
Al-Marghinani in Al-Hidayah prefers the view of Abu Hanifah and Muhammad, and it is the mufta bihi position.
The reliance on custom and the principle of asil vs. dakheel gives this view precedence.

اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد - ۱۶
که قسامت حفظ اہل خطہ پر واجب ہوگی مشتر بین پر نہ ہوگی کیونکہ متعارف یہی ہے کہ اہل خطہ ہی اس علاقہ اور بقعہ کی حفاظت کے ذمہ دار ہوتے ہیں اور یہ بھی وجہ ہے کہ اہل خطہ اصیل میں اور مشتر میں دخیل ہیں اور تدبیر کی ولایت اصیل کو ہوتی ہے دخیل کو نہیں ہوتی ، بعض حضرات نے کہا ہے کہ امام ابوحنیفہ نے اہل کوفہ کا یہ عمل درآمد دیکھا کہ اہل خطہ تدبیر کے متولی ہوتے ہیں مشترین نہیں ہ ہوتے تو یہ حکم ارشاد فرمایا۔
Chapter of Qasamah. Explanation: Some residents of a locality are original inhabitants who own lands, and some live there without ownership (rent etc.). On whom is qasamah? The view of the two (Abu Hanifah and Muhammad) is that qasamah is only on owners, not on residents. Abu Yusuf says qasamah is on both, because qasamah and blood-money relate to administration (tadbir) and all are equal in that. The proof of Imam Abu Yusuf: The Prophet صلى الله عليه وسلم made qasamah and blood-money obligatory on the Jews of Khaybar even though they were not owners but only residents. This shows non-owners also have qasamah. The proof of the two: aid (nusrah) of the place is specific to owners, not residents, because the resident's dwelling is not permanent unlike the owner. Thus authority of administration is on owners, and protection is their duty; negligence is by them, so they are held liable. As for the Jews of Khaybar, they were owners — the Prophet left them on their properties and took kharaj from them. Those people of the locality on whom qasamah is obligatory. He said: It is upon the people of the plan (ahl al-khattah) and not upon the purchasers (mushtarin); this is the saying of Abu Hanifah and Muhammad. Abu Yusuf said: All are partners, because liability is due to leaving protection by one who has authority of protection, and authority is based on ownership, and they are equal in that. For them (the two): The owner of the plan is specifically for aiding the place, customarily, and because he is original, the purchaser is subsidiary, and authority of administration goes to the original. It is said that Abu Hanifah built this on what he witnessed in Kufa. Translation of Quduri: He said: And it (obligation of qasamah) is on ahl al-khattah, not on purchasers; this is the saying of the two. Abu Yusuf said: All are partners, because liability is due to abandoning protection by one who has authority of protection, and in this way he is considered a negligent criminal; authority is based on ownership, and they are equal in that. For them (the two) the proof is that the owner of the plan is specifically for aiding the place, customarily, and because he is original, the purchaser is subsidiary, and authority of administration goes to the original. It is said that Abu Hanifah based this on what he witnessed in Kufa. Explanation: Among the people of the locality on whom qasamah is obligatory, some are those to whom the Imam gave land at the time of conquest — they are ahl al-khattah or their descendants; the other group are those who bought and settled. Both are equal owners. Which group is liable? Imam Abu Yusuf said: Both groups, because both own and have authority of protection; negligence is by both, so both are liable. The school of the two (Abu Hanifah and Muhammad) is that qasamah is upon ahl al-khattah only, not on purchasers, because customarily ahl al-khattah are responsible for protection, and also because they are original and purchasers are subsidiary; authority of administration goes to the original, not the subsidiary. Some said that Imam Abu Hanifah saw the practice of the people of Kufa that ahl al-khattah take charge of administration, not purchasers, so he gave this ruling.
Source pages p. 40

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidaya presents an intra-Hanafi dispute on the liability for qasamah (compurgation/oaths) when a person is found killed in a locality. The chapter begins by distinguishing two types of residents: the original inhabitants (ahl al-khattah) who were granted land by the Imam, and later purchasers (mushtarin) who bought property. The question is: on whom does the obligation of qasamah (and consequential blood-money) fall? The position of Abu Hanifah and Muhammad al-Shaybani is that qasamah is only on the original inhabitants (ahl al-khattah). Their reasoning is that the duty of protection and administration of the locality is customarily entrusted to the original settlers; they are the 'asil (original) while newcomers are dakheel (subsidiary). Authority of administration belongs to the original. Furthermore, the permanence of ownership gives them a stronger connection to the place. They rebut Abu Yusuf's proof from the Khaybar incident by noting that the Jews of Khaybar were actual owners of the land (the Prophet allowed them to remain on their property under kharaj), not mere renters. Abu Yusuf argues that qasamah is on all residents because liability arises from abandoning the duty of protection, and all owners share the authority of protection equally. The text notes that Abu Hanifah's ruling was influenced by his observation of the practice in Kufa, where ahl al-khattah indeed handled administration. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is that of Abu Hanifah and Muhammad, as it is considered the stronger view.

Key Terms
القسامة (al-qasāmah): A procedure where the claimant swears fifty oaths to establish right to blood-money, or the accused swears to deny liability; in this context, it refers to the obligation to swear oaths to defend against accusation when a corpse is found.
أهل الخطة (ahl al-khattah): The original inhabitants of a locality who were granted land by the Imam at the time of conquest; they are considered the primary residents with authority over administration and protection.
مشترين (mushtarīn): Those who purchased property in the locality later and settled; they are considered subsidiary (dakheel) to the original inhabitants.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifah and Muhammad, on whom does the obligation of qasamah fall when a corpse is found in a locality?
A) On all residents equally
B) On the original inhabitants (ahl al-khattah) only
C) On the purchasers (mushtarin) only
D) On the 'aqilah of the deceased

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, qasamah liability is on the original inhabitants (ahl al-khattah) due to their role as primary custodians, not on later purchasers.

Qasamah When Only One or None of Ahl al-Khattah Remain
Ruling on qasamah when ahl al-khattah are reduced to one or completely absent

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on qasamah liability when ahl al-khattah are reduced to one or completely absent, and apply it to determine who bears the obligation.

Core Idea
Qasamah stays with the original residents even if one remains; only when all are gone does it shift to purchasers.

In this lesson, we examine a specific ruling from al-Quduri regarding qasamah liability when the original inhabitants of a locality decrease or leave entirely. The ruling clarifies that the obligation does not become shared equally — it remains with the original residents as long as at least one remains, and only when none remain do the new owners assume responsibility. Understanding this prioritization is crucial for correctly assigning blood-money and oath obligations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The passage treats two distinct cases: (1) only one person from ahl al-khattah remains; (2) none remain because all have sold their properties.
Ahl al-khattah are the original settlers granted land by the state.
2
State the ruling for each scenario
For scenario 1: the single remaining person bears full qasamah and diyah obligation. For scenario 2: all purchasers collectively bear the obligation.
The ruling is the same as when all ahl al-khattah were present — obligation is not divided.
3
Understand the legal reasoning (ta'lil)
The authority (wilayah) over the locality originally belongs to ahl al-khattah. If they all leave, it transfers to the purchasers exclusively, as there is no one to precede or compete.
This is based on ownership and residence-based responsibility, not tribal affiliation.
4
Compare with other schools
Other madhahib (e.g., Shafi'i) may place liability on the 'aqilah (agnatic helpers) universally, without the ahl al-khattah/mushtarin distinction.
The Hanafi position is unique in prioritizing original residents.

Source Text

اہل خطہ پر قسامت و دیت کا حکم
قال وإن بقى واحد منهم فكذلك يعنى من أهل الخطة لما بينا وإن لم يبق واحد منهم بأن يدعوا كلهم فهو على المشترين؛ لأن الولاية انتقلت إليهم أو خلصت لهم لزوال من يتقدمهم أو يزاحمهم
ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور اگر ان میں ایک باقی رہ گیا ہو تو ایسے ہی یعنی اہل خطہ میں سے اس دلیل کی وجہ سے جو کہ ہم بیان کر چکے ہیں اور اگر ان میں سے کوئی باقی نہ رہا ہو اس طریقہ پر کہ ان سب نے بیچ دی ہو تو قسامت مشتر بین پر ہوگی اس لئے کہ ولایت ان کی جانب منتقل ہو گئی یا فقط انہیں کے لئے رہ گئی ہے ان لوگوں کے نہ رہنے کی وجہ سے جو ان سے مقدم ہیں یا ان سے مزاحم ہیں ۔
تشریح اور اگر وہاں محلہ کے اندر اہل خطہ میں سے صرف ایک آدمی رہ گیا ہے تو بھی یہی حکم ہے یعنی وہی تد بیر کا ولی ہے اور اسی پر قسامت ودیت ہے البتہ اگر اہل خطہ میں سے کوئی بھی وہاں پر نہ رہا ہو بلکہ سب مشتر ین ہو تو اب مشترین ذمہ دار ہوں گے اور اب ان پر قسامت اور دیت واجب ہوگی کیونکہ جو ان کے مرہم تھے اور جو ان سے مقدم تھے اب وہ نہیں رہے تو اب ولایت خالص انہی کے لئے رہ گئی ہے۔
Ruling of qasamah and blood-money on ahl al-khattah. He said: And if one of them remains, it is the same — meaning from ahl al-khattah — for the reason we have explained. And if none of them remain, such that they all sell, then qasamah is on the purchasers, because the authority transfers to them or becomes exclusively for them due to the removal of those who preceded them or competed with them. Translation of Quduri: He said: And if one of them remains, it is the same, i.e., from ahl al-khattah, due to the proof we have stated. And if none of them remain, such that they all sell, then qasamah is on the purchasers, because authority has transferred to them or become exclusively theirs due to the absence of those who were before them or competed with them. Explanation: And if within the locality only one person from ahl al-khattah remains, the same ruling applies: he is the caretaker of administration and upon him is qasamah and blood-money. However, if none of ahl al-khattah remain there, and all are purchasers, then the purchasers become responsible and qasamah and blood-money are obligatory on them, because those who were their superiors and predecessors are gone, so authority remains purely for them.
Source pages p. 41

Commentary
This passage provides the ruling on qasamah liability when the ahl al-khattah population changes. The rule is: If at least one original inhabitant (ahl al-khattah) remains in the locality, the entire obligation of qasamah and the consequent blood-money (diyah) falls on that one person alone. He alone must swear the oaths or be liable. However, if absolutely none of the ahl al-khattah remain — meaning they have all sold their properties and left — then the authority of administration transfers fully to the purchasers (mushtarin). In that case, the purchasers collectively bear the responsibility of qasamah and blood-money. The reasoning is that the authority of protection and administration (wilayat al-tadbir) originally vested in the ahl al-khattah; when they are completely absent, the purchasers become the sole residents with the duty of protection. This ruling is consistent with the earlier principle that the original inhabitants are the primary duty-bearers, but if they are entirely gone, the subsidiary residents step into that role.

Key Terms
ولایت (wilāyah): Authority or guardianship over the administration and protection of a locality, which determines liability for qasamah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If all original inhabitants (ahl al-khattah) sell their properties and leave, on whom does the obligation of qasamah fall?
A) No one is liable
B) The purchasers (mushtarin)
C) The government
D) The nearest relative of the deceased

Key Takeaway
The obligation of qasamah remains with the original inhabitants (ahl al-khattah) as long as at least one remains; only when all are gone does it transfer exclusively to the purchasers.

Diyat — Blood Money

Qasamah and Diyah When Corpse Found in a House
Intra-Hanafi dispute on qasamah responsibility for a dead body found in a private home.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi internal dispute on qasamah liability when a corpse is found in a private house and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Qasamah is jointly on the owner and his present 'āqilah; if absent, the owner swears alone.

When a dead body is discovered inside someone's home, the law of qasamah applies to determine responsibility for swearing oaths. The Hanafi school has an internal disagreement: Abu Hanifah and Muhammad hold that both the house owner and his supporting tribe ('āqilah) must swear if present, while Abu Yusuf places the entire burden on the 'āqilah. This lesson dissects the reasoning and the practical consequence of this difference.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
State the view of Abu Hanifah and Muhammad (owner + present 'āqilah) and the view of Abu Yusuf (only 'āqilah).
2
Analyze the reasoning for each
For the majority: duty to aid the place (nusrat al-buq'ah) binds all present. For Abu Yusuf: owner is more specific, so no sharing; analogy to locality.
The majority's argument is based on general obligation, Abu Yusuf's on exclusivity.
3
Critique the opposing argument
The majority responds that the analogy to a locality is flawed because the 'āqilah are present and bound to aid, unlike a whole locality where they may be absent.
4
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
Under majority: owner swears with present 'āqilah; under Abu Yusuf: 'āqilah swear alone and owner is exempt.
The difference affects who must appear in court to swear.
5
Identify the mufta bihi position
The view of Abu Hanifah and Muhammad (owner + present 'āqilah) is the relied-upon position for fatwa.
This is the Zahir al-Riwayah position.

Source Text

مقتول کسی مکان سے ملا تو قسامت مالک پر اور دیت عاقلہ پر ہے
وإذا وجد قتيل فى دار فالقسامة على رب الدار وعلى قومه وتدخل العاملة فى القسامة إن كانوا حضورا وإن كانوا غيبا فالقسامة على رب الدار يكرر عليه الأيمان وهذا عند أبي حنيفة ومحمد وقال أبويوسف الاقسامة على العاقلة؛ لأن رب الدار أخص به من غیره فلایشار كه غيره فيها كأهل المحلة لا يشاركهم فيها عواقلهم ولهما أن الحضور لزمتهم نصرة البقعة كما تلزم صاحب الدار فيشاركونه في القسامة
ترجمہ اور جب مقتول کسی گھر میں پایا جائے تو قسامت گھر والے پر اور اس کی قوم پر ہوگی اور مددگار برادری قسامت میں داخل ہوگی اگر وہ لوگ حاضر ہوں اور اگر غائب ہوں تو قسامت گھر والے پر ہوگی اس پر ایمان کو ( قسموں کو ) مکرر کیا جائے گا اور یہ طرفین کے نزدیک ہے اور ابو یوسف نے فرمایا کہ عاقلہ پر قسامت نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ مالک دار اس مکان کیساتھ زیادہ مخصوص ہے اپنے غیر کے مقابلہ میں ان پس اسکے اس کا غیر شریک نہ ہو گا قسامت کے اندر جیسے اہل محلہ کہ قسامت میں اُن کے ساتھ ان کے عواقل شریک نہ ہونگے اور طرفین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ حاضرین پر بقعہ کی نصرت لازم ہے جیسا کہ نصرت صاحب دار پر لازم ہے پس ما لک دار کے قیامت کے اندر حاضرین عواقل شریک ہوں گے۔ تشریح معقول کسی مکان میں ملا تو قسامت مالک مکان پر ہوگی اور دیت اس کے عاقلہ پر ہوگی ۔ اب اس پر سوال یہ ہے کہ قیامت
When a slain person is found in a house, qasamah is on the owner of the house and on his people (qawm), and the helping tribesmen (al-'āmilah) enter into the qasamah if they are present. If they are absent, then qasamah is on the owner of the house and oaths are repeated on him. This is according to Abu Hanifah and Muhammad. Abu Yusuf said: Qasamah is on the 'āqilah (the tribe/clan), because the owner of the house is more specific to it than others, so no one else shares with him in it, just as the people of a locality are not shared by their 'āqilah. For them (the two): The present ones are bound to aid the place as the owner is bound, so they share with him in qasamah. Explanation: [If] a slain person is found in a house, qasamah is on the owner of the house and blood-money is on his 'āqilah. Now there is a question about qasamah...
Source pages p. 41

Commentary
This passage discusses the liability for qasamah and blood-money when a dead body is discovered inside a private house. According to Abu Hanifah and Muhammad al-Shaybani, the owner of the house (rabb al-dār) is primarily responsible for qasamah (swearing oaths), and his 'āqilah (supportive clan or tribe) also participate in the qasamah if they are present in the locality. If the 'āqilah are absent (ghuyyab), then the owner alone must swear oaths repeatedly (each oath is taken multiple times, up to fifty). However, according to Abu Yusuf, the qasamah liability falls entirely on the 'āqilah (the clan), not on the owner, because the owner is too exclusively connected to the house for others to share the liability—similar to how the people of a locality alone bear qasamah without their 'āqilah. Abu Yusuf's view is that the 'āqilah are the ones who provide aid (nusrah) in general, so they should bear the oath-taking. The majority (Abu Hanifah and Muhammad) respond that the duty to aid the place (nusrat al-buq'ah) is incumbent on all present residents, just as it is on the owner; thus the 'āqilah share in qasamah. The practical difference: under the majority view, if 'āqilah are present, they swear alongside the owner; if absent, the owner swears fifty oaths alone. Under Abu Yusuf, the 'āqilah always swear, and the owner does not. The relied-upon position is that of Abu Hanifah and Muhammad.

Key Terms
عاقلة (al-ʿāqilah): The supporting clan or group of a person who are collectively responsible for paying blood-money (diyah); in this context, they also participate in qasamah oaths if present.
رب الدار (rabb al-dār): The owner of the house where the corpse is found; he is primarily responsible for qasamah according to Abu Hanifah and Muhammad.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifah and Muhammad, what happens to qasamah if the 'āqilah of the house owner are absent?
A) Qasamah is dropped
B) The house owner swears oaths alone, which are repeated
C) The 'āqilah swear remotely
D) The nearest relative swears

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, qasamah for a corpse found in a house is primarily on the owner, but his 'āqilah share the oaths if present; if absent, the owner swears repeatedly.

Qasamah: Ahl al-Khittah vs. Mushtereen
States where qasamah falls based on custodianship

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to determine on whom qasamah falls based on custodianship and apply the transfer of wilayah from ahl al-khittah to mushtereen.

Core Idea
Qasamah falls on custodians of the land; when custodians vanish, liability transfers.

This lesson clarifies the Hanafi ruling on collective responsibility (qasamah) for an unsolved murder in a district. It distinguishes between original settlers (ahl al-khittah) and newcomers (mushtereen) and explains how custodianship (wilayah) determines liability. By the end, you will be able to assign liability correctly in various scenarios.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that the act is qasamah (collective oath/diyah liability) and the ruling is that it is wajib on the guardians of the locality.
The ruling is based on the principle of wilayah (authority/custodianship).
2
Distinguish between ahl al-khittah and mushtereen
Ahl al-khittah are the original settlers with customary management authority; mushtereen are later buyers without such authority.
The distinction is unique to Hanafi fiqh, derived from the planning of Kufa.
3
Trace the proof (dalil)
Imam Abu Hanifa relied on the practice (urf) of the people of Kufa, where ahl al-khittah managed the district.
The dalil is customary practice (urf), which has zanni thubut and dalalah.
4
Apply the transfer rule
If all ahl al-khittah leave or sell, wilayah transfers to the mushtereen, making them liable for qasamah. If only one remains, he bears sole responsibility.
This is based on the principle that wilayah goes to those who succeed in custodianship.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب القسامة
اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد - ۱۶
که قسامت حفظ اہل خطہ پر واجب ہوگی مشتر بین پر نہ ہوگی کیونکہ متعارف یہی ہے کہ اہل خطہ ہی اس علاقہ اور بقعہ کی حفاظت کے ذمہ دار ہوتے ہیں اور یہ بھی وجہ ہے کہ اہل خطہ اصیل میں اور مشتر میں دخیل ہیں اور تدبیر کی ولایت اصیل کو ہوتی ہے دخیل کو نہیں ہوتی ، بعض حضرات نے کہا ہے کہ امام ابوحنیفہ نے اہل کوفہ کا یہ عمل درآمد دیکھا کہ اہل خطہ تدبیر کے متولی ہوتے ہیں مشترین نہیں ہ ہوتے تو یہ حکم ارشاد فرمایا۔
اہل خطہ پر قسامت و دیت کا حکم
قال وإن بقى واحد منهم فكذلك يعنى من أهل الخطة لما بينا وإن لم يبق واحد منهم بأن يدعوا كلهم فهو على المشترين؛ لأن الولاية انتقلت إليهم أو خلصت لهم لزوال من يتقدمهم أو يزاحمهم ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور اگر ان میں ایک باقی رہ گیا ہو تو ایسے ہی یعنی اہل خطہ میں سے اس دلیل کی وجہ سے جو کہ ہم بیان کر چکے ہیں اور اگر ان میں سے کوئی باقی نہ رہا ہو اس طریقہ پر کہ ان سب نے بیچ دی ہو تو قسامت مشتر بین پر ہوگی اس لئے کہ ولایت ان کی جانب منتقل ہو گئی یا فقط انہیں کے لئے رہ گئی ہے ان لوگوں کے نہ رہنے کی وجہ سے جو ان سے مقدم ہیں یا ان سے مزاحم ہیں ۔ تشریح اور اگر وہاں محلہ کے اندر اہل خطہ میں سے صرف ایک آدمی رہ گیا ہے تو بھی یہی حکم ہے یعنی وہی تد بیر کا ولی ہے اور اسی پر قسامت ودیت ہے البتہ اگر اہل خطہ میں سے کوئی بھی وہاں پر نہ رہا ہو بلکہ سب مشتر ین ہو تو اب مشترین ذمہ دار ہوں گے اور اب ان پر قسامت اور دیت واجب ہوگی کیونکہ جو ان کے مرہم تھے اور جو ان سے مقدم تھے اب وہ نہیں رہے تو اب ولایت خالص انہی کے لئے
رہ گئی ہے۔
Chapter of Qasamah. Ashraf al-Bidayah Urdu commentary of Hidayah Volume 16. That qasamah is obligatory on the people of the khittah, not on the mushtereen, because the custom is that the people of the khittah are responsible for guarding that area and locality. And this is also the reason that the people of the khittah are original and the mushter are newcomers, and the authority of management is for the original, not for the newcomer. Some scholars said that Imam Abu Hanifa saw the practice of the people of Kufa that the people of the khittah undertake management, not the mushtereen, so he issued this ruling. Ruling on qasamah and diyah on ahl al-khittah. He said: And if one of them remains, then it is the same, meaning from the people of the khittah, due to what we have explained. And if none of them remain, such that they all sold, then it is upon the mushtereen, because the wilayah has transferred to them or become exclusive to them due to the removal of those who precede them or compete with them. Translation: Al-Quduri said: And if one of them remains, then it is the same, i.e., from the people of the khittah, due to the reason we have stated. And if none of them remain, in the manner that they all sold, then qasamah is upon the mushtereen, because wilayah has transferred to them or become exclusively for them due to the absence of those who are before them or compete with them. Explanation: And if only one person from the people of the khittah remains in the neighbourhood, then the same ruling applies, i.e., he is the guardian of management and upon him is qasamah and diyah. But if none of the people of the khittah remain, rather all are mushtereen, then the mushtereen are responsible, and upon them qasamah and diyah become obligatory, because those who were before them and preceded them are no longer there, so wilayah remains exclusively for them.
Source pages p. 41

Commentary
This passage states the ruling on who bears the collective responsibility (qasamah) for a murder found in a district. The original settlers (ahl al-khittah) are liable because they have the customary authority (wilayah) to guard the area. Newcomers (mushtereen) are not liable as long as any original settler remains. The reasoning is that wilayah belongs to the original settlers. However, if all original settlers leave or sell their properties, wilayah transfers to the newcomers, making them liable. The text also addresses the case when only one original settler remains – he alone bears the full responsibility. This is based on the practice of Kufa observed by Imam Abu Hanifa.

Key Terms
قسامت (qasamah): Collective oaths taken by the locality to deny responsibility for a murder, or the liability for blood money when the oath is taken.
اہل خطہ (ahl al-khittah): The original settlers of a district who were granted land and are responsible for its management.
مشتر (mushter): Newcomers who buy property in the district but are not original settlers; they lack custodianship.
ولایت (wilayah): Authority or guardianship over a locality that entails responsibility for its protection.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If all original settlers (ahl al-khittah) sell their properties and leave, upon whom does qasamah fall?
A) No one
B) The successors (mushtereen)
C) The state
D) The victim's family

Key Takeaway
Qasamah liability is tied to custodianship (wilayah), which rests with original settlers and transfers only when they all depart.

Qasamah When Murder in a House: Owner vs. Aqilah Dispute
Explains intra-Hanafi dispute on qasamah liability

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on qasamah liability when a murdered person is found in a house, distinguish the views of Abu Hanifa/Muhammad and Abu Yusuf, and apply the reconciled ruling based on the presence or absence of the 'aqilah.

Core Idea
Qasamah liability for house murder: owner always liable, 'aqilah share only if present.

This passage addresses an important intra-Hanafi dispute: when a murdered body is found in a house, who bears the qasamah (sworn oaths) – only the house owner, or also his 'aqilah (supporting clan)? Understanding this dispute clarifies how early Hanafi jurists balanced individual connection to a property with communal responsibility for protection. The resolution, attributed to Imam al-Karkhi, provides a practical rule based on the presence of the 'aqilah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the common scenario
Start with the basic ruling: if a murdered person is found in a house, qasamah is upon the house owner and his people. Note that the 'aqilah enters if present; otherwise only the owner.
This is the starting point before the dispute.
2
Contrast Abu Yusuf's view
Abu Yusuf argues that qasamah is only on the owner because of his special connection to the house; no one else shares, just as in a neighbourhood where 'awaqil do not share with residents.
His analogy is key to understanding his reasoning.
3
Analyze the majority view's proof
Abu Hanifa and Muhammad argue that present 'aqilah are obligated to defend the locality just as the owner is, so they share the qasamah liability.
The concept of nusrah (obligation to protect) is central.
4
Reconcile the two narrations
Note that two conflicting rulings appear in the Hanafi corpus. Follow Imam al-Karkhi's reconciliation: the first narration (owner alone) applies when 'aqilah are absent; the second (owner + 'aqilah) applies when they are present.
This is the mufta bihi position.
5
Determine the practical consequence
The thamarah al-khilaf: Under Abu Yusuf, only the owner takes all oaths. Under the majority, if 'aqilah are present, they share the oaths; if absent, only the owner.
This affects the number of oaths each party must swear.

تو پہلا مسئلہ پہلی روایت کے مطابق ہے اور دوسرا دوسری روایت کے مطابق ہے اور امام کرفی سے یہ تطبیق منقول ہے کہ پہلی روایت عاقلہ کے غائب ہونے کی حالت پر محمول ہے اور دوسری روایت عاقلہ کے حاضر ہونے کی حالت پر محمول ہے۔ تنبه ۲ گھر والے پر قیامت تب واجب ہے جب کہ ولی مقتول اس پر قتل کا دعوی کرے اور اگر ولی اس کے علاوہ کسی اور پر دعوی کرے تو اس پر نہ قسامت ہے اور نہ دیت ہے۔
And when a murdered person is found in a house, then qasamah is upon the owner of the house and upon his people (qawm), and the supporting clan (al-'amilah) enters into qasamah if they are present. If they are absent, then qasamah is upon the owner of the house; the oaths are repeated upon him. This is according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. Abu Yusuf said: Qasamah is upon the 'aqilah (supporting clan) because the owner of the house is more specific to it than others, so others do not share with him in it, just as the people of the neighbourhood: their 'awaqil do not share with them in qasamah. And their (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad's) proof is that the presence [of the 'aqilah] makes them obligated to defend the locality, just as the owner of the house is obligated, so they share with him in qasamah. Translation: And when a murdered person is found in a house, qasamah is upon the owner of the house and upon his people, and the supporting clan enters into qasamah if they are present. If they are absent, qasamah is upon the owner of the house; the oaths are repeated upon him. And this is according to the two sides (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad). Abu Yusuf said that qasamah is upon the 'aqilah because the owner of the house is more specific to it than others, so others do not share with him in qasamah, just as the people of the neighbourhood: their 'awaqil do not share with them in qasamah. And the proof of the two sides is that the present ones are obligated to defend the locality, just as the owner of the house is obligated, so the present 'awaqil share with him in qasamah. Explanation: If a murdered person is found in a house, qasamah is upon the owner of the house, and diyah is upon his 'aqilah. Now the question is whether qasamah is only on the house owner or also on the 'aqilah of the owner. There is difference. Imam Abu Yusuf said that qasamah is only on the owner, not on the 'aqilah. The two sides (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) said that there is detail: if the 'aqilah are present in the city, they also have qasamah; if they are absent, there is no qasamah on them, rather only on the owner; repeated oaths will be taken from him. Imam Abu Yusuf's proof is that the owner of the house has special connection to this house and place, so why would another share qasamah with him? Just as when qasamah is upon the people of the neighbourhood, their supporting clan does not enter into qasamah, similarly here. The proof of the two sides is that protection of this locality is obligatory upon the owner of the house, and similarly upon those present among the 'awaqil, so the present 'awaqil will be included in qasamah. Note 1: Earlier in the page this ruling was stated: qasamah is only on the owner, and here it is said that it is also obligatory on the 'aqilah if present. The resolution is that diyah is always on the 'aqilah, and regarding qasamah, there are two narrations: 1) qasamah is only on the house owner; 2) qasamah is on both the owner and the 'aqilah. The first ruling is according to the first narration, and the second according to the second narration. And from Imam Karkhi it is reported that the reconciliation is that the first narration is concerning the case when the 'aqilah are absent, and the second narration is concerning the case when the 'aqilah are present. Note 2: Qasamah is obligatory upon the house owner only when the guardian of the murdered person claims murder against him; if the guardian claims against someone else, then there is no qasamah or diyah upon him.
Source pages p. 41

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding qasamah when a murdered body is found in a house. According to Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad, the house owner is liable for qasamah, and if the 'aqilah (supporting clan) are present in the city, they also share the liability. If they are absent, only the owner takes the oaths. Imam Abu Yusuf holds that only the owner is liable, analogizing to the case of a neighbourhood where only the residents (not their 'awaqil) bear qasamah. The text then reconciles two conflicting narrations: one stating qasamah is only on the owner, another that it includes the 'aqilah. Imam al-Karkhi explains that the first applies when the 'aqilah are absent, the second when they are present. A second note clarifies that the owner is only liable if the victim's guardian specifically accuses him of murder.

Key Terms
عاقلہ ('aqilah): The supporting clan (male agnates) who are responsible for paying diyah and also share qasamah if present according to one view.
عاملة (al-'amilah): The supporting clan (equivalent to 'aqilah) mentioned in the text.
نصرة (nusrah): Obligation to defend and protect the area.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon position in the Hanafi school, when does the house owner bear qasamah alone?
A) Always
B) When the 'aqilah are absent
C) When the 'aqilah are present
D) Never

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi mufta bihi position: qasamah for a murder in a house is wajib on the owner and also on the 'aqilah if they are present; if absent, only on the owner.
