Effect of Accusing a Specific Person on Qasamah Liability
Ruling that accusing an insider does not remove qasamah from the locality, while accusing an outsider does.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on qasamah when the wali accuses an insider versus an outsider, and explain the legal reasoning (talil) behind the distinction.

Core Idea
Accusing an insider does not remove qasamah from the locality; accusing an outsider does, because the obligation itself proves the killer is from among them.

In the chapter on qasamah, a key question arises: if the wali (heir) identifies a specific suspect from the locality, does the rest of the locality still bear the qasamah? Al-Quduri and Al-Hidayah present a clear ruling with a nuanced distinction. This lesson unpacks the reasoning that determines when the locality remains liable and when it does not.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
Recognize that the ruling distinguishes between the wali accusing a specific person from the locality (insider) versus accusing someone from outside the locality (outsider).
The term 'locality' refers to the group of people among whom the slain body is found.
2
State the ruling for each scenario
If the wali accuses an insider, qasamah (and diyah) remains wajib on the locality. If he accuses an outsider, qasamah falls from the locality.
This is the clear ruling from the text.
3
Extract the legal reasoning (talil)
The obligation of qasamah on the locality is itself evidence (dilalah) that the killer is from among them. Accusing an insider does not contradict this presumption; accusing an outsider does.
The reasoning is based on the condition that the locality's liability is constructive: they are deemed killers for not preventing the crime.
4
Apply the condition to the outsider scenario
When the wali claims an outsider, it indicates the killer is not from the locality, so the condition for their liability is missing, and the claim against them ceases.
The locality is not liable merely by the appearance of the body; it requires the wali's claim.
5
Recognize the underlying principle
The principle is that the locality's liability is constructive, based on their failure to prevent the crime. This justifies the difference in rulings.
This principle is unique to Hanafi fiqh in qasamah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال وإن ادعى الولى على واحد من أهل المحلة بعينه لم تسقط القسامة عنهم وقد ذكرناه وذكرنا فيه القياس والاستحسان.
ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور اگر ولی نے محلہ والوں میں سے معین کسی ایک شخص پر قتل کا دعوی کیا تو اہل محلہ سے قیامت ساقط نہ ہو گی اور ہم اس کو بیان کر چکے ہیں اور ہم اس میں قیاس اور استحسان کو بیان کر چکے ہیں۔ تشریح اس کی تفصیلی وضاحت پر تو سبق میں تفصیل سے گذر چکی ہے۔
قال وإن ادعى على واحد من غيرهم سقطت عنهم ووجه الفرق قد بيناه من قبل وهو أن وجوب القسامة عليهم دليل على أن القاتل منهم فتعيينه واحدا منهم لا ينافي ابتداء الأمر لأنه منهم بخلاف ما إذا عين من غيرهم لأن ذلك بيان أن القاتل ليس منهم وهم إنما يغرمون إذا كان القاتل منهم لكونهم قتلة تقديرا حيث لم يأخذوا على يد الظالم ولأن أهل المحلة لا يغرمون بمجرد ظهور القتيل بين أظهرهم إلا بدعوى الولى فإذا ادعى القتل على غيرهم امتنع دعواه عليهم وسقط لفقد شرطه
ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اوراگران کے غیر میں سے کسی ایک پر ولی نے قتل کا دعوی کیا تو اہل محلہ سے قسامت ساقط ہو جائے گی اور وجہ فرق کو ہم پہلے بیان کر چکے ہیں اور وہ وجہ یہ ہے کہ اہل محلہ پر قسامت کا وجوب اس بات کی دلیل ہے کہ قاتل انہی میں سے ہے تو ان میں سے ایک کو متعین کر دینا پہلی بات کے منافی نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ وہ ایک انہی میں سے ہے بخلاف اس صورت کے جبکہ ولی ان کے کسی غیر کو معین کرے اس لئے کہ یہ ( غیر کی تعیین ) اس بات کا بیان ہے کہ قاتل ان میں سے نہیں ہے اور اہل محلہ اسی وقت ضامن ہوتے ہیں جبکہ قاتل ان میں سے ہو ان کے تقدیرا قاتل ہونے کی وجہ سے اس حیثیت سے کہ انہوں نے ظالم کا ہاتھ نہیں پکڑا اور اس لئے کہ اہل محلہ محض ان کے درمیان مقتول کے ظہور سے ضامن نہیں ہوتے مگر ولی کے دعوئی کے ساتھ پس جب ولی نے ان کے غیر پر قتل کا دعوی کر دیا تو مدگی کا اہل محلہ پر دعوئی منتفع ہو گیا اور تاوان ساقط ہو گیا اس کی شرط کے مفقود ہونے کی وجہ ہے۔ تشریح اگر ولی مقتول نے اہل محلہ کے علاوہ کسی اور شخص پر قتل کا دعوی کیا ہو تو اب اہل محلہ پر نہ قسامت ہے اور نہ دیت ہے اس کی وجہ فرق ماقبل میں مذکور ہو چکی نیز یہ بھی وجہ ہے کہ جب اہل محلہ پر قسامت واجب ہوتی ہے تو یہ اس بات کی دلیل ہوتی ہے کہ قاتل انہی میں سے کوئی ایک ہے۔ تو جب ولی نے اہل محلہ میں سے کسی ایک کو متعین کر دیا تو بات اب بھی جوں کی توں رہی کیونکہ پہلے بھی اہل محلہ قاتل شمار کئے گے تھے اور جب اُن میں سے ایک کو متعین کر دیا تو نقد میر اور اب بھی بدستور قاتل ہیں کیونکہ ان پر ضروری تھا کہ وہ قاتل کا ہاتھ پکڑیں اور اس کو ظلم نہ کریں۔
He said: If the wali (heir) accuses a specific person from the people of the locality, qasamah does not fall from them. And we have mentioned it, and we have mentioned therein the analogy and istihsan. Translation: Al-Quduri said: And if the wali accuses a specific one of the people of the locality, qasamah does not fall from them, and we have already stated it, and we have stated the qiyas and istihsan in it. Explanation: The detailed clarification has already passed in the lesson. He said: And if he accuses one from other than them, it (qasamah) falls from them. And the reason for the difference we have already explained: and that is that the obligation of qasamah upon them is proof that the killer is among them, so specifying one of them does not contradict the initial premise because he is from them. Unlike if he specifies one from outside them, because that clarifies that the killer is not from them. And they are only liable if the killer is from among them, because they are constructively killers since they did not seize the hand of the oppressor. And because the people of the locality are not liable merely by the appearance of the slain among them except with the claim of the wali. So if he claims murder upon other than them, his claim against them ceases and the penalty falls due to the missing condition. Translation: Al-Quduri said: And if he accuses one from outside them, qasamah falls from them, and we have already explained the reason for the difference: the obligation of qasamah upon them indicates that the killer is from among them. So specifying one of them does not contradict initial premise because he is from them. Unlike when he specifies an outsider, because that clarifies the killer is not from them. And they only guarantee if the killer is from among them because they are constructively killers for not preventing the oppressor. And they are not liable merely by the appearance of the slain among them except with the claim of the wali. So when he claims murder upon other than them, his claim against them is negated and the penalty drops due to loss of condition. Explanation: If the wali of the slain accuses a specific person other than the inhabitants of the locality, then neither qasamah nor diyah is upon the inhabitants. The reason for difference has been mentioned, also that when qasamah is wajib on them, it indicates the killer is among them. So when the wali specifies one of them, the matter remains the same because before also they were considered killers, and when he specifies one, it remains as before because it was their duty to seize the oppressor and not let him commit oppression.
Source pages p. 50

Commentary
This passage from the chapter on qasamah comprises two related rulings. First, if the wali (legal heir of the slain) accuses a specific person from the locality, the qasamah (and diyah) does not fall from the locality as a whole. The reason is that the obligation of qasamah on the locality itself is evidence that the killer is deemed to be among them. Accusing one specific individual from the locality does not contradict that, because that individual is part of the group. The original presumption (an-nafs al-amr) remains: the killer is from among them. Therefore, the locality remains liable for the constructive killing. Second, if the wali accuses someone from outside the locality, the qasamah falls from the locality. The reasoning (talil) is that such an accusation indicates that the killer is not from that locality. The locality's liability is conditioned on the killer being from them (constructively, as they failed to prevent the crime). If the killer is allegedly an outsider, the condition is missing, so the liability drops. The text also mentions the principle that the locality is not liable solely because a dead body appears among them; they only become liable when the wali makes a claim. If the wali claims against an outsider, his claim against the locality is effectively withdrawn. This distinguishes the two cases.

Key Terms
الولي (al-walī): The legal heir of the slain person, who has the right to demand qasas or diyah.
القسامة (al-qasāmah): Oath compurgation: fifty oaths by men of the locality, or if they refuse, they pay diyah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If the wali accuses an outsider (not from the locality) of the murder, what happens to the qasamah obligation on the locality?
A) It remains wajib on the locality.
B) It falls from the locality.
C) It becomes mustahab.
D) It is transferred to the accused's tribe.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi ruling distinguishes between accusing an insider (qasamah remains) and an outsider (qasamah falls) based on the presumption that the killer is from the locality, which is proven by the very obligation of qasamah.

Effect of Accusation on Qasamah: Insider vs. Outsider
Ruling statement with talil on qasamah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on qasamah when the wali accuses a specific person from the mahalla versus an outsider, and explain the legal reasoning (talil) based on the condition of the killer's origin.

Core Idea
Accusing a neighbor does not remove qasamah; accusing an outsider does — the condition is the killer being from among them.

This passage from Al-Hidayah presents two scenarios regarding the obligation of qasamah on a neighborhood when a murdered person is found. The key is the wali's accusation: if he accuses a resident, the collective liability remains; if he accuses an outsider, it falls. Understanding this distinction requires tracking the condition that triggers liability: that the killer be from among the neighbors.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
Read the passage and note the two cases: (1) wali accuses a specific person from the mahalla, (2) wali accuses someone from outside the mahalla.
2
State the ruling for each
For case 1: qasamah does NOT fall from the neighborhood. For case 2: qasamah FALLS from the neighborhood.
3
Trace the reasoning (farq)
The passage explains that the obligation of qasamah on them is evidence that the killer is from among them. Accusing one of them is consistent with that; accusing an outsider contradicts it, because it shows the killer is not from them.
4
Identify the condition
The passage states that the neighborhood is only liable if the killer is from among them. The wali's claim against an outsider removes that condition.
Note: This is a condition (shart) for qasamah liability.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال وإن ادعى الولى على واحد من أهل المحلة بعينه لم تسقط القسامة عنهم وقد ذكرناه وذكرنا فيه القياس والاستحسان. قال وإن ادعى على واحد من غيرهم سقطت عنهم ووجه الفرق قد بيناه من قبل وهو أن وجوب القسامة عليهم دليل على أن القاتل منهم فتعيينه واحدا منهم لا ينافي ابتداء الأمر لأنه منهم بخلاف ما إذا عين من غيرهم لأن ذلك بيان أن القاتل ليس منهم وهم إنما يغرمون إذا كان القاتل منهم لكونهم قتلة تقديرا حيث لم يأخذوا على يد الظالم ولأن أهل المحلة لا يغرمون بمجرد ظهور القتيل بين أظهرهم إلا بدعوى الولى فإذا ادعى القتل على غيرهم امتنع دعواه عليهم وسقط لفقد شرطه
He said: If the wali accuses a specific person from among the people of the neighborhood, the qasamah does not fall from them, and we have mentioned it and we have mentioned therein qiyas and istihsan. He said: And if he accuses a person from other than them, it (the qasamah) falls from them, and the explanation of the difference we have already stated: it is that the obligation of qasamah upon them is evidence that the killer is from among them. So designating one of them does not contradict the initial situation, because that one is from them. Contrary to when he designates someone from outside them, because that indicates that the killer is not from among them. And they only become liable if the killer is from among them, because they are considered killers by legal presumption (taqdeeran), since they did not restrain the oppressor. And the people of the neighborhood are not liable merely due to the appearance of the slain person among them, except with the claim of the wali. So when he claims murder against someone else, his claim against them is prevented and it falls due to the absence of its condition.
Source pages p. 50

Commentary
This passage presents two contrasting rulings from the Hidayah regarding the obligation of qasamah (oath-taking) and diyat (blood-money) on the people of a neighborhood (ahl al-mahalla) when a murdered person is found among them. The first scenario: The legal guardian (wali) of the victim accuses a specific individual who is a resident of that neighborhood. In this case, the qasamah does not fall from the entire neighborhood because they remain under suspicion as a collective. The reasoning is that the initial obligation of qasamah on them was based on the presumption that the killer is among them. Specifying one of them does not change this presumption, as that person is indeed from among them. The second scenario: The wali accuses someone from outside the neighborhood. Here, the qasamah falls from the neighborhood. The reason is that this accusation reveals that the killer is not from among them, so the basis for their liability (that the killer is from among them) is removed. The passage further explains that the liability of the neighborhood is not automatic upon finding a corpse; it requires the wali's claim against them. If the wali claims against an outsider, he cannot simultaneously claim against the neighborhood, as that would be contradictory. The condition for the neighborhood's liability is that the killer be from among them, and that condition is now absent. The author mentions that the ruling is based on a distinction (farq) between the two cases, which has been explained previously, and that the opposite ruling (qiyas) and the preferred ruling (istihsan) have also been discussed.

Key Terms
القسامة (al-qasamah): An oath-taking procedure in homicide cases where the blood-money is claimed from the inhabitants of a locality when the killer is unknown.
المحلة (al-mahalla): The neighborhood or locality where the corpse is found; its inhabitants are collectively responsible for qasamah.
الولي (al-wali): The legal guardian of the deceased who has the right to claim qasamah and diyat.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It falls entirely.
B) It remains.
C) It is transferred to the accused.
D) It requires bayyinah.

Key Takeaway
The wali's accusation only removes qasamah from the neighborhood if the accused is an outsider; otherwise, the collective liability remains because the condition (killer from among them) is still met.

Diyat — Blood Money

Liability in Sword Fights: Neighborhood and the Accused
Explaining the ruling on liability of the neighborhood and the fighting group when a corpse is found after a sword fight.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on liability for diyat when a corpse is found after a sword fight and explain how the burden of proof shifts between the neighborhood and the accused fighters.

Core Idea
Neighborhood liable unless guardians accuse fighters; fighters liable only upon evidence.

When a group fights with swords and a corpse is left, who is responsible for the blood-money? The Hanafi school applies the principles of qasamah and the burden of proof. This passage from Al-Hidayah clarifies the default liability of the neighborhood and the effect of an accusation against the fighters, balancing compensation for the victim with protection against false claims.

Guided Path
1
Identify the default ruling
The passage begins by stating that if a group fights and a corpse is left, the blood-money is upon the people of the neighborhood (ahl al-mahalla).
This is the default position based on the concept of qasamah: the locality is responsible for the safety of those within.
2
Understand the reasoning
The reason given is that the slain is among them and they were obligated to protect him.
The neighborhood is held responsible because the death occurred in their area and they had a duty of protection.
3
Note the exception
If the guardians (awliya') specifically accuse the fighters or a specific man, the neighborhood is absolved.
The accusation implies that the killer is not from the neighborhood, so the locality is exonerated.
4
Analyze the effect on the accused
The accused fighters are not automatically liable; they are not liable until the guardians produce evidence (bayyinah).
This is based on the hadith: 'al-bayyinah 'ala al-mudda'i' (the burden of proof is on the claimant).
5
Evaluate the overall ruling
The ruling balances ensuring compensation for the victim (via neighborhood liability) and protecting the accused from false claims (via requiring evidence).
This is a distinctive Hanafi approach to unresolved homicides.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال وإذا التقى قوم بالسيوف فأجلوا عن قتيل فهو على أهل المحلة؛ لأن القتيل بين أظهرهم والحفظ عليهم إلا أن يدعى الأولياء على أولئك أو على رجل منهم بعينه فلم يكن على أهل المحلة شيء لأن هذه الدعوى تضمنت براءة أهل المحلة عن القمامة. قال ولا على أولئك حتى يقيموا البيئة؛ لأن بمجرد الدعوى لا يثبت الحق للحديث الذي رويناه أما يسقط به الحق عن أهل المحلة لأن قوله حجة على نفسه
He said: When a group of people clash with swords and then leave a slain person, it (the blood-money) is upon the people of the neighborhood, because the slain is among them and they were obligated to protect him. Unless the guardians (awliya') claim against those (fighters) or against a specific man among them; then there is nothing upon the people of the neighborhood, because this claim implies the innocence of the people of the neighborhood from the qasamah. He said: And there is nothing upon those (fighters) until they produce evidence (bayyinah), because the right is not established by mere claim, according to the hadith we narrated. However, the right falls from the people of the neighborhood, because his statement is a proof against himself.
Source pages p. 51

Commentary
This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses a scenario where a group of people engage in a sword fight, and after they disperse, a dead body is found among them. The ruling is that the people of the neighborhood (ahl al-mahalla) are liable for the blood-money (diyat) of the victim. The reasoning is that the corpse was found in their area, and they had the duty to protect (hifz) the victim. This is similar to the general principle of qasamah: when a corpse is found in a locality and the killer is unknown, the locality bears the diyat, and they take oaths (qasamah) to establish their lack of involvement. However, an exception is when the guardians (awliya' al-dam) specifically accuse the fighting group as a whole or a particular individual from them. In that case, the locality is absolved, because the accusation shifts the liability to the accused party. The passage then addresses the liability of the accused fighters: they are not automatically liable simply because they are accused. The guardians must produce evidence (bayyinah) to prove their claim. This is based on the prophetic hadith that 'the burden of proof is on the claimant' (al-bayyinah 'ala al-mudda'i). Mere accusation does not establish liability. However, the mere accusation does have an effect: it absolves the people of the neighborhood from liability, because the guardian's statement is considered a proof against himself (i.e., he has admitted that the killer is not from the neighborhood by accusing outsiders). So the neighborhood is released, but the accused fighters are not liable until proven.

Key Terms
البيئة (al-bayyinah): Evidence or proof required to establish a claim in court.
القمامة (al-qasamah): The oath-taking procedure for homicide when the killer is unknown. (OCR corruption; correct term is القسامة.)
أولياء (awliya'): Plural of wali, the legal guardians of the victim who have the right to claim qasamah and diyat.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is required for the fighters who were accused of murder to be liable for diyat?
A) Mere accusation by the wali.
B) The corpse being found among the fighters.
C) The wali producing evidence (bayyinah).
D) The fighters refusing to take an oath.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, the neighborhood bears liability for an unidentified slain found after a fight, but a specific accusation shifts the burden to the accused, who must be proven guilty by evidence.

Dispute on Qasamah for Wounded Person Transferred Home
Presents Abu Hanifa's and Abu Yusuf's rulings on qasamah after transfer of wounded person

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on qasamah when a wounded person is transferred home and dies, and distinguish Abu Hanifa's view from Abu Yusuf's based on the condition of being bedridden.

Core Idea
A wound that leads to death only imposes qasamah if the victim was bedridden, ensuring death is attributable to the wound.

Qasamah is a device for imposing liability when homicide is suspected but no direct proof. This passage presents a dispute between the founder and his leading student: if a person is wounded in a tribe, taken home, and later dies from that wound, when does the tribe become liable? The answer hinges on a single condition: was the victim bedridden? Understanding this clarifies how the Hanafi school attributes causation in criminal liability.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
The scenario: a person is wounded in a tribe, then transferred home and dies from that wound. The question is whether the tribe must perform qasamah and pay diyah.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position
Abu Hanifa rules that if the victim was bedridden (sahib firaash) from the time of injury until death, then qasamah and diyah are on the tribe.
3
State Abu Yusuf's opposing view
Abu Yusuf says no qasamah and no diyah because only a wound less than death (ma dun al-nafs) occurred in the tribe, and qasamah is only for homicide.
Abu Yusuf further argues that if the victim was not bedridden, death may have been from another cause.
4
Understand Abu Hanifa's proof
Abu Hanifa argues that the wound, when death ensues, becomes a killing (qatl), thus qisas is obligatory. The condition of bedriddenness removes doubt about causation.
5
Note the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: if a judge follows Abu Hanifa, the tribe must pay diyah and perform qasamah; if Abu Yusuf, no liability.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
کسی محلہ میں کوئی زخمی ہو گیا اور کوئی اٹھا کر اسے گھر رکھ آیا پھر زخمی اسی زخم کی تکلیف سے مر گیا تو قسامت اور دیت کس پر ہے؟ اقوال فقہاء اور ہر ایک کی دلیل قال ومن جرح في قبيلة فنقل إلى أهله فمات من تلك الجراحة فإن كان صاحب فراش حتى مات فالقسامة والدية على القبيلة وهذا قول أبي حنيفة وقال أبويوسف لا قسامة ولا دية لأن الذى حصل في القبيلة أو المحلة ما دون النفس ولا قسامة فيه فصار كما إذا لم يكن صاحب فراش وله أن الجرح إذا اتصل به الموت صار قتلا ولهذا وجب القصاص فإن كان صاحب فراش أضيف إليه وإن لم يكن احتمل أن يكون الموت من غير الجرح فلا یلزم بالشک
And whoever is wounded in a tribe and then transferred to his family and dies from that wound, then if he was bedridden (sahib firaash) until death, the qasamah and diyah are on the tribe. This is the statement of Abu Hanifa. And Abu Yusuf said: no qasamah and no diyah, because what occurred in the tribe or locality is less than death (ma dun al-nafs) and there is no qasamah for that, so it becomes as if he was not bedridden. And his (Abu Hanifa's) proof: the wound, when death is connected to it, becomes murder, and therefore qisas is obligatory. If he was bedridden, it is attributed to him (the wounder); if he was not, it is possible that death was from something other than the wound, so it is not imposed due to doubt.
Source pages p. 55

Commentary
This passage addresses a specific scenario in qasamah: a person is wounded in a tribe or locality, then taken to his home, and later dies from that wound. The ruling depends on whether he was 'sahib al-firaash' (bedridden) from the time of injury until death. Imam Abu Hanifa rules that if he was bedridden, the qasamah (collective oath) and diyah (blood money) are imposed on the tribe because the continuity of bed-rest indicates the wound was the cause of death. Abu Yusuf disagrees: since the wound itself did not immediately cause death in the tribe, only an injury less than death (madun nafs) occurred in the tribe, and qasamah is only for homicide (nafs), not for wounds. Moreover, if he was not bedridden, there is doubt about the cause of death. Abu Hanifa's proof is based on the connection between the wound and death: if death follows, the wound becomes a killing act (qatl), thus qisas is due. The condition of bedriddenness ensures attribution. The passage illustrates the Hanafi principle of taking precaution (ihtiyat) in criminal liability. The authority weight is from Zahir al-Riwayah.

Key Terms
صَاحِب فِرَاش (sahib firaash): A person who is bedridden due to his wound, indicating continuous injury and inability to move
مَا دُونَ النَّفْس (ma dun al-nafs): An injury less than death, i.e., a wound that does not lead to immediate death

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Under which condition does Imam Abu Hanifa impose qasamah and diyah on the tribe for a wounded person transferred home?
A) If the person dies immediately in the locality
B) If the person was bedridden from injury until death
C) If the person names his attacker before death
D) If the tribe admits the wound

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, the tribe's liability for a transferred wounded person depends on whether the victim was bedridden—this condition removes doubt about causation.

Woman's Qasamah and Diyah in a Village She Owns
Intra-Hanafi dispute on qasamah for a woman owning a village

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Yusuf and the tarfayn (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) on qasamah and diyah for a woman who owns a village, and explain the supporting proof for each.

Core Idea
When a woman owns a village, qasamah may fall on her despite her lack of nusrah.

This lesson examines a specific intra-Hanafi dispute: a woman owns an entire village, and a dead body is found there. Normally, women are not from ahl al-qasamah because they lack nusrah. However, her ownership raises the question of qasamah. Imam Abu Yusuf maintains the general rule, while the two parties (tarfayn) make an exception, and later scholars add that she shares in diyah payment.

Guided Path
1
Recall the general rule on ahl al-qasamah
Understand that women, children, the insane, and slaves are not from ahl al-qasamah because they lack nusrah (ability to provide military assistance). This is the baseline.
2
Identify the exceptional scenario
A woman owns an entire village and all inhabitants are her subjects. A dead body is found there. Ownership creates suspicion of murder (tuhma), potentially triggering qasamah.
The suspicion is key for the tarfayn's view.
3
Outline Abu Yusuf's position
Abu Yusuf adheres to the general rule: women are not ahl al-nusrah, so they are not ahl al-qasamah. Therefore, both qasamah and diyah fall on the woman's aqila (paternal relatives).
His dalil: lack of nusrah.
4
Outline the tarfayn's position
Abu Hanifa and Muhammad depart from their usual stance. They rule: qasamah is wajib on the woman herself because qasamah is for negating suspicion, and the woman's ownership realizes that suspicion. Diyah, however, remains on her aqila.
Their dalil: qasamah is based on tuhma, not nusrah.
5
Explain the later scholars' addition
Later scholars (muta'akhkhirin) address whether the woman contributes to diyah payments. They say she does share with the aqila because she is treated as a murderer (qatila), and a murderer shares in the diyah burden.
This resolves the practical consequence of the tarfayn's view.

But if a woman owns an entire village and all the people there are her subjects, and a [dead body] is found in that village, what is the ruling? So Imam Abu Yusuf is on his principle which has been mentioned before, that a woman is not from the people of qasamah because she is not from the people of nusrah (assistance). Therefore, qasamah is not wajib on the woman, but rather qasamah and diyah are wajib on her aqila. And the two parties (tarfayn) here departed from their previous principle; they said that qasamah is only wajib on the woman, but diyah is wajib on her aqila. The proof of the two parties: Indeed, qasamah is for negating suspicion, and the suspicion of murder from the woman is realized. Translation: And the proof of the two parties is that qasamah occurs due to negation of suspicion, and the suspicion of murder from the woman is realized. Explanation: This is the proof of the two parties: qasamah is based not on nusrah but on removing the suspicion of murder, and since here this woman is the owner of the village, the suspicion of murder exists, therefore qasamah also becomes wajib. Statement of the later scholars: The later scholars said that the woman enters with the aqila in bearing [the diyah] in this issue because we have placed her in the position of a murderer, and the murderer shares with the aqila. Translation: The later scholars said that in bearing the diyah, the woman will enter with the aqila in this issue because we have placed her in the position of a murderess, and the murderer (in diyah) shares with the aqila. Yes, this was the question: When the aqila pays the diyah, will the woman also share with them in paying the diyah? So the later scholars said that the woman will also enter among them because the woman is in the position of a murderess, and the murderer shares with the aqila, therefore she will also [share].
Source pages p. 59

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding qasamah (oaths) and diyah (blood money) when a woman is the sole owner of a village and a dead body is found there. First, the text recalls the established principle that women, children, the insane, and slaves are not among ahl al-qasamah (those who swear oaths) because they are not ahl al-nusrah (capable of providing military assistance). However, the specific scenario of a woman owning an entire village creates an exception due to her ownership. Imam Abu Yusuf adheres to his original principle: since the woman is not from ahl al-nusrah, she is not liable for qasamah; instead, her aqila (male paternal relatives) bear both the qasamah and diyah. The 'tarfayn' (likely Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani) depart from their usual stance, ruling that qasamah is specifically on the woman because it serves to negate suspicion, and the woman's ownership generates suspicion of murder, but diyah remains on her aqila. Their proof is that qasamah's purpose is to clear suspicion, not tied to nusrah. Later scholars (muta'akhkhirin) add that when the aqila pays diyah, the woman also contributes because she is treated as a murderer (qatila), and a murderer shares the burden with the aqila. This resolves whether she merely bears the oath or also the financial responsibility: she shares in the diyah payment as well.

Key Terms
قسامت (qasamah): Oaths taken by the people of a locality or the aqila to deny responsibility for a found dead body, or to claim blood money.
عاقلہ (aqila): The male paternal relatives (asabah) who bear the diyah on behalf of a killer or for a found dead body.
دیت (diyah): Blood money paid as compensation for homicide or injury; in this context, for a found dead body where the killer is unknown.
نصرت (nusrah): Ability to provide military or defensive assistance; a criterion for being from ahl al-qasamah.
تہمت (tuhma): Suspicion of murder; qasamah is prescribed to remove this suspicion.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the tarfayn (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), on whom is qasamah wajib in the case of a woman owning a village?
A) On the woman's aqila
B) On the woman herself
C) On the villagers
D) On no one

Key Takeaway
In exceptional cases where a woman's sole ownership creates strong suspicion of murder, qasamah may be wajib on her despite her general exclusion from ahl al-qasamah.

Diyah for Dead Body on Land of a Non-Resident Owner
Ruling on whose liability when dead body found on land of non-resident owner

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that the landowner bears diyah for a dead body found on his land when he is not a resident of the adjacent village, and explain the reasoning based on nusrah.

Core Idea
The landowner is more entitled to defend his land than the villagers, so he bears diyah.

In this passage, al-Marghinani addresses a specific scenario: a murdered person is found on private land adjacent to a village, but the landowner does not reside there. The question is who must pay the diyah (blood money). The author rules decisively that the liability falls on the landowner, using the principle of nusrah (defense and protection). This lesson unpacks the legal reasoning and shows how ownership creates a stronger duty of care than mere proximity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scenario
The case involves a dead body on private land near a village. The key detail is that the landowner is not a resident of that village.
The villagers are not automatically liable just because the land is near them.
2
State the Ruling
The diyah is wajib on the landowner, not on the villagers. This is the clear ruling from the matn of al-Hidayah.
This ruling is mufta bihi in the Hanafi school.
3
Identify the Proof
The proof is rational: the landowner is ahaqq (more entitled) to the nusrah (defense/protection) of his land than the villagers are.
Nusrah here means the duty to guard and secure the land.
4
Understand the Legal Reasoning
Because ownership gives a stronger right and duty to protect, the landowner bears the consequence (daman) when a homicide occurs on his property. This is a principle of priority based on connection to the land.
This is not a textual proof but a legal maxim derived from customary and rational considerations.
5
Note the Textual Caution (Tanbih)
The commentary notes a manuscript discrepancy: the word 'qala' (he said) before 'huwa' may be spurious. The correct text likely omits it.
This caution shows the importance of textual criticism in fiqh.

If a murdered person is found outside the village on a particular person's private land, but the landowner is not among the residents of that village, then on whom is the diyah? And if a man is found murdered on a man's land adjacent to a village, and the owner of the land is not from its people, he (the author) said: it is on the owner of the land because he is more entitled to the defense (nusrah) of his land than the people of the village. Translation: And if a murdered man is found on a person's land, such land that is on the edge of a village, and the landowner is not a resident of that village, then the diyah is on the landowner because the landowner is more entitled to the defense of his land compared to the villagers. Source pages p. 59

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling on diyah when a dead body is found on private land belonging to a person who is not a resident of the adjacent village. The author (al-Marghinani) states clearly that the diyah is on the landowner, not on the villagers. The proof is that the landowner is more entitled (ahaqq) to defend (nusrah) his own land than the villagers are. The commentary elaborates that the landowner has a stronger interest in protecting his property, so he bears the liability (daman) for any homicide that occurs there. This applies even if the land is near a village; the villagers are not liable because the landowner's connection to the land is closer. The passage ends with a textual caution (tanbih) noting a discrepancy in the manuscript: the word 'qala' (he said) appears before 'huwa' in some versions, but other books omit it, and the commentator suggests the text would be more appropriate without it.

Key Terms
نصرت (nusrah): Defense, protection, or ability to provide military assistance; here specifically the duty to defend one's land.
ضمان (daman): Liability; the obligation to pay diyah.
احق (ahaqq): More entitled or more deserving; the comparative form of haqq (right).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The landowner bears diyah for a homicide on his land because his right and duty to defend it (nusrah) are stronger than those of the villagers.

Blood Money Liability on Landowner
Ruling on diyah liability of landowner when corpse found on his land

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on diyah liability when a corpse is found on land and identify the condition that determines liability.

Core Idea
The landowner bears blood money for a corpse found on his land, even if he does not reside there.

In this passage from the commentary on al-Hidayah, we examine a specific ruling within the chapter on qasamah: who is liable for blood money when a dead body is discovered on a privately owned plot? The answer hinges on the landowner's primary responsibility for protecting his property, overriding any collective village liability. This ruling clarifies an important principle in Hanafi criminal law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
State clearly who is liable for the blood money according to the passage.
The passage explicitly says 'the blood money is upon the landowner.'
2
Identify the condition
Note the specific scenario: the land is at the edge of a village, but the landowner is not a resident of that village.
This condition proves that residence does not affect liability.
3
Understand the rationale
Explain why the landowner bears liability: he is more entitled to protect his land than the villagers.
The rationale is based on the landowner's inherent right and duty (nasr wa hifazah) over his property.
4
Note the textual note
Observe the tanbih regarding the word 'huwa' and the omission of 'qala' in some manuscripts.
This shows the commentator's attention to textual accuracy.
5
Compare with potential alternative views
Consider that other schools might hold the village collectively liable, but Hanafi position is clear.
The passage does not elaborate on other views, but the ruling is decisive in Hanafi fiqh.

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on al-Hidayah presents a specific ruling regarding blood money (diyah) liability when a corpse is found on privately owned land. The author states that the blood money is incumbent upon the landowner (malik al-zamin), not upon the villagers (ahl al-basati). The reasoning is that the landowner has a greater right and responsibility to protect his own land. The commentator provides a clarifying example: even if the landowner does not reside in the village where his land is located, he still bears the liability because his connection to the land is stronger than that of the villagers. The passage also includes a textual note (tanbih) pointing out a discrepancy in the manuscript: the word 'huwa' here conflicts with the phrase 'qala al-musannif' typically found in the original text, and thus other books omit 'qala' to avoid inconsistency. This ruling is part of the broader chapter on qasamah, which deals with oaths and compensation in homicide cases where the killer is unknown.

Key Terms
دیت (diyah): Blood money; compensation paid for unintentional killing or injury, here specifically for the death of a person found on land.
مالک زمین (malik al-zamin): The owner of the land on which the corpse is found; the person responsible for protecting that land.
قسامة (qasamah): A procedure of fifty oaths taken by the plaintiff or defendant in homicide cases where the killer is unknown; the chapter heading here.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the landowner is solely liable for blood money when a corpse is found on his land, because his right and duty to protect his land supersedes collective village responsibility.

Kitab al-Ma'aqil: Defining Ma'aqil and the 'Aqila's Liability for Diyah
Defines Ma'aqil and explains 'Aqila's liability with proof from hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definition of Ma'aqil and 'Aqila, explain the linguistic reason for calling diyah 'aql, and identify the ruling that diyah for shibh 'amd and khata' is wajib upon the 'Aqila, citing the hadith proof.

Core Idea
Diyah restrains bloodshed; in shibh 'amd and khata', it is wajib upon the 'Aqila, not the killer.

In this passage from Ashraf al-Hidaya, the commentator introduces Kitab al-Ma'aqil, explaining the terminology: Ma'aqil (plural of ma'qila) means diyah, so-called because it holds back bloodshed. The chapter then presents a key ruling: the diyah due for quasi-intentional (shibh 'amd) and accidental (khata') killings is obligatory upon the 'Aqila—the killer's paternal relatives—not upon the killer himself. The ruling is supported by a hadith in which the Prophet ﷺ commands the guardians to pay the diyah, establishing the basis for collective responsibility.

Guided Path
1
Identify the terminology: Ma'aqil, 'Aqila, and 'aql
Read the initial definitions: Ma'aqil is the plural of ma'qila, meaning diyah. 'Aqila are those who pay the diyah (the supporting tribe). 'Aql literally means 'to restrain,' and diyah is called 'aql because it prevents bloodshed.
Notice the linguistic connection: 'aql → restrains → diyah restrains retaliation.
2
Recognize the ruling: diyah in shibh 'amd and khata' is wajib upon the 'Aqila
The text explicitly states that every diyah that becomes wajib by reason of the killing itself (not through reconciliation or other cause) in cases of shibh 'amd and khata' is upon the 'Aqila, not the killer.
This includes both quasi-intentional and accidental killings.
3
Locate the dalil: the hadith of Hammal ibn Malik
The proof cited is the Prophet's command: 'للأولياء قوموا فدوه' (To the guardians: Arise and ransom him). The word 'الأولياء' refers to the killer's guardians, i.e., his 'Aqila.
The hadith is a sound (zanni al-thubut) tradition, sufficient for obligation (wujub) in Hanafi usul.
4
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah: imperative indicates obligation
The imperative verb 'قوموا' (arise) followed by 'فدوه' (ransom him) indicates a command. In Hanafi usul, an imperative (amr) from the Prophet conveys obligation (wujub) unless there is evidence to the contrary.
Thus, the hadith establishes that the 'Aqila must pay the diyah as an obligation.

Ashraf al-Hidaya, Urdu commentary on Hidaya, volume 16. Kitab al-Ma'aqil. Translation: This book is about the people of Ma'aqil. Commentary: Previously in the preceding discussion was about diyat, and in this will be discussed those upon whom diyah is wajib. Here the original text is: 'Kitab Ahl al-Ma'aqil', and the people of Ma'aqil are 'Aqila, but the common practice of the authors is to express it with the deletion of the added word. The meaning of 'aql and ma'aqil, the reason for calling diyah 'aql. Al-Ma'aqil is the plural of ma'qila, and it is diyah, and diyah is called 'aql because it restrains blood from being shed, i.e., it holds back. Translation: Ma'aqil is the plural of ma'qila, and it is diyah, and diyah is called 'aql because it prevents blood from being shed, i.e., it restrains. Commentary: In this section, the author explained that ma'aqil is the plural of ma'qila, and ma'qila means diyah, and the reason for this naming is that 'aql means to restrain, and since diyah also prevents bloodshed, diyah is called 'aql. As for diyah preventing bloodshed, that is obvious. Which diyah is obligatory upon the 'Aqila? Why is diyah obligatory upon the 'Aqila and with what proof? He (al-Quduri) said: And the diyah in shibh 'amd and khata', and every diyah that is wajib by reason of the killing itself is upon the 'Aqila, and the 'Aqila are those who pay the 'aql, i.e., the diyah, and we have mentioned this in the Book of Diyat. And the basis for its obligation upon the 'Aqila is the saying of the Prophet (peace be upon him) in the hadith of Hammal ibn Malik (may Allah be pleased with him) to the guardians: 'Arise and ransom him.' Translation: Al-Quduri said: And the diyah in shibh 'amd and khata', and every diyah that is wajib by reason of the killing itself is upon the 'Aqila, and the 'Aqila are those who pay the 'aql, i.e., diyah, and we have mentioned this in the Book of Diyat. And the basis for the obligation upon the 'Aqila is the command of the Prophet (peace be upon him) in the hadith of Hammal ibn Malik to the heirs of the criminal: 'Arise and pay his diyah.' Commentary: Every diyah that is wajib by reason of the killing itself, i.e., not due to reconciliation for intentional killing or due to something else, but wajib due to the killing itself, meaning that the cause of that diyah is the killing, whether the killing is shibh 'amd or khata'. In such a case, that diyah will not be wajib upon the killer himself, but upon his supporting tribe. The details of diyat have passed in the Book of Diyat. Now as for the reason why the obligation of diyah is upon the 'Aqila, the author presented a hadith in which the Prophet (peace be upon him) commanded the heirs of the killer to pay the diyah.
Source pages p. 61

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on the Hidayah, specifically introducing Kitab al-Ma'aqil. The author first explains the terminology: 'Ma'aqil' is the plural of 'ma'qila', which means diyah (blood money). Diyah is called 'aql because it restrains bloodshed—an etymological point rooted in the Arabic word 'aql (to hold back). The chapter deals with the 'Aqila, the tribe or paternal relatives who bear the responsibility of paying diyah in certain types of killing. The commentator then cites the ruling from al-Quduri: the diyah for shibh 'amd (quasi-intentional) and khata' (accidental) killing, and every diyah that becomes obligatory by reason of the act of killing itself (not due to reconciliation or other causes), is payable by the 'Aqila, not by the killer himself. The proof (dalil) for this obligation is the hadith of Hammal ibn Malik (رضی الله عنه), where the Prophet ﷺ commanded the guardians (awliya') of the killer to pay the diyah. This demonstrates that the liability shifts from the individual to his supportive group. The commentator reiterates that such diyah is wajib upon the support group, and details of various diyat amounts are already covered in the previous chapter.

Key Terms
معاقل (ma‘āqil): Plural of ma‘qila, meaning diyah (blood money).
عاقلہ (‘āqila): The tribe or paternal relatives who bear the payment of diyah.
عقل (‘aql): Literally 'to restrain'; used metaphorically for diyah because it restrains bloodshed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) The hadith of Hammal ibn Malik

Key Takeaway
The diyah for shibh 'amd and khata' is wajib upon the 'Aqila, not the killer, as established by the Prophet's command in the hadith of Hammal ibn Malik.

Diyat — Blood Money
intermediate
8 min
The Rational Basis for 'Aqila's Liability
Rational proof for 'Aqila's liability in diyat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the rational (aqli) argument for why the 'Aqila pays diyah in accidental and quasi-intentional killings, and identify the underlying principle of leniency (takhfif).

Core Idea
The 'Aqila pays diyah not as punishment but to prevent the killer's ruin while honoring the victim's life.

The Hanafi school holds that in cases of accidental (khata') or quasi-intentional (shibh 'amd) killing, the blood-money (diyah) is paid by the killer's support group ('Aqila), not solely by the killer. This lesson unpacks the rational justification for this ruling, which is based on the principles of preserving life and preventing undue hardship. You will see how the shared responsibility reflects communal supervision and mercy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two premises of the rational argument
First: The victim's life is sacred, so compensation is due. Second: The killer is excused (ma'dhur) due to error or lack of lethal intent, so imposing full diyah on him would be ruinous and thus unjust.
These premises are found in the Arabic text: 'الخاطئ معذور' and 'في ایجاب مال عظیم احجافه و استیصاله'.
2
Understand the conclusion: joining the 'Aqila
To avoid the killer's ruin while still providing compensation, the law joins the 'Aqila to share the burden. This achieves leniency (takhfif) for the killer without neglecting the victim's right.
The text says: 'فضم اليه العاقلة تحقيقا للتخفيف' – 'then the 'Aqila is joined with him to achieve leniency.'
3
Analyze why the 'Aqila is specifically chosen
The killer's strength and ability to act come from his supporters (the 'Aqila). Their failure to supervise him constitutes negligence; therefore, they are held partially responsible.
The text argues: 'لانه انما قصر لقوة فيه و تلك بانصاره و هم العاقلة فكانوا هم المقصرين' – 'because he fell short due to his strength, and that strength is from his supporters, so they are the ones who fell short'.
4
Connect to the hadith basis
The Prophet (peace be upon him) ordered the heirs of a woman who accidentally killed another to pay diyah, establishing collective responsibility. This hadith is the textual proof (dalil naqli), while the rational argument (dalil aqli) explains the wisdom behind it.
The hadith of Hamal ibn Malik is summarized at the beginning of the passage.

دلیل عقلی
ولان النفس محترمة لا وجه الى الاهدار والخاطئ معذور و كذا الذى تولى شبه العمد نظرا الى الآلة فلا وجه الى ايجاب العقوبة عليه و في ایجاب مال عظیم احجافه و استیصاله فيصير عقوبة فضم اليه العاقلة تحقيقا للتخفيف و انما خصوا بالضم لانه انما قصر لقوة فيه و تلک بانصاره و هم العاقلة فكانوا هم المقصرين في تركهم مراقبته فخصوا به
ترجمہ اور اس لئے کہ نفس محترم ہے جس کے بعدار کی کوئی وجہ نہیں ہے اور خاطی معذور ہے اور ایسے ہی وہ شخص جو شبہ عد کا متولی ہوا آلہ کا لحاظ کرتے ہوئے تو اس پر عقوبت واجب کرنے کی کوئی وجہ نہیں ہے اور مال کے واجب کرنے میں اس کو پریشانی میں مبتلا کرنا اور اس کو ہلاک کرنا ہے تو یہ ایجاب مال عذاب ہوگا تو اسکی جانب عاقلہ کو ملا دیا جائے گا تخفیف کی تحقیق کی غرض سے اور ملانے کے ساتھ عاقلہ مختص ہیں اسلئے کہ قائل نے کوتاہی کی ہے اپنے اندر قوت کی وجہ سے اور اس کی قوت اس کے مددگاروں کے ذریعہ ہے اور مددگار عاقلہ ہیں تو عاقلہ ہی کوتاہی کرنے والے ہوئے ان کے چھوڑنے میں اس کی نگرانی کو تو ضم کے ساتھ عاقا مختص ہوئے۔ تشریح یہ عاقلہ پر دیت واجب ہونے کی عقلی دلیل ہے جس کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ مقتول کا نفس محترم ہے، جس کو ہدر قرار نہیں دیا جا سکتا اور خاطی بھی معذور ہے، خطا قبل ہوا ہو تب بھی معذور ہے اور شبہ عمد کے اندر بھی معذور ہے، کیونکہ یہاں آلہ کا استعمال تادیب کے لئے تھا وہ اتفاق سے مر گیا بہر حال دونوں صورتوں میں قاتل معذور ہے۔ پھر بھی اگر قاتل کے اوپر عقوبت واجب کر دی جائے اور وہ بھی پوری دیت تو قاتل کی بربادی اور ہلاکت یقینی ہے اس لئے تحقیقا اس کے ساتھ اس کے عاقلہ کو ملا دیا جائے گا تا کہ قاتل بربادی سے بچ جائے ۔ اب رہا یہ سوال کہ جب تخفیف کی غرض سے ملانے کی ضرورت تھی تو عاقلہ کی تخصیص کیوں؟ تو اس کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ قاتل کی کوتاہی یہ ہے کہ اس نے تثبت و احتیاط کا دامن چھوڑا ہے اور اس میں آدمی کی قوت کا دخل ہے اور آدمی کی قوت اس کی برادری اور خاندان اور متعلقین سے ہوتی ہے اس وجہ سے تقدیر عاقلہ کی جانب سے تقصیر پائی گئی کہ انھوں نے اس کی نگرانی کو کیوں چھوڑا ہے اس لئے ضم کے ساتھ عاقلہ ہی خاص کئے گئے ہیں۔
The summary of the hadith is that Hamal ibn Malik had two wives. One of them struck the other with a tent peg, causing her to miscarry and die. Upon this, the Prophet (peace be upon him) ordered the heirs of the woman who struck to pay her diyah. Rational Proof: Because a human life is sacred, there is no basis for disregarding it. The one who errs is excused, and likewise the one who commits quasi-intentional (shibh amd) considering the instrument, so there is no basis for imposing punishment on him. Imposing a heavy financial burden on him would be oppressive and ruinous, so it would become a punishment. Therefore, the 'Aqila is joined with him to achieve leniency. They are specifically joined because the killer has fallen short due to his strength, and that strength comes from his supporters—who are the 'Aqila. Thus they are the ones who fell short by failing to supervise him, so they are singled out for joining.
Source pages p. 63

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. It begins by summarizing a hadith where a woman accidentally kills another, and the Prophet orders her heirs to pay diyah. Then it provides a rational argument for why the 'Aqila (the killer's support group) must pay the blood money in cases of accidental or quasi-intentional killing. The reasoning is that the victim's life is sacred and cannot be wasted, but the killer is also excused (ma'dhur) due to error or lack of intent to kill. If the full diyah were imposed solely on the killer, it would destroy him, so the 'Aqila is added to share the burden and alleviate hardship. The 'Aqila is specifically chosen because the killer's strength comes from his supporters, and their failure to supervise him constitutes a form of negligence. This follows the Hanafi principle of istihsan (equity) to prevent undue hardship.

Key Terms
عاقلہ (al-‘āqilah): The group of supporters (tribe, clan, or registry) responsible for paying blood money on behalf of the killer in cases of accidental or quasi-intentional killing.
شبہ عمد (shibh al-‘amd): Quasi-intentional killing where the act is intentional but the instrument used is not one that normally kills, e.g., a light stick used for discipline.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the Hanafi school assign the payment of diyah to the 'Aqila in cases of accidental killing?
A) To punish the killer's tribe
B) To compensate the victim's family quickly
C) To prevent the killer's financial ruin while still compensating the victim
D) To encourage tribal solidarity

Key Takeaway
The 'Aqila's liability is a mechanism of leniency (takhfif) to balance the sanctity of life with the killer's inability to bear full diyah.

Diyat — Blood Money

Definition of 'Aqila: Ahl al-Diwan vs Relatives
Defining 'Aqila as ahl al-diwan and disputing the Shafi'i view of relatives

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of 'Aqila, identify the Shafi'i counter-position, and evaluate the Hanafi proof based on 'Umar's practice and ijma.

Core Idea
The 'Aqila are defined by the diwan in organized armies — a Hanafi application of the principle of nusra to changing circumstances.

This passage presents the Hanafi view that blood money (diyah) is paid by the 'Aqila, who are the people of the diwan (military registry) if the killer is a soldier. It then contrasts the Shafi'i position that the 'Aqila are always the relatives. The Hanafi proof rests on the practice of Caliph 'Umar (RA) and the silent consensus of the Companions, applying the underlying meaning of support (nusra) rather than a literal abrogation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
Who is responsible for paying diyah in cases of accidental killing? This is the core question disputed between Hanafi and Shafi'i schools.
2
State the Hanafi position
The Hanafi school holds that the 'Aqila are ahl al-diwan (people registered in the military registry) if the killer is a soldier. This is based on the practice of 'Umar (RA).
The diwan was a military registry introduced by 'Umar.
3
State the Shafi'i position
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that the 'Aqila are the killer's relatives (asaba), citing the practice of the Prophet (SAW) and the idea that diyah is a form of connection (silah).
4
Examine the Hanafi proof
The Hanafi proof is the action of 'Umar (RA) who assigned diyah to ahl al-diwan in the presence of the Companions without objection, indicating an implicit ijma.
This is a qawl al-sahabi that is considered qati' in transmission and dalaala.
5
Understand the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school argues that this is not an abrogation but a continuation of the same principle (diyah on ahl al-nusra) applied to new circumstances where support comes from the diwan rather than kinship.
The principle of nusra (support) remains constant; the means change.

عاقلہ کا مصداق
قال والعاقلة اهل الديوان ان كان القاتل من أهل الديوان يؤخذ من عطايا هم في ثلث سنين واهل الديوان اهل الرايات وهم الجيش الذين كتبت اساميهم فى الديوان وهذا عندنا وقال الشافعى الدية على اهل العشيرة لانه کان کذلک علی عهد رسول الله ولا نسخ بعده ولانه صلة والا ولى بها الاقارب ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا اور عاقلہ اہل دیوان ہیں اگر قاتل اہل دیوان میں سے ہو دیت ان کے عطایا سے تین سال میں لی جائے گی اور اہل دیوان اہل رایات (جھنڈے والے) ہیں اور یہ وہ شکر ہے جن کے نام دیوان میں درج ہوں اور یہ ہمارے نزدیک لیے تمام شافعی نے فرمایا کہ دیت قبیلہ والوں پر ہے اس لئے کہ رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم کے زمانہ میں ایسا ہی تھا اور آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم کے بعد منسوخ نہیں ہوا اور اس لئے کہ دیت تو صلہ ہے۔ اور صلہ کے زیادہ لائق اقارب ہیں۔ تشریح دیت عاقلہ پر بر بناء نصرت واجب ہوتی ہے۔ اب ضرورت پیش آئی کہ اہل نصرت کون لوگ ہیں اور وہ کون ہیں جن کو عاقلہ کہا جائے گا تو اس میں سے اول نمبر اہل دیوان ہیں ، اب سوال ہوگا کہ دیوان کون ہیں تو اس کو واضح کیا گیا ہے۔ جس کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ لوگ فوج میں بھرتی ہوتے ہیں تو ان کا نام سرکاری کا غذات درجسٹروں میں درج ہوتا ہے۔ پھر انکی مختلف کمپنیاں ہوتی ہیں اور مختلف جماعتیں ہوتی ہیں اور الگ رجسٹروں میں ان کے نام درج ہوتے ہیں۔ یعنی ہر کمپنی کا رجسٹر الگ الگ ہوتا ہے۔ تو جولوگ ایک کمپنی کے افراد ہیں وہ آپس میں ایک دوسرے کے عاقلہ ہیں کیونکہ اگر ان میں سے کسی کو کوئی حادثہ پیش آتا ہے تو وہ اپنے رفقاء سے مدد طلب کرے گا لہذا اگر ان میں سے کسی سے ایسا فعل صادر ہو جائے جس سے دیت واجب ہو تو وہ انہی اہل دیوان پر واجب ہوگی اور دیوان بمعنی رجیستر ہے۔ یعنی اس کی کمپنی کے لوگوں پر اور اہل دیوان پر دیت واجب ہونا ہمارا مسلک ہے اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک اہل دیوان پر دبیت واجب نہ ہوگی بلکہ دیت کا وجوب خاندان کے لوگوں پر ہوگا۔ امام شافعی کی دلیل اول تو یہ ہے کہ آنحضرت صلى الله عليه وسلم کے زمانہ میں دیت صرف خاندان وقبیلہ پر ہی واجب ہوتی تھی اور جب آپ کے بعد کوئی نبی نہیں ہے تو آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم کے بعد حکم منسوخ بھی نہیں ہو سکتا۔ دوسری دلیل ان کی یہ ہے کہ دیت تو ایک صلہ ہے اور صلات کے حقدارا قارب ہی ہوا کرتے ہیں لہذا دیت اقارب پر واجب ہوگی۔
دلیل احناف
ولنا قضية عمر رضى الله عنه فانه لما دون الدواوين جعل العقل على اهل الديوان وكان ذلك بمحضر من الصحابة من غير نكير منهم وليس ذلك بنسخ بل هو تقرير معنى لان العقل كان على اهل النصرة وقد كانت بانواع بالقرابة والحلف والولاء والعد وفى عهد عمر رضى الله عنه قد صارت بالديوان فجعلها على اهله اتباعاً للمعنى
ترجمہ اور ہماری دلیل عمر کا فیصلہ ہے کہ جب انہوں نے رجسٹر مدون کئے تو اہل دیوان پر دیت کو مقرر کیا اور یہ صحابہ کی موجودگی میں فیر نکیر کے ہوا اور یہ نسخ نہیں ہے بلکہ معنی یہ تقریر ( اثبات) ہے اس لئے کہ دیت اہل نصرت پر ہوتی ہے اور نصرت کی مختلف انواع ہیں۔ (۱) قرابت کی وجہ سے۔ (۲) اور معاہدوں کی وجہ سے۔ (۳) اور ولاء کی وجہ سے ۔ (۴) اور شمار کرنے کی وجہ سے اور عمر ۔ کے دور میں نصرت دیوان کی وجہ سے ہو گئی تھی تو آپ نے دیت کو اہل دیوان پر کر دیا معنی کا اتباع کرتے ہوئے تشریح یہ امام ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل ہے۔ جس کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ اہل دیوان پر وجوب دیت میں صحابہ کا اجماع ہے۔ اس لئے کہ حضرت عمر فاروق نے جب رجسٹروں کو مدون کیا تو اہل دیوان پر دیت مقرر فرمادی اور آپ نے یہ کام صحابہ کی موجودگی میں کیا جس پر کسی نے کوئی
The definition of 'Aqila: He said: The 'Aqila are the people of the diwan; if the killer is from the people of the diwan, it is taken from their stipends over three years. The people of the diwan are the people of the banners, i.e., the army whose names are recorded in the diwan. This is our view. Al-Shafi'i said: The diyah is upon the people of the clan, because it was so in the time of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) and there was no abrogation after him, and because it is a connection (silah) and the relatives are most entitled to it. ... Our proof: The ruling of 'Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) when he organized the diwans and assigned the 'aql (diyah) to the people of the diwan, and that was in the presence of the Companions without any disapproval from them. This is not abrogation but rather a confirmation of the meaning, because the diyah was upon the people of support (ahl al-nusra), and it had various types: through kinship, alliance, clientage, and counting. In the era of 'Umar, support became through the diwan, so he assigned it to its people, following the meaning.
Source pages p. 63

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute. It begins by defining 'Aqila according to the Hanafi school: they are ahl al-diwan (people registered in the military registry). If the killer is a soldier registered in the diwan, his diyah is taken from the stipends of his fellow soldiers in the diwan over three years. The text then presents the Shafi'i view: diyah is upon the relatives ('asaba) of the killer, based on the practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him) and the idea that diyah is a form of connection (silah) that should go to relatives. The Hanafi proof is the practice of Caliph 'Umar (RA) who, when he organized the diwans (military registries), assigned the diyah to the people of the diwan. This was done in the presence of the Companions without any objection, constituting an ijma (consensus). This is not an abrogation of the earlier practice but rather a continuation of the same principle: diyah is upon those who provide support (nusra). In the Prophet's time, support was based on kinship and alliances; in 'Umar's time, support was based on the diwan (military organization), so he applied the same principle. This shows the Hanafi use of istihsan and attention to customary practice ('urf).

Key Terms
عاقلہ (al-‘āqilah): The group responsible for paying blood money; in Hanafi law, it is ahl al-diwan (military registry) for soldiers, otherwise relatives or tribe.
دیوان (al-dīwān): A register or administrative bureau, especially the military registry where soldiers' names and stipends are recorded.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi proof for making ahl al-diwan the 'Aqila?
A) A verse from the Quran
B) A hadith from the Prophet
C) The practice of 'Umar with silent consensus of the Companions
D) Logical analogy to inheritance

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school defines 'Aqila as ahl al-diwan for soldiers, a ruling based on 'Umar's practice and the principle of nusra, not an abrogation of earlier custom.

Diyat — Blood Money
intermediate
8 min
The 'Aqila: Ahl al-Diwan vs. Relatives in Diyah
Hanafi-Shafi'i dispute on 'aqila in diyat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on who constitutes the 'aqila and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument using the principle of nusrah.

Core Idea
Diyah follows the source of support (nusrah), not fixed blood ties.

In this lesson, we examine a dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools over who bears liability for blood money (diyah). The Hanafis argue that the 'aqila are the ahl al-diwan (army registry) because support (nusrah) in 'Umar's time came from that institution. The Shafi'is insist on relatives. The key is understanding that 'Umar's action was not abrogation but application of the same principle.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core issue
What is the specific ruling being disputed? Determine the exact point of divergence between the schools.
The dispute is about the identity of the 'aqila in diyat.
2
State both positions
Clearly articulate the Hanafi view and the Shafi'i view from the passage.
Hanafi: 'aqila are ahl al-diwan. Shafi'i: 'aqila are relatives/tribe.
3
Examine each school's dalil
Identify the proof each school offers for its position. Note the type of evidence (Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, Qiyas, etc.).
Shafi'i: Prophetic practice and diyah as a gift. Hanafi: 'Umar's action with silent ijma of the Companions.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
How does the Hanafi school rebut the Shafi'i argument? Focus on the claim of abrogation.
The Hanafis argue that 'Umar's action is not naskh but taqrir (affirmation) of the meaning of nusrah.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
What is the practical difference in application between the two positions?
For military personnel, Hanafi: registry group pays; Shafi'i: blood relatives pay.

كتاب المعاقل
اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد ۱۹ اور اہل دیوان اہل رایات (جھنڈے والے) ہیں اور یہ وہ شکر [؟] ہے جن کے نام دیوان میں درج ہوں اور یہ ہمارے نزدیک لیے تمام شافعی نے فرمایا کہ دیت قبیلہ والوں پر ہے اس لئے کہ رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم کے زمانہ میں ایسا ہی تھا اور آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم کے بعد منسوخ نہیں ہوا اور اس لئے کہ دیت تو صلہ ہے۔ اور صلہ کے زیادہ لائق اقارب ہیں۔ تشریح دیت عاقلہ پر بر بناء نصرت واجب ہوتی ہے۔ اب ضرورت پیش آئی کہ اہل نصرت کون لوگ ہیں اور وہ کون ہیں جن کو عاقلہ کہا جائے گا تو اس میں سے اول نمبر اہل دیوان ہیں ، اب سوال ہوگا کہ دیوان کون ہیں تو اس کو واضح کیا گیا ہے۔ جس کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ لوگ فوج میں بھرتی ہوتے ہیں تو ان کا نام سرکاری کا غذات درجسٹروں میں درج ہوتا ہے۔ پھر انکی مختلف کمپنیاں ہوتی ہیں اور مختلف جماعتیں ہوتی ہیں اور الگ رجسٹروں میں ان کے نام درج ہوتے ہیں۔ یعنی ہر کمپنی کا رجسٹر الگ الگ ہوتا ہے۔ تو جولوگ ایک کمپنی کے افراد ہیں وہ آپس میں ایک دوسرے کے عاقلہ ہیں کیونکہ اگر ان میں سے کسی کو کوئی حادثہ پیش آتا ہے تو وہ اپنے رفقاء سے مدد طلب کرے گا لہذا اگر ان میں سے کسی سے ایسا فعل صادر ہو جائے جس سے دیت واجب ہو تو وہ انہی اہل دیوان پر واجب ہوگی اور دیوان بمعنی رجیستر ہے۔ یعنی اس کی کمپنی کے لوگوں پر اور اہل دیوان پر دیت واجب ہونا ہمارا مسلک ہے اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک اہل دیوان پر دبیت واجب نہ ہوگی بلکہ دیت کا وجوب خاندان کے لوگوں پر ہوگا۔ امام شافعی کی دلیل اول تو یہ ہے کہ آنحضرت صلى الله عليه وسلم کے زمانہ میں دیت صرف خاندان وقبیلہ پر ہی واجب ہوتی تھی اور جب آپ کے بعد کوئی نبی نہیں ہے تو آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم کے بعد حکم منسوخ بھی نہیں ہو سکتا۔
دوسری دلیل ان کی یہ ہے کہ دیت تو ایک صلہ ہے اور صلات کے حقدارا قارب ہی ہوا کرتے ہیں لہذا دیت اقارب پر واجب ہوگی۔
دلیل احناف
ولنا قضية عمر رضى الله عنه فانه لما دون الدواوين جعل العقل على اهل الديوان وكان ذلك بمحضر من الصحابة من غير نكير منهم وليس ذلك بنسخ بل هو تقرير معنى لان العقل كان على اهل النصرة وقد كانت بانواع بالقرابة والحلف والولاء والعد وفى عهد عمر رضى الله عنه قد صارت بالديوان فجعلها على اهله اتباعاً للمعنى
ترجمہ اور ہماری دلیل عمر کا فیصلہ ہے کہ جب انہوں نے رجسٹر مدون کئے تو اہل دیوان پر دیت کو مقرر کیا اور یہ صحابہ کی موجودگی میں فیر [؟] نکیر کے ہوا اور یہ نسخ نہیں ہے بلکہ معنی یہ تقریر ( اثبات) ہے اس لئے کہ دیت اہل نصرت پر ہوتی ہے اور نصرت کی مختلف انواع ہیں۔ (۱) قرابت کی وجہ سے۔ (۲) اور معاہدوں کی وجہ سے۔ (۳) اور ولاء کی وجہ سے ۔ (۴) اور شمار کرنے کی وجہ سے اور عمر ۔ کے دور میں نصرت دیوان کی وجہ سے ہو گئی تھی تو آپ نے دیت کو اہل دیوان پر کر دیا معنی کا اتباع کرتے ہوئے تشریح یہ امام ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل ہے۔ جس کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ اہل دیوان پر وجوب دیت میں صحابہ کا اجماع ہے۔ اس لئے کہ حضرت عمر فاروق نے جب رجسٹروں کو مدون کیا تو اہل دیوان پر دیت مقرر فرمادی اور آپ نے یہ کام صحابہ کی موجودگی میں کیا جس پر کسی نے کوئی
نکیر نہیں فرمائی۔
اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد ۱۹
اور امام شافعی کا اس کو شیخ کہنا غیر مناسب ہے بلکہ یہ حکم اصلی کا اثبات و تقریر ہے اس لئے کہ دیت کا وجوب اہل نصرت پر ہے اور
نصرت کی چند قسمیں ہیں ۔
- قرابت کی وجہ سے بھی نصرت ہوتی ہے۔
- حلیف کی وجہ سے یعنی آپس میں نصرت پر معاہدہ ہو جائے جس کو ولاء الموالات کہتے ہیں۔
اور بھی نصرت دار عتاقہ کی وجہ سے ہوتی ہے۔
-۴- اور کبھی نصرت اس بناء پر ہوتی ہے کہ کوئی شخص کسی قوم میں رہنے کی وجہ سے انہی میں سے شمار ہونے لگے جیسے ابلیس لعین باب عبادت میں فرشتوں کے ساتھ مشغول ہونے کی وجہ سے انہی میں سے شمار ہوتا تھا۔ اگر چہ وہ ان کی جنس میں سے نہیں ہے۔ بہر حال نصرت کی یہ مختلف انواع تھیں اور عمر کے دور میں نصرت دیوان کی وجہ سے ہوگئی اور یہ نصرت بابل الدیوان [؟] ان سے پہلے نہ تھی تو معنی کا لحاظ کرتے ہوئے حضرت عمر نے اہل دیوان پر دیت واجب کردی تو یہ نسخ نہیں ہے بلکہ حکم اصلی کے معنی کا لحاظ ہے۔
Book of Blood Money. Ashraf al-Bidaya, Urdu commentary on Hidayah, volume 19: Ahl al-diwan are the people of flags (banner-holders), and they are those whose names are recorded in the registry. And this is our view. But al-Shafi'i said that blood money is on the tribe because it was like that in the time of the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, and it was not abrogated after him, and because blood money is a gift, and relatives are more deserving of a gift. Commentary: Blood money is obligatory on the 'aqila based on support. Now the need arises as to who are the people of support and who are called 'aqila. Among them, the first are ahl al-diwan. Then it will be asked: who are the diwan? It has been clarified: it means that when people enroll in the army, their names are recorded in official registers. Then they have different companies and different groups, and their names are recorded in separate registers. So those who are members of one company are each other's 'aqila because if an accident occurs to one of them, he will seek help from his companions. Hence, if any act occurs from one of them that necessitates blood money, it will be obligatory on these ahl al-diwan. And diwan means register. So it is our madhhab that blood money is obligatory on the people of his company and on ahl al-diwan. And according to Imam al-Shafi'i, blood money is not obligatory on ahl al-diwan, rather its obligation is on the family members. Imam al-Shafi'i's first proof: In the time of the Prophet, blood money was only obligatory on the family and tribe, and since there is no prophet after him, the ruling cannot be abrogated. His second proof: Blood money is a gift, and the recipients of a gift are usually relatives, so blood money will be obligatory on relatives. Our proof: We have the case of 'Umar, may Allah be pleased with him, when he organized the registers, he placed blood money on the people of the register. That was in the presence of the Companions without any objection from them. That is not abrogation but rather affirmation of the meaning, because blood money was on the people of support, and support used to be through kinship, alliance, clientage, and counting. In the era of 'Umar, it had become through the register, so he placed it on its people following the meaning. Translation: Our proof is the decision of 'Umar: when he organized the registers, he fixed blood money on ahl al-diwan, and this was in the presence of the Companions without any objection. This is not abrogation but rather affirmation (establishment) of the meaning because blood money is on the people of support, and support has different types: (1) through kinship, (2) through treaties, (3) through clientage, and (4) through counting. In 'Umar's era, support had become through the diwan, so he placed blood money on ahl al-diwan, following the meaning. Commentary: This is the proof of Imam Abu Hanifa. Its essence is that there is agreement of the Companions on the obligation of blood money on ahl al-diwan, because when 'Umar organized the registers, he fixed blood money on ahl al-diwan, and he did this in the presence of the Companions, and no one objected. Ashraf al-Hidayah, commentary on Hidayah volume 19. And Imam al-Shafi'i's calling it abrogation is inappropriate; rather it is affirmation and establishment of the original ruling because the obligation of blood money is on the people of support, and there are several types of support: (1) support through kinship, (2) support through alliance, i.e., a contract of mutual support called wala' al-muwalat, (3) support through emancipation, and (4) sometimes support is based on a person living among a people and being reckoned as one of them, like Iblis was reckoned among the angels due to his devotion in worship, even though he was not of their species. In any case, these were various types of support, and in 'Umar's time support had become through the diwan, and this support through the diwan did not exist before. So he made blood money obligatory on ahl al-diwan, considering the meaning, and this is not abrogation but rather consideration of the meaning of the original ruling.
Source pages p. 64

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafis and Shafi'is regarding who constitutes the 'aqila (the group liable for paying blood money). The author first states the Hanafi position: the 'aqila are ahl al-diwan (the army registry) because support (nusrah) now comes from that institution. Then he presents the Shafi'i view: the 'aqila should be the relatives/tribe, based on the practice of the Prophet and because diyah is a gift. The Hanafi response is that the Prophet's practice was based on the principle of support, which in his time came from kinship and alliance. When 'Umar established the diwan, support shifted to the registry. Thus, the change is not an abrogation but an application of the same principle to new circumstances. The Hanafi evidence is the action of 'Umar with silent consensus of the Companions, which is considered an ijma. The passage clarifies that the ruling is based on the underlying meaning (ma'na) of nusrah, not on a fixed text.

Key Terms
عاقلہ ('āqila): The group of people who are liable to pay blood money (diyah) on behalf of a person who commits unintentional homicide.
دیوان (dīwān): The official military registry or department where soldiers' names and stipends are recorded.
نصرت (nuṣrah): Mutual help, support, and cooperation that forms the basis of the 'aqila relationship.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why did 'Umar place diyah on ahl al-diwan instead of the tribe?
A) Because it was an arbitrary decision.
B) Because the Prophet had abrogated the earlier ruling.
C) Because support (nusrah) in his time came through the diwan, so it follows the same principle.
D) Because the Companions did not object to changing the ruling.

Key Takeaway
The 'aqila are defined by the source of support (nusrah), not fixed blood ties, so they can change with social structures.

Basis of 'Aqila: Profession and Alliance
Extension of 'aqila to professional and allied groups

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the basis of 'aqila according to the Hanafi school and apply it to contemporary scenarios.

Core Idea
The 'aqila are those who mutually support you — whether by blood, profession, or alliance.

This lesson examines the Hanafi extension of 'aqila beyond blood ties. The passage teaches that the 'aqila is defined by social support (nusrah), which can be based on a common profession or an alliance. This ruling adapts the concept to changing societal structures.

Guided Path
1
Identify the principle
What determines the 'aqila? The text indicates it is mutual support (nusrah).
The original 'aqila was based on tribal blood ties.
2
Recognize the two new bases
The jurists explicitly mention profession (hirfah) and alliance (hilf/muwalat).
These are expansions from the original ruling.
3
Understand legal reasoning
The Hanafi jurists extended the ruling based on the type of mutual support present in a community.
They said 'if today there is a people...' showing ijtihad.
4
Note the dynamic nature
The 'aqila system is not static; it can be applied to any form of mutual support.
The commentary states 'these are not the only four forms'.
5
Compare with original 'aqila
Originally 'aqila were blood relatives. Now they can be professionals or allies.
This shows the school's adaptability.

Source Text
